Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507 Administrative garnishment order.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(1): Subject to Subsection (2), if a judgment is entered against a debtor, the office may issue an administrative garnishment order against the debtor's personal property, including wages, in the possession of a party other than the debtor in the same manner and with the same effect as if the order was a writ of garnishment issued by a court with jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(2): The office may issue the administrative garnishment order if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(2)(a): the order is signed by the director or the director's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(2)(b): the underlying debt is for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(2)(b)(i): nonpayment of a civil accounts receivable or a civil judgment of restitution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(2)(b)(ii): nonpayment of a judgment, or abstract of judgment or award filed with a court, based on an administrative order for payment issued by an agency of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(3): 70C-7-103 An administrative garnishment order issued in accordance with this section is subject to the procedures and due process protections provided by Rule 64D, Utah Rules of Civil Procedure, except as provided by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4): An administrative garnishment order issued by the office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a): contain a statement that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(i): if known:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(i)(A): the nature, location, account number, and estimated value of the property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(i)(B): the name, address, and phone number of the person holding the property;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(ii): whether any of the property consists of earnings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(iii): the amount of the judgment and the amount due on the judgment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(a)(iv): the name, address, and phone number of any person known to the plaintiff to claim an interest in the property;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(b): identify the defendant, including the defendant's name and last known address;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(c): notify the defendant of the defendant's right to reply to answers and request a hearing as provided by Rule 64D, Utah Rules of Civil Procedure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(4)(d): state where the garnishee may deliver property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5): The office may, in the office's discretion, include in an administrative garnishment order:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(a): the last four digits of the defendant's Social Security number;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(b): the last four digits of the defendant's driver license number;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(c): the state in which the defendant's driver license was issued;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d): one or more interrogatories inquiring:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(i): whether the garnishee is indebted to the defendant and, if so, the nature of the indebtedness;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(ii): whether the garnishee possesses or controls any property of the defendant and, if so, the nature, location, and estimated value of the property;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(iii): whether the garnishee knows of any property of the defendant in the possession or under the control of another and, if so:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(iii)(A): the nature, location, and estimated value of the property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(iii)(B): the name, address, and telephone number of the person who has possession or control of the property;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(iv): whether the garnishee is deducting a liquidated amount in satisfaction of a claim against the plaintiff or the defendant, whether the claim is against the plaintiff or the defendant, and the amount deducted;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(v): the date and manner of the garnishee's service of papers upon the defendant and any third party;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(vi): the dates on which any previously served writs of continuing garnishment were served; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(5)(d)(vii): any other relevant information, including the defendant's position, rate of pay, method of compensation, pay period, and computation of the amount of the defendant's disposable earnings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(a): A garnishee who acts in accordance with this section and the administrative garnishment issued by the office is released from liability unless an answer to an interrogatory is successfully controverted.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(b): Except as provided in Subsection (6)(c), if the garnishee fails to comply with an administrative garnishment issued by the office without a court or final administrative order directing otherwise, the garnishee is liable to the office for an amount determined by the court.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c): The amount for which a garnishee is liable under Subsection (6)(b) includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c)(i)(A): the value of the judgment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c)(i)(B): the value of the property, if the garnishee shows that the value of the property is less than the value of the judgment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c)(ii): reasonable costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(c)(iii): attorney fees incurred by the parties as a result of the garnishee's failure.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(6)(d): If the garnishee shows that the steps taken to secure the property were reasonable, the court may excuse the garnishee's liability in whole or in part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(7)(a): If the office has reason to believe that a garnishee has failed to comply with the requirements of this section in the garnishee's response to a garnishment order issued under this section, the office may submit a motion to the court requesting the court to issue an order against the garnishee requiring the garnishee to appear and show cause why the garnishee should not be held liable under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(7)(b): The office shall attach to a motion under Subsection (7)(a) a statement that the office has in good faith conferred or attempted to confer with the garnishee in an effort to settle the issue without court action.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(8): A person is not liable as a garnishee for drawing, accepting, making, or endorsing a negotiable instrument if the instrument is not in the possession or control of the garnishee at the time of service of the administrative garnishment order.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(9)(a): A person indebted to the defendant may pay to the office the amount of the debt or an amount to satisfy the administrative garnishment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(9)(b): The office's receipt of an amount described in Subsection (9)(a) discharges the debtor for the amount paid.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(10): A garnishee may deduct from the property any liquidated claim against the defendant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(a): If a debt to the garnishee is secured by property, the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(a)(i): is not required to apply the property to the debt when the office issues the administrative garnishment order; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(a)(ii): may obtain a court order authorizing the office to buy the debt and requiring the garnishee to deliver the property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(b): Notwithstanding Subsection (11)(a)(i):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(b)(i): the administrative garnishment order remains in effect; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(b)(ii): the office may apply the property to the debt.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(c): The office or a third party may perform an obligation of the defendant and require the garnishee to deliver the property upon completion of performance or, if performance is refused, upon tender of performance if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(c)(i): the obligation is secured by property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(c)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(c)(ii)(A): the obligation does not require the personal performance of the defendant; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(11)(c)(ii)(B): a third party may perform the obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(a): The office may issue a continuing garnishment order against a nonexempt periodic payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(b): This section is subject to the Utah Exemptions Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(c): A continuing garnishment order issued in accordance with this section applies to payments to, or for the benefit of, the defendant from the date of service upon the garnishee until the earliest of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(c)(i): the last periodic payment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(c)(ii): the judgment upon which the administrative garnishment order is issued is stayed, vacated, or satisfied in full; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(c)(iii): the office releases the order.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(d): No later than seven days after the last day of each payment period, the garnishee shall with respect to that period:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(d)(i): answer each interrogatory;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(d)(ii): serve an answer to each interrogatory on the office, the defendant, and any other person who has a recorded interest in the property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(d)(iii): deliver the property to the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(e): If the office issues a continuing garnishment order during the term of a writ of continuing garnishment issued by a court, the order issued by the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(e)(i): is tolled when a writ of garnishment or other income withholding is already in effect and is withholding greater than or equal to the maximum portion of disposable earnings described in Subsection (13);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(e)(ii): is collected in the amount of the difference between the maximum portion of disposable earnings described in Subsection (13) and the amount being garnished by an existing writ of continuing garnishment if the maximum portion of disposable earnings exceed the existing writ of garnishment or other income withholding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(12)(e)(iii): shall take priority upon the termination of the current term of existing writs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(13): The maximum portion of disposable earnings of an individual subject to seizure in accordance with this section is the lesser of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(13)(a): 25% of the defendant's disposable earnings for any other judgment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(13)(b): the amount by which the defendant's disposable earnings for a pay period exceeds the number of weeks in that pay period multiplied by 30 times the federal minimum wage as provided in 29 U.S.C. Sec. 201 et seq., Fair Labor Standards Act of 1938.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(a): In accordance with the requirements of this Subsection (14), the office may, at its discretion, determine a dollar amount that a garnishee is to withhold from earnings and deliver to the office in a continuing administrative garnishment order issued under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(b): The office may determine the dollar amount that a garnishee is to withhold from earnings under Subsection (14)(a) if the dollar amount determined by the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(b)(i): does not exceed the maximum amount allowed under Subsection (13); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(b)(ii): is based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(b)(ii)(A): earnings information received by the office directly from the Department of Workforce Services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(b)(ii)(B): previous garnishments issued to the garnishee by the office where payments were received at a consistent dollar amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(c): The earnings information or previous garnishments relied on by the office under Subsection (14)(b)(ii) to calculate a dollar amount under this Subsection (14) shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(c)(i): for one debtor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(c)(ii): from the same employer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(c)(iii): for two or more consecutive quarters; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(14)(c)(iv): received within the last six months.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(15): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(15)(a): A garnishee who provides the calculation for withholdings on a defendant's wages in the garnishee's initial response to an interrogatory in an administrative garnishment order under this section is not required to provide the calculation for withholdings after the garnishee's initial response if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(15)(a)(i): the garnishee's accounting system automates the amount of defendant's wages to be paid under the garnishment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(15)(a)(ii): the defendant's wages do not vary by more than five percent from the amount disclosed in the garnishee's initial response.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(15)(b): Notwithstanding Subsection (15)(a), upon request by the office or the defendant, a garnishee shall provide, for the last pay period or other pay period specified by the office or defendant, a calculation of the defendant's wages and withholdings and the amount garnished.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(a): A garnishee under an administrative garnishment order under this section is entitled to receive a garnishee fee, as provided in this Subsection (16), in the amount of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(a)(i): $10 per garnishment order, for a noncontinuing garnishment order; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(a)(ii): $25, as a one-time fee, for a continuing garnishment order.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(b): A garnishee may deduct the amount of the garnishee fee from the amount to be remitted to the office under the administrative garnishment order, if the amount to be remitted exceeds the amount of the fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(c): If the amount to be remitted to the office under an administrative garnishment order does not exceed the amount of the garnishee fee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(c)(i): the garnishee shall notify the office that the amount to be remitted does not exceed the amount of the garnishee fee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(c)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(c)(ii)(A): the garnishee under a noncontinuing garnishment order shall return the administrative garnishment order to the office, and the office shall pay the garnishee the garnishee fee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(c)(ii)(B): the garnishee under a continuing garnishment order shall delay remitting to the office until the amount to be remitted exceeds the garnishee fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(d): If, upon receiving the administrative garnishment order, the garnishee does not possess or control any property, including money or wages, in which the defendant has an interest:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(d)(i): the garnishee under a continuing or noncontinuing garnishment order shall, except as provided in Subsection (16)(d)(ii), return the administrative garnishment order to the office, and the office shall pay the garnishee the applicable garnishee fee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(16)(d)(ii): if the garnishee under a continuing garnishment order believes that the garnishee will, within 90 days after issuance of the continuing garnishment order, come into possession or control of property in which the defendant owns an interest, the garnishee may retain the garnishment order and deduct the garnishee fee for a continuing garnishment once the amount to be remitted exceeds the garnishee fee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(17): 78A-2-216 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(18): An administrative garnishment instituted in accordance with this section shall continue to operate and require that a person withhold the nonexempt portion of earnings at each succeeding earning disbursement interval until the total amount due in the garnishment is withheld or the garnishment is released in writing by the court or office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-507(19): If the office issues an administrative garnishment order under this section to collect an amount owed on a civil accounts receivable or a civil judgment of restitution, the administrative garnishment order shall be construed as a continuation of the criminal action for which the civil accounts receivable or civil judgment of restitution arises if the amount owed is from a fine, fee, or restitution for the criminal action.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508 Written request to receive a credit for a restitution payment -- Eligibility requirements.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(a): "Debt" means any amount that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(a)(i): an individual owes as part of a criminal judgment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(a)(ii): is collected and managed by the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(b): "Eligible individual" means an individual who meets the requirements of Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(c): "Qualifying debt" means a debt that is a fine, a fee, a surcharge, or any other money, that is deposited into the General Fund by the state treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(1)(d): "Voluntary payment" means a payment on a debt that is made before, or in the absence of, a legal proceeding or administrative action to collect or enforce the collection of the debt.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(2): An individual is eligible for a credit described in Subsection (3) if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(2)(a): the individual submits a written request, on or after May 1, 2024, and before May 1, 2026, to the office requesting the credit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(2)(b): the individual owes a debt of $3,000 or greater at the time of the written request; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(2)(c): the individual was sentenced before July 1, 2021, for a criminal judgment for which the individual owes a debt.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(3)(a): If an eligible individual makes a voluntary payment toward any restitution owed by the individual, the office shall issue a credit against any qualifying debt owed by the individual in the amount of 75% of the amount applied to restitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(3)(b): The office may issue the credit described in Subsection (3) to any voluntary payment made toward restitution before the written request was submitted as described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(4): The office shall provide:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(4)(a): reasonable notice of eligibility before May 1, 2026, to any individual that may be eligible for the credit as described in Subsection (2)(b) and (c); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(4)(b): if an individual submits a written request as described in Subsection (2)(a), a written confirmation as to whether the individual is an eligible individual and will receive a credit as described in Subsection (3).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(5): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the office may make rules regarding the administration of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(6): By no later than November 30, 2025, the office shall report to the Judiciary Interim Committee on the outcomes of this section and whether the eligibility period described in Subsection (2) should be extended beyond May 1, 2026.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-3-508(7): Nothing in this section authorizes the office to reimburse or refund an individual for any payment on a debt.

*************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.1 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.1(1): 31A-37-102 "Captive insurance company" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.1(2): "Covered entity" means a participating entity of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.1(2)(a): the Risk Management Fund; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.1(2)(b): any captive insurance company created by the risk manager.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5 Risk manager -- Appointment -- Duties.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(1)(a): There is created within the department the Division of Risk Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(1)(b): The executive director shall, with the approval of the governor, appoint a risk manager as the division director, who shall be qualified by education and experience in the management of general property and casualty insurance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2): (4); 34A-2-203; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The risk manager shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(a): (4); 34A-2-203 except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(a)(i): all property and casualty insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(a)(ii): reinsurance of property and casualty insurance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(a)(iii): 34A-2-203 subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act make rules, in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(i): prescribing reasonable and objective underwriting and risk control standards for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(i)(A): all covered entities of the Risk Management Fund; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(i)(B): any captive insurance company created by the risk manager;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(ii): prescribing the risks to be covered by the Risk Management Fund and the extent to which these risks will be covered;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(iii): prescribing the properties, risks, deductibles, and amount limits eligible for payment out of the Risk Management Fund;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(iv): prescribing procedures for making claims and proof of loss; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(b)(v): establishing procedures for the resolution of disputes relating to coverage or claims, which may include binding arbitration;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(c): implement a risk management and loss prevention program for covered entities for the purpose of reducing risks, accidents, and losses to assist covered entities in fulfilling their responsibilities for risk control and safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d): coordinate and cooperate with any covered entity having responsibility to manage and protect state properties, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(i): the state fire marshal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(ii): the director of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(iii): the Department of Public Safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(iv): institutions of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(v): school districts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(d)(vi): charter schools;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(e): maintain records necessary to fulfill the requirements of this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(f): manage the Risk Management Fund and any captive insurance company created by the risk manager in accordance with economically and actuarially sound principles to produce adequate reserves for the payment of contingencies, including unpaid and unreported claims, and may purchase any insurance or reinsurance considered necessary to accomplish this objective; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(2)(g): inform the covered entity's governing body and the governor when any covered entity fails or refuses to comply with reasonable risk control recommendations made by the risk manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(3): Before the effective date of any rule, the risk manager shall provide a copy of the rule to each covered entity affected by it.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(4): The risk manager may not use a captive insurance company created by the risk manager to purchase:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(4)(a): workers' compensation insurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(4)(b): health insurance; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-101.5(4)(c): life insurance.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102 Risk manager -- Powers.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1): Title 31A, Chapter 37, Captive Insurance Companies Act The risk manager may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(a): enter into contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(b): Title 31A, Chapter 37, Captive Insurance Companies Act form one or more captive insurance companies authorized under
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(c): purchase insurance or reinsurance;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(d): adjust, settle, and pay claims;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(e): pay expenses and costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(f): study the risks of all covered entities and properties;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(g): issue certificates of coverage or insurance for covered entities with respect to any risks covered by the Risk Management Fund or any captive insurance company created by the risk manager;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(h): make recommendations about risk management and risk reduction strategies to covered entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(i): in consultation with the attorney general, prescribe insurance, indemnification, and liability provisions to be included in all state contracts;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(j): review covered entity building construction, major remodeling plans, program plans, and make recommendations to the covered entity about needed changes to address risk considerations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(k): attend covered entity planning and management meetings when necessary;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(l): review any proposed legislation and communicate with legislators and legislative committees about the liability or risk management issues connected with any legislation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(1)(m): solicit any needed information about covered entity plans, programs, or risks necessary to perform the risk manager's responsibilities under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(2)(a): The risk manager may expend money from the Risk Management Fund to procure and provide coverage to all covered entities and their indemnified employees, except those entities or employees specifically exempted by statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(2)(b): The risk manager shall apportion the costs of that coverage according to the requirements of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(3): 63A-1-114; 63J-1-410 Before charging a rate, fee, or other amount to an executive branch agency, or to a subscriber of services other than an executive branch agency, the director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(3)(a): 63A-1-114 submit the proposed rates, fees, or other amount and cost analysis to the Rate Committee established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(3)(b): 63J-1-410 obtain the approval of the Legislature as required by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-102(4): The director shall conduct a market analysis by July 1, 2005, and periodically thereafter, of proposed rates and premiums, which analysis shall include a comparison of the division's rates and premiums with the rates and premiums of other public or private sector providers where comparable services and rates are reasonably available.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-104 Course-of-construction insurance for facilities constructed by This is the Place Foundation.

The risk manager may provide course-of-construction insurance for facilities constructed by This is the Place Foundation at This is the Place State Park and bill the Division of State Parks for the cost of the insurance.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-203 Refusal of agency to pay charges -- Notice to the Division of Finance for collection.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-203(1): If any agency of the state refuses to remit any payment as charged by the risk manager within 30 days after the date due, the risk manager may certify to the  director of the Division of Finance the fact of the refusal and the amount of the delinquent payment, together with a request that the amount be transferred from funds of the delinquent agency to the Risk Management Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-203(2): The risk manager shall mail a copy of the certification and request to the delinquent agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-203(3): The risk manager shall resolve claims against the fund in an expeditious manner.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-206 Limits on use of risk management data as evidence.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Notwithstanding any other provisions of law, any reports, recommendations, surveys, schedules, lists, or data compiled, or action taken or not taken by or at the request of the risk manager to identify, evaluate, or plan the safety enhancement or risk reduction of any potential accident sites or other hazards related to any entity covered by the Risk Management Fund may not be admitted into evidence in any court, or used for any other purposes in any action for damages arising from any occurrence at a location mentioned or addressed in those reports, recommendations, surveys, schedules, lists, or data.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-207(2): 63G-2-201(5); 63G-2-206 Notwithstanding Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208 Investment of Risk Management Fund.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(1): 63A-4-201 The state treasurer shall invest the assets of the Risk Management Fund created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(2): Nothing in this section requires a specific outcome in investing.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(3): The state treasurer may deduct any administrative costs incurred in managing fund assets from earnings before distributing the earnings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(4)(a): The state treasurer may employ professional asset managers to assist in the investment of the assets of the funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(4)(b): The treasurer may only provide compensation to asset managers from earnings generated by the funds' investments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(a): The state treasurer shall invest and manage the assets of the funds as a prudent investor would by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(a)(i): considering the purposes, terms, distribution requirements, and other circumstances of the funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(a)(ii): exercising reasonable care, skill, and caution in order to meet the standard of care of a prudent investor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(b): In determining whether the state treasurer has met the standard of care of a prudent investor, the judge or finder of fact shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(b)(i): consider the state treasurer's actions in light of the facts and circumstances existing at the time of the investment decision or action, and not by hindsight; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(b)(ii): evaluate the state treasurer's investment and management decisions respecting individual assets:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(b)(ii)(A): not in isolation, but in the context of a fund portfolio as a whole; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-4-208(5)(b)(ii)(B): as a part of an overall investment strategy that has risk and return objectives reasonably suited to the funds.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1)(a): "Capital development project" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1)(a)(i): a remodeling or site or utility improvement project with a total cost of $3,500,000 or more;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1)(a)(ii): a new facility with a construction cost of $500,000 or more; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1)(a)(iii): a purchase of real property if an appropriation is requested and made for the purchase.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(1)(b): "Capital development project" does not include a capital improvement project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2): "Capital improvement project" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(a): a remodeling, alteration, replacement, repair, or site or utility improvement project:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(a)(i): with a total cost of less than $3,500,000; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(a)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(a)(ii)(A): with a total cost of $3,500,000 or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(a)(ii)(B): that will be paid for with funds that are not state funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(b): a utility infrastructure improvement project that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(b)(i): has a total cost of less than $7,000,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(b)(ii): consists of two or more projects that, if done separately, would each cost less than $3,500,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(b)(iii): the division determines is more cost effective or feasible to be completed as a single project; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(2)(c): a new facility with a total construction cost of less than $500,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(a): "New facility" means a new building constructed on state property regardless of the source of the funding that pays for construction of the new building.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(b): "New facility" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(b)(i): an addition to an existing building; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(b)(ii): the enclosure of space that was not previously fully enclosed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(c): "New facility" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(c)(i): the replacement of state-owned space that is demolished or that is otherwise removed from state use, if the total construction cost of the replacement space is less than $3,500,000; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(3)(c)(ii): the construction of facilities that do not fully enclose a space.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(4): "Replacement cost" means, as determined by the Division of Risk Management:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(4)(a): for state facilities, excluding auxiliary facilities as defined by the director, the cost to replace those facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(4)(b): for infrastructure, as defined by the director, the cost to replace the infrastructure.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-401(5): "State funds" means public money appropriated by the Legislature.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405 Capital improvement projects.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1): 63A-5b-401(3)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(a): On or before January 15 of each year, the division shall, on behalf of all agencies, submit a list of anticipated capital improvement project requirements to the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b): 63A-5b-401(3)(c) The division shall ensure that the capital improvements project list identifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(i): each single capital improvement project that costs more than $1,000,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(ii): each multiple capital improvement project within a single building or facility that collectively costs more than $1,000,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(iii): each single capital improvement project that will be constructed over multiple years with a yearly cost of $1,000,000 or more and an aggregate cost of more than $3,500,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(iv): each multiple capital improvement project within a single building or facility with a yearly cost of $1,000,000 or more and an aggregate cost of more than $3,500,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(v): each single capital improvement project previously reported to the Legislature as a capital improvement project under $1,000,000 that, because of an increase in costs or scope of work, will now cost more than $1,000,000;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(vi): each multiple capital improvement project within a single building or facility previously reported to the Legislature as a capital improvement project under $1,000,000 that, because of an increase in costs or scope of work, will now cost more than $1,000,000; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(1)(b)(vii): 63A-5b-401(3)(c) each capital improvement project described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(a): Unless otherwise directed by the Legislature, the division shall prioritize capital improvement projects on the capital improvement project list up to the level of appropriation made by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(b): In prioritizing capital improvement projects, the division shall consider the results of facility evaluations completed by an architect or engineer as stipulated by the division's facilities maintenance standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c): In prioritizing capital improvement projects, the division shall allocate at least 90% of the funds that the Legislature appropriates for capital improvement projects to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(i): capital improvement projects that address:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(i)(A): a structural issue;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(i)(B): fire safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(i)(C): a code violation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(i)(D): any issue that impacts health and safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii): capital improvement projects that upgrade:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii)(A): an HVAC system;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii)(B): an electrical system;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii)(C): essential equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii)(D): an essential building component; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(ii)(E): infrastructure, including a utility tunnel, water line, gas line, sewer line, roof, parking lot, or road; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(c)(iii): capital improvement projects that demolish and replace an existing building that is in extensive disrepair and cannot be fixed by repair or maintenance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(d): In prioritizing capital improvement projects, the division may not allocate more than 10% of the funds that the Legislature appropriates for capital improvement projects to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(d)(i): remodeling and aesthetic upgrades to meet state programmatic needs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(2)(d)(ii): construct an addition to an existing building or facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(3): The division may require an entity that benefits from a capital improvement project to repay the capital improvement funds from savings that result from the capital improvement project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-405(4): 63A-5b-401(3)(c) The division may provide capital improvement project funding to a single project or to multiple projects within a single building or facility, even if the total cost of the project or multiple projects is $3,500,000 or more, if:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502 Programming.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(a): "Program document" means a final document that contains programming information.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b): "Programming" means services to define the scope and purpose of an anticipated project, and may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(i): researching criteria applicable to the scope and purpose of an anticipated project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(ii): identifying the scale of the project and the type of facilities and the level of specialized functions that will be required;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(iii): identifying and prioritizing values and goals that will impact the project, including institutional purposes, growth objectives, and cultural, technological, temporal, aesthetic, symbolic, economic, environmental, safety, sustainability, and other relevant criteria;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(iv): evaluating functional efficiency, user comfort, building economics, environmental sustainability, and visual quality;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(v): identifying objectives for the project, including such elements as image, efficiencies, functionality, cost, and schedule;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(vi): identifying and evaluating the constraints that will have an impact on the project such as legal requirements, financial constraints, location, access, visibility, and building services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(vii): developing standards such as area allowances, space allocation, travel distances, and furniture and equipment requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(viii): establishing general space quality standards related to such elements as lighting levels, equipment performance, acoustical requirements, security, and aesthetics;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(ix): identifying required spaces;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(x): establishing sizes and relationships;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(xi): establishing space efficiency factors or the ratio of net square footage to gross square footage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(1)(b)(xii): documenting particular space requirements such as special HVAC, plumbing, power, lighting, acoustical, furnishings, equipment, or security needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2): A program document may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(a): incorporate written and graphic materials; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b): include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(i): an executive summary;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(ii): documentation of the methodology used to develop the programming;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(iii): value and goal statements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(iv): relevant facts upon which the programming was based;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(v): conclusions derived from data analysis;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(vi): relationship diagrams;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(vii): flow diagrams;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(viii): matrices identifying space allocations and relationships;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(ix): space listings by function and size; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(2)(b)(x): space program sheets, including standard requirements and special HVAC, plumbing, power, lighting, acoustical, furnishings, equipment, or security needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(a): establishing the types of projects for which programming and a program document are required;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(b): establishing the scope of programming required for defined categories of projects;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(c): establishing the circumstances under which an agency must obtain authorization from the director to engage in programming;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(d): governing the funding of programming;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(e): relating to the administration of programming; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-502(3)(f): regarding any restrictions that may be imposed on a person involved in programming from participating in the preparation of construction documents for a project that is the subject of the programming.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503 Planning Fund expenditures authorized -- Ceiling on expenditures -- Recovery.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(1): The Planning Fund shall be used to make payments for engineering, architectural, and other planning expenses necessary to make a meaningful cost estimate of any facility or improvement with a demonstrable or immediate need.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(2): The director may make expenditures from the Planning Fund in order to provide planning information to the governor and the Legislature, up to a maximum of $350,000 in outstanding Planning Fund commitments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(3)(a): The director shall authorize all payments made from the Planning Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(3)(b): Payments from the Planning Fund shall be a charge on the project for which they were drawn.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(3)(c): If the Legislature appropriates money for a building project for which planning costs have previously been paid from the Planning Fund, the director shall credit that amount to the Planning Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(4): (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(4)(a): The director may expend money from the Planning Fund for architectural and engineering services incident to the planning and preparation of applications for funds on construction financed by other than state sources, including federal grants.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-503(4)(b): (4)(a) Upon approval of financing referred to in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(1)(a): "Facility" means any building, structure, or other improvement that is constructed:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(1)(a)(i): on property that the state or any of the state's departments, commissions, institutions, or agencies owns; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(1)(a)(ii): by the state or any of the state's departments, commissions, institutions, or agencies on property that the state does not own.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(1)(b): "Facility" does not mean an unoccupied structure that is a component of the state highway system.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-601(2): "Local government" means the county, municipality, or local school district that would have jurisdiction to act as the compliance agency if the division did not have jurisdiction to act as the compliance agency.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602 Design criteria, standards, and procedures.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(1): The director shall establish design criteria, standards, and procedures for the planning, design, and construction of a new facility and for improvements to an existing facility, including life-cycle costing, cost-effectiveness studies, and other methods and procedures that address:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(1)(a): the need for the facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(1)(b): the effectiveness of the facility's design;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(1)(c): the efficiency of energy use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(1)(d): the usefulness of the facility over the facility's lifetime.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(2): Before proceeding with construction, the director and the officials charged with the administration of the affairs of the particular agency shall approve the location, design, plans, and specifications.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(3): The director shall prepare or have prepared by one or more private persons the designs, plans, and specifications for the projects administered by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(4): 63A-5b-604 Before construction may begin, the director shall review the design of projects exempted from the division's administration under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(4)(a): complies with any restrictions placed on the project by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(4)(b): is appropriate for the purpose and setting of the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(5): Title 63J, Chapter 1, Budgetary Procedures Act Notwithstanding the requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(5)(a): accelerate the design of a project funded by an appropriation act passed by the Legislature in the Legislature's annual general session;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(5)(b): use an unencumbered existing account balance to fund that design work; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-602(5)(c): reimburse the account balance from the amount funded for the project when the appropriation act funding the project becomes effective.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605 Requirement for bidders to list subcontractors -- Changing subcontractors -- Bidders as subcontractors.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1)(a): "First-tier subcontractor" means a subcontractor who contracts directly with the prime contractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1)(b)(i): "Subcontractor" means a person under contract with a contractor or another subcontractor to provide services or labor for the construction, installation, or repair of an improvement to real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1)(b)(ii): "Subcontractor" includes a trade contractor or specialty contractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(1)(b)(iii): "Subcontractor" does not include a supplier that provides only materials, equipment, or supplies to a contractor or subcontractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(2): The director shall apply the provisions of this section to achieve fair and competitive bidding and to discourage bid-shopping by contractors.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3): (3)(a)(ii); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a): (3)(a)(ii); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(i): (3)(a)(ii); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(i)(A): (3)(a)(ii) On a public construction project, the director shall, except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(i)(B): (3) A bidder that is not one of the apparent lowest three bidders may also submit a list of the bidder's first-tier subcontractors containing the information required by this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(ii): A bidder is not required to list a first-tier subcontractor if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(ii)(A): the bidder's total bid is less than $500,000 and the first-tier subcontractor's bid is less than $20,000; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(a)(ii)(B): the bidder's total bid is $500,000 or more and the first-tier subcontractor's bid is less than $35,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(b): A bidder shall submit the list required under this section within 24 hours after the bid opening time, not including Saturday, Sunday, and any state holiday.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(3)(c): A list submitted under this section does not limit the director's right to authorize a change in the listing of any subcontractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(4): The director may not consider a bid submitted by a bidder that fails to submit a list meeting the requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(5): A bidder shall verify that all subcontractors listed as part of the bidder's bid are licensed as required by state law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(a): After 24 hours after the bid opening, a bidder may change the bidder's subcontractors only after:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(a)(i): receiving permission from the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(a)(ii): establishing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(a)(ii)(A): that the change is in the best interest of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(a)(ii)(B): the reasons for the change that meet the standards established by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(6)(b): If the director approves a change in subcontractors that results in a net lower contract price for subcontracted work, the director may require the bidder to reduce the total of the prime contract to reflect the change.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7): (7)(b)(i); (7)(b)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(a): A bidder may list the bidder as a subcontractor if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(a)(i): the bidder is currently licensed to perform the portion of the work for which the bidder lists the bidder as a subcontractor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(a)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(a)(ii)(A): the bidder intends to perform the work of a subcontractor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(a)(ii)(B): the bidder intends to obtain a subcontractor at a later date to perform the work because the bidder was unable to obtain a bid from a qualified subcontractor or from a qualified subcontractor at a cost that the bidder considers to be reasonable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b): (7)(b)(i); (7)(b)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(i): If the bidder intends to perform the work of a subcontractor, the director may, by written request, require that the bidder provide the director with information indicating the bidder's:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(i)(A): previous experience in the type of work to be performed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(i)(B): qualifications for performing the work.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(ii): (7)(b)(i) A bidder shall respond in writing within five business days after receiving the director's written request under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(iii): (7)(b)(ii) If the information a bidder submits under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(iii)(A): require the bidder to use a subcontractor for the portion of the work in question and obtain the subcontractor bid under the supervision of the director; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(7)(b)(iii)(B): reject the bidder's bid.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(a): If a bidder intends to obtain a subcontractor at a later date to perform work described in the bidder's bid, the bidder shall provide documentation with the subcontractor list required under this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(a)(i): describing the bidder's efforts to obtain a bid of a qualified subcontractor at a reasonable cost; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(a)(ii): explaining  why the bidder was unable to obtain a qualified subcontractor bid.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(b): If a bidder who intends to obtain a subcontractor at a later date to perform the work described in a bid is awarded a contract, the director:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(b)(i): shall supervise the bidder's efforts to obtain a qualified subcontractor bid; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(8)(b)(ii): may not adjust the amount of the contract awarded in order to reflect the actual amount of the subcontractor's bid.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(9): The division may not disclose any subcontractor bid amounts obtained under this section until the division has awarded the project to a contractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-605(10): In addition to all other reasons allowed by statute or rule, the director may reject all bids if all of the bidders whose bids are within the budget of the project fail to submit a subcontractor list as required under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606 Dispute resolution process -- Penalties for fraud or bad faith claim.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2): 63G-4-401; 63G-4-402 The director shall consider, and the rules may include:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(e): a provision for an independent hearing officer, panel, or arbitrator to extend the time period for resolution of the claim by not to exceed 60 additional days for good cause;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(f): a provision for the extension of required time periods if the claimant agrees;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(g): requirements that decisions be issued in writing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(h): provisions for an administrative appeal of a decision;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(i): provisions for the timely payment of claims after resolution of the dispute, including any appeals;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(k): a requirement that a claim or dispute that does not include a monetary claim against the division or an agent of the division is not limited to the dispute resolution process provided for in this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(l): requirements for claims and disputes to be eligible for the dispute resolution process under this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(m): the use of an independent hearing officer or panel or the use of arbitration or mediation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(2)(n): the circumstances under which a subcontractor may file a claim directly with the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(3)(a): is bound by the decision reached under this process, subject to any modification of the decision on appeal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(3)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code may not pursue a claim, protest, or dispute under the dispute resolution process established in
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(4): A fraudulent misrepresentation made by or bad faith claim pursued by a contractor, subcontractor, or supplier, may be grounds for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-606(4)(a): the director to suspend or debar the contractor, subcontractor, or supplier; or

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(6)(a)(i): ensure that each contract the contractor enters with a subcontractor that is subject to the requirements of this section requires the subcontractor to obtain and maintain an offer of qualified health coverage for the subcontractor's eligible employees and the eligible employees' dependents during the duration of the subcontract; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(6)(a)(ii): obtain from a subcontractor referred to in Subsection (6)(a)(i) a written statement demonstrating that the subcontractor offers qualified health coverage to eligible employees and eligible employees' dependents.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(6)(b)(i): shall be from:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(7)(a)(ii): A contractor is not subject to penalties for the failure of a subcontractor to obtain and maintain an offer of qualified health coverage as required in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(7)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(7)(b)(i): A subcontractor that fails to obtain and maintain an offer of qualified health coverage during the duration of the subcontract as required in this section is subject to penalties in accordance with administrative rules made by the division under this section, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(7)(b)(ii): A subcontractor is not subject to penalties for the failure of a contractor to maintain an offer of qualified health coverage as required in this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-607(15)(c): may require as a condition of providing the written statement that a contractor or subcontractor hold the administrator harmless for an action arising under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-608 Obligations beyond authorized funding prohibited -- Exceptions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-608(1): Unless otherwise specifically instructed by the terms of the appropriation for a particular project, the director shall assure that no obligations beyond the authorized funding are incurred in the construction of any project authorized by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-608(2): The director may expend appropriations for statewide projects from funds provided by the Legislature for the purposes and within the guidelines established by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-608(3): The director may consent to the drafting of a plan or the awarding of a contract that will exceed in cost the funding currently available for the project only if the Legislature has specifically provided for extending construction of a building or the completion of a project into future fiscal periods.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609 Expenditure of appropriated funds supervised by director -- Contingencies -- Disposition of project reserve funds -- Set aside for Utah Percent-for-Art Program.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1): 63A-5b-503 The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1)(a)(i): supervise the expenditure of funds in providing plans, engineering specifications, sites, and construction of the buildings for which legislative appropriations are made; and

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1)(b): 63A-5b-503
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1)(b)(i): expend the amount necessary from appropriations for planning, engineering, and architectural work; and

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(1)(c)(ii): that are over and above all amounts obligated by contract for planning, engineering, architectural work, sites, and construction contracts.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(a)(ii): 6% to 9.5% for remodeling projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(b): The director shall hold the statewide contingency funds to cover:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(b)(ii): unforeseen, necessary costs beyond those specifically budgeted for the project.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(c)(i): The Legislature shall annually review the percentage and the amount held in the statewide contingency reserve.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(2)(c)(ii): The Legislature may reappropriate to other building needs, including the cost of administering building projects, any amount from the statewide contingency reserve that is in excess of the reserve required to meet future contingency needs.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(a)(i): One percent of the amount appropriated for the construction of any new state building or facility may be appropriated and set aside for the Utah Percent-for-Art Program administered by the Division of Fine Arts under Title 9, Chapter 6, Part 4, Utah Percent-for-Art Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(a)(ii): The total amount appropriated and set aside under Subsection (5)(a)(i) may not exceed:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(a)(ii)(A): $200,000, if the new state building or facility is not located in a county of the first class; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(a)(ii)(B): $250,000, if the new state building or facility is located in a county of the first class.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(b): The director shall release to the Division of Fine Arts any funds included in an appropriation to the division that are designated by the Legislature for the Utah Percent-for-Art Program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(c): Funds from appropriations for a state building or facility may not be set aside:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(c)(i): if any part of the funds is derived from the issuance of bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-609(5)(c)(ii): to the extent the set aside of funds would jeopardize the federal income tax exemption otherwise allowed for interest paid on bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-610 Transfer from project reserve money.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-610(1): With the approval of and through an appropriation by the Legislature, the division shall transfer at least $100,000 annually from the project reserve money to the General Fund to pay for personal service expenses associated with the management of construction projects.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-610(2): With the approval of and as directed by the Legislature, the division shall transfer additional money from the project reserve money to pay administrative costs associated with the management of construction projects and other division responsibilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701 Operation and maintenance for state facilities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(1): As used in this section, "maintenance functions" means all programs and activities related to the operation and maintenance of a state facility, including preventive maintenance and inspection.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(a): The director shall direct or delegate maintenance functions for an agency, except for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(a)(i): the State Capitol Preservation Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(a)(ii): an institution of higher education.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(b): The director may delegate responsibility for maintenance functions to an agency only if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(b)(i): the agency requests the responsibility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(b)(ii): the director determines that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(b)(ii)(A): the agency has the necessary resources and skills to comply with maintenance functions standards approved by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(b)(ii)(B): the delegation would result in net cost savings to the state as a whole.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(c): The State Capitol Preservation Board and an institution of higher education are exempt from division oversight of maintenance functions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(2)(d): An institution of higher education shall comply with the division's facility maintenance functions standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3)(a): An institution of higher education shall annually report to the division, in a format required by the division, on the institution of higher education's compliance with the division's maintenance functions standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3)(b): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3)(b)(i): prescribe a standard format for reporting compliance with the division's maintenance functions standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3)(b)(ii): report to the Legislature on the compliance or noncompliance with the standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-701(3)(b)(iii): conduct periodic audits to ensure that institutions of higher education are complying with the standards and report the results of the audits to the Legislature.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702 Standards and requirements for state facilities -- Life-cycle cost effectiveness.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(1)(a): "Clean energy system" means a system designed to use solar, wind, geothermal power, wood, hydropower, nuclear, or other clean energy source to heat, cool, or provide electricity to a building.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(1)(b): "Life cycle cost-effective" means the most prudent cost of owning, operating, and maintaining a facility, including the initial cost, energy costs, operation and maintenance costs, repair costs, and the costs of energy conservation and clean energy systems.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2): The director shall, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, make rules:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(a): that establish standards and requirements for determining whether a state facility project is life cycle cost-effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(b): for the monitoring of an agency's operation and maintenance expenditures for a state-owned facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(c): to establish standards and requirements for utility metering;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(d): that create an operation and maintenance program for an agency's facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(e): that establish a methodology for determining reasonably anticipated inflationary costs for each operation and maintenance program described in Subsection (2)(d);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(f): that require an agency to report the amount the agency receives and expends on operation and maintenance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(2)(g): that provide for determining the actual cost for operation and maintenance requests for a new facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(3): The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(3)(a): ensure that state-owned facilities, except for facilities under the control of the State Capitol Preservation Board, are life cycle cost-effective;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(3)(b): conduct ongoing facilities audits of state-owned facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(3)(c): monitor an agency's operation and maintenance expenditures for state-owned facilities as provided in rules made under Subsection (2)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(4)(a): An agency shall comply with the rules made under Subsection (2) for new facility requests submitted to the Legislature for a session of the Legislature after the 2017 General Session.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-702(4)(b): The Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst and the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall, for each agency with operation and maintenance expenses, ensure that each required budget for the agency is adjusted in accordance with the rules described in Subsection (2)(e).


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703 Agency lease payments.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(a): Beginning July 1, 2020, the division shall implement a program to charge agencies, except institutions of higher education, lease payments for the agency's use and occupancy of space within a building.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(b): Before July 1, 2020, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(b)(i): conduct a market analysis of market lease rates for comparable space in buildings comparable to division-owned buildings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(b)(ii): establish lease rates for an agency's use and occupancy of a division-owned building.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c): The lease rates shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(i): consistent with market rates for comparable space in comparable buildings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(ii): calculated to cover:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(ii)(A): an amortized amount for capital replacement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(ii)(B): an amount for capital improvements; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(ii)(C): operation and maintenance costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(1)(c)(iii): in proportion to legislative appropriations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-703(2): 63J-1-102 In making appropriations to cover lease payments under this section, the Legislature shall create a line item, as defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(1): "Agency optional term" means an option that is exclusively exercisable by a leasing agency to extend the lease term.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(2): "High-cost lease" means a real property lease that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(2)(a): has an initial term including any agency optional term of 10 years or more; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(2)(b): will require lease payments of more than $5,000,000 over the term of the lease, including any agency optional term.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3)(a): "Leasing agency" means a department, commission, board, council, agency, institution, officer, corporation, fund, division, office, committee, authority, laboratory, library, unit, bureau, panel, or other administrative unit of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3)(b): "Leasing agency" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3)(b)(i): the legislative branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3)(b)(ii): the judicial branch; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(3)(b)(iii): an institution of higher education.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-801(4): "Significant lease terms" includes the duration of the lease, the frequency of the periodic payments, a renewal clause, a purchase option, a cancellation clause, a repair and maintenance clause, and a restriction on use of the property.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802 Leasing responsibilities of the director.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1): (1)(f); (1)(f) The director shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(d): (1)(f) apply the criteria contained in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(e): (1)(f) evaluate each lease under the division's control and apply the criteria contained in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f): in evaluating leases:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(i): determine whether the lease is cost-effective when the needs of the leasing agency to be housed in the leased facilities are considered;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(ii): determine whether another option such as construction, use of other state-owned space, or a lease-purchase agreement is more cost-effective than leasing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(iii): determine whether the significant lease terms are cost-effective and provide the state with sufficient flexibility and protection from liability;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(iv): compare the proposed lease payments to the current market rates, and evaluate whether the proposed lease payments are reasonable under current market conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(v): compare proposed significant lease terms to the current market, and recommend whether these proposed terms are reasonable under current market conditions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(f)(vi): if applicable, recommend that the lease or modification to a lease be approved or disapproved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(g): based upon the evaluation, include in the report recommendations that identify viable alternatives to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(g)(i): make the lease cost-effective; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(g)(ii): meet the leasing agency's needs when the lease expires; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(h): upon request, provide the information included in the report to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(h)(i): the leasing agency benefitted by the lease; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(1)(h)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(2): The director may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(2)(a): subject to legislative appropriation, enter into a facility lease with a term of up to 10 years if the length of the lease's term is economically advantageous to the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-802(2)(b): subject to legislative appropriation, enter into a facility lease with a term of more than 10 years if the length of the lease's term is economically advantageous to the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803 Reporting of leasing activity.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803(1): The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803(1)(a): prepare a standard form upon which a leasing agency and another state institution or entity can report the current and proposed lease activity of the leasing agency, institution, or entity, including any lease renewal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803(1)(b): develop procedures and mechanisms within the division to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803(1)(b)(i): obtain and share information about each leasing agency's real property needs; and
