Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-803(2)(b): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804 Leasing by the Administrative Office of the Courts -- Judicial Council approval required for high-cost lease -- Director's responsibilities.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(1): Before executing a high-cost lease or a modification to a lease that results in a high-cost lease, the Administrative Office of the Courts shall submit a draft of the new lease or modification to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(1)(a): the Judicial Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(1)(b): the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(2): The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(2)(a): review the draft submitted by the Administrative Office of the Courts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(2)(b): within 30 days after receiving the draft, submit a report on the draft to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(2)(b)(i): the Judicial Council; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(2)(b)(ii): the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3): (2)(b) A report under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(a): the director's opinion about:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(a)(i): whether the lease or modification is cost-effective when the needs of the entity to be housed in the leased facility are considered;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(a)(ii): whether another option such as construction, use of other state-owned space, or a lease-purchase agreement is more cost-effective than leasing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(a)(iii): whether the significant lease terms are cost-effective and provide the state with sufficient flexibility and protection from liability;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(b): a comparison of the proposed lease payments to the current market rates, and a recommendation as to whether the proposed lease payments are reasonable under current market conditions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(c): a comparison of proposed significant lease terms to the current market, and a recommendation as to whether the proposed terms are reasonable under current market conditions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(3)(d): a recommendation from the director that the lease or modification to a lease be approved or disapproved.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(4)(a): The Administrative Office of the Courts may not execute a new high-cost lease or modification to an existing lease that will result in a high-cost lease unless the lease or modification is approved by a majority vote of the Judicial Council.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-804(4)(b): The Judicial Council shall consider the recommendations of the director in determining whether to approve a high-cost lease or modification resulting in a high-cost lease.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(1): "Applicant" means a person who submits a timely, qualified proposal to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(2): 78B-6-520.3 "Condemnee" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(3): "Division-owned property" means real property, including an interest in real property, to which the division holds title, regardless of who occupies or uses the real property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(4): "Local government entity" means a county, city, town, special district, special service district, community development and renewal agency, conservation district, school district, or other political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(5): 63A-5b-303 "Primary state agency" means a state agency for which the division holds title to real property that the state agency occupies or uses, as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(6): "Private party" means a person who is not a state agency, local government entity, or public purpose nonprofit entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(7): "Public purpose nonprofit entity" means a corporation, association, organization, or entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(7)(a): is located within the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(7)(b): is not a state agency or local government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(7)(c): is exempt from federal income taxation under Section 501(c)(3), Internal Revenue Code; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(7)(d): operates to fulfill a public purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(8): 63A-5b-903 "Qualified proposal" means a written proposal that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(8)(a): 63A-5b-903 meets the criteria established by the division by rule under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(8)(b): if submitted by a local government entity or public purpose nonprofit entity, explains the public purpose for which the local government entity or public purpose nonprofit entity seeks a transfer of ownership or lease of the vacant division-owned property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(8)(c): the director determines will, if accepted and implemented, provide a material benefit to the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(9): 63A-5b-304 "Secondary state agency" means a state agency:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(9)(a): 63A-5b-304 that is authorized to hold title to real property that the state agency occupies or uses, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(9)(b): for which the division does not hold title to real property that the state agency occupies or uses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(10): "State agency" means a department, division, office, entity, agency, or other unit of state government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(11): "Transfer of ownership" includes a transfer of the ownership of vacant division-owned property that occurs as part of an exchange of the vacant division-owned property for another property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(12): "Vacant division-owned property" means division-owned property that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(12)(a): a primary state agency is not occupying or using; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(12)(b): the director has determined should be made available for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(12)(b)(i): use or occupancy by a primary state agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(12)(b)(ii): a transfer of ownership or lease to a secondary state agency, local government entity, public purpose nonprofit entity, or private party.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(13): "Written proposal" means a brief statement in writing that explains:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(13)(a): the proposed use or occupancy, transfer of ownership, or lease of vacant division-owned property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-901(13)(b): how the state will benefit from the proposed use or occupancy, transfer of ownership, or lease.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904 Division authority with respect to vacant division-owned property -- Limitations.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(1): 63A-5b-909; 63A-5b-908 Subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(1)(a): provide for a primary state agency's occupancy or use of vacant division-owned property, if the director determines that the primary state agency's occupancy or use is in the best interests of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(1)(b): effect a transfer of ownership or lease of vacant division-owned property, as provided in this section; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(1)(c): 63A-5b-908 refer vacant division-owned property to the Department of Transportation for sale by auction, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2): The division may effect a transfer of ownership or lease of vacant division-owned property without receiving fair market value in return if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2)(a): the director determines that the transfer of ownership or lease is in the best interests of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2)(b): for a proposed transfer of ownership or lease to a local government entity, public purpose nonprofit entity, or private party, the director determines that the local government entity, public purpose nonprofit entity, or private party intends to use the property to fulfill a public purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2)(c): the director requests and receives a recommendation on the proposed transfer of ownership or lease from the Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2)(d): the director communicates the Executive Appropriations Committee's recommendation to the executive director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(2)(e): the executive director approves the transfer of ownership or lease.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(3): 63A-5b-908
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(3)(a): If the division effects a transfer of ownership of vacant division-owned property without receiving fair market value in return, the division shall require the documents memorializing the transfer of ownership to preserve to the division:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(3)(a)(i): in the case of a transfer of ownership of vacant division-owned property to a secondary state agency, local government entity, or public purpose nonprofit entity for no or nominal consideration, a right of reversion, providing for the ownership of the property to revert to the division if the property ceases to be used for the public benefit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(3)(a)(ii): in the case of any other transfer of ownership of vacant division-owned property, a right of first refusal allowing the division to purchase the property from the transferee for the same price that the transferee paid to the division if the transferee wishes to transfer ownership of the former vacant division-owned property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-904(3)(b): 63A-5b-908 Subsection (3)(a) does not apply to the sale of vacant division-owned property at an auction under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907 Priorities for vacant division-owned property -- Division to convey vacant division-owned property.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(1): This section applies to a proposed transfer of ownership or lease of vacant division-owned property at less than fair market value.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(2)(a): An applicant that is a state agency has priority for vacant division-owned property over an applicant that is a local government entity, a public purpose nonprofit entity, and a private party.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(2)(b): An applicant that is a local government entity and an applicant that is a public purpose nonprofit entity have:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(2)(b)(i): priority for vacant division-owned property over an applicant that is a private party; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(2)(b)(ii): between them the same priority for vacant division-owned property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(3): If the division receives multiple timely qualified proposals from applicants with the highest and same priority, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(3)(a): notify the executive director of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(3)(a)(i): the availability of the vacant division-owned property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(3)(a)(ii): the applicants with the highest and same priority that have submitted qualified proposals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(3)(b): provide the executive director with a copy of the timely qualified proposals submitted by the applicants with the highest and same priority.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(4): (3); (4) Within 30 days after being notified under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(4)(a): determine which applicant's qualified proposal is most likely to result in the highest and best public benefit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(4)(b): (4) notify the division of the executive director's decision under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(5): (2); (4) The division shall effect a transfer of ownership or lease of the vacant division-owned property to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(5)(a): (2) the applicant with the highest priority under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907(5)(b): (4) the applicant whose qualified proposal was determined by the executive director under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907.5 Lease of division-owned property to a private party.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907.5(1): If the division leases division-owned property to a private party, the division shall, within 30 days after a lease agreement is executed, provide written notice of the lease to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907.5(1)(a): the municipality in which the division-owned property is located, if the division-owned property is within a municipality; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907.5(1)(b): the county in whose unincorporated area the division-owned property is located, if the division-owned property is not located within a municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-907.5(2): Nothing in this part may be used by a private party leasing division-owned property as a basis for not complying with applicable local land use ordinances and regulations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908 Referring vacant division-owned property to the Department of Transportation for auction.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1): 63A-5b-905; 63A-5b-905 The division may refer vacant division-owned property to the Department of Transportation for a public auction if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(a): 63A-5b-905; 63A-5b-905 for a conveyance, lease, or disposal of vacant division-owned property for less than fair market value:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(a)(i): 63A-5b-905 the division has provided notice under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(a)(ii): 63A-5b-905 the division receives no qualified proposals in response to the notice under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(b): the director determines that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(b)(i): there is no reasonable likelihood that within the foreseeable future:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(b)(i)(A): a primary state agency will use or occupy the vacant division-owned property; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(b)(i)(B): a secondary state agency, local government entity, or public purpose nonprofit entity will seek a transfer of ownership or lease of the vacant division-owned property; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(b)(ii): disposing of the vacant division-owned property through a public auction is in the best interests of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(c): the director requests and receives a recommendation on the proposed public auction from the Legislative Executive Appropriations Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(d): the director communicates the Executive Appropriations Committee's recommendation to the executive director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(1)(e): the executive director approves the public auction.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(2): If the division refers a vacant division-owned property to the Department of Transportation for public auction, the Department of Transportation shall publicly auction the vacant division-owned property under the same law and in the same manner that apply to a public auction of Department of Transportation property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(3): At a public auction conducted under Subsection (2), the Department of Transportation may, on behalf of the division, accept an offer to purchase the vacant division-owned property.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(4): The division and the Department of Transportation shall coordinate together to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(4)(a): manage the details of finalizing any sale of the vacant division-owned property at public auction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(4)(b): ensure that the buyer acquires proper title and that the division receives the net proceeds of the sale.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-908(5): If a public auction under this section does not result in a sale of the vacant division-owned property, the Department of Transportation shall notify the division and refer the vacant division-owned property back to the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-911 Authority to transfer land for commuter rail station and related development.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division may transfer title to a parcel of land it owns in a county of the first class to a public transit district for the purpose of facilitating the development of a commuter rail transit station and associated transit oriented development if:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-911(1): the parcel is within one mile of the proposed commuter rail transit station and associated transit oriented development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-911(2): the division receives in return fair and adequate consideration.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-912 Report to Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The division shall, on or before the third Wednesday in November of every even-numbered year, present a written report to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee that identifies state land and buildings that are no longer needed and can be sold by the state.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(1): "Energy efficiency measure" means an action taken or initiated by an agency that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(1)(a): reduces the agency's energy or fuel use or resource energy consumption, water or other resource consumption, operation and maintenance costs, or cost of energy, fuel, water, or other resource; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(1)(b): increases the agency's energy or fuel efficiency or resource consumption efficiency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(2): 63A-5b-1002 "Energy efficiency program" means a program established under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(3): 63A-5b-1003 "Fund" means the State Facility Energy Efficiency Fund created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(4): "Performance efficiency agreement" means an agreement entered into by an agency whereby the agency implements one or more energy efficiency measures and finances the costs associated with implementation of performance efficiency measures using the stream of expected savings in costs resulting from implementation of the performance efficiency measures as a funding source for repayment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5)(a): "State facility" means any building, structure, or other improvement that is constructed on property that the state, any of the state's departments, commissions, institutions, or agencies, or a state institution of higher education owns or leases as a tenant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5)(b): "State facility" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5)(b)(i): an unoccupied structure that is a component of the state highway system;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5)(b)(ii): a privately owned structure that is located on property that the state, any of the state's departments, commissions, institutions, or agencies, or a state institution of higher education owns or leases as a tenant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1001(5)(b)(iii): a structure that is located on land administered by the trust lands administration under a lease, permit, or contract with the trust lands administration.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002 State Building Energy Efficiency Program.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(a): develop and administer the energy efficiency program, which shall include guidelines and procedures to improve energy efficiency in the maintenance and management of state facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(b): provide information and assistance to agencies in the agencies' efforts to improve energy efficiency in state facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(c): analyze energy consumption by agencies to identify opportunities for improved energy efficiency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(d): establish an advisory group composed of representatives of agencies to provide information and assistance in the development and implementation of the energy efficiency program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(e): submit to the governor and to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee of the Legislature an annual report that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(e)(i): identifies strategies for long-term improvement in energy efficiency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(e)(ii): identifies goals for energy conservation for the upcoming year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(1)(e)(iii): details energy management programs and strategies that were undertaken in the previous year to improve the energy efficiency of agencies and the energy savings achieved.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(2): Each agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(2)(a): designate a staff member that is responsible for coordinating energy efficiency efforts within the agency with assistance from the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(2)(b): provide energy consumption and costs information to the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(2)(c): develop strategies for improving energy efficiency and reducing energy costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(2)(d): provide the division with information regarding the agency's energy efficiency and reduction strategies.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3): 63A-5b-701
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3)(a): An agency may enter into a performance efficiency agreement for a term of up to 20 years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3)(b): 63A-5b-701 Before entering into a performance efficiency agreement, the agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3)(b)(i): 63A-5b-701 utilize the division to oversee the project unless the project is exempt from the division's oversight or the oversight is delegated to the agency under the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3)(b)(ii): obtain the prior approval of the governor or the governor's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(3)(b)(iii): provide the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst with a copy of the proposed agreement before the agency enters into the agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(4): An agency may consult with the energy efficiency program manager within the division regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(4)(a): the cost effectiveness of energy efficiency measures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(4)(b): ways to measure energy savings that take into account fluctuations in energy costs and temperature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5): (5); (5)(b)(i); (5)(b)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(a): (5) Except as provided under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(b): (5)(b)(i) An agency shall use energy savings to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(b)(i): fund the cost of the energy efficiency measures; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(b)(ii): (5)(b)(i) if funds are available after meeting the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(c): (5)(b)(i) The Legislature may remove energy savings if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(c)(i): (5)(b)(i) an agency has complied with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1002(5)(c)(ii): no new cost-effective energy efficiency measure is available for implementation.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004 State facility energy efficiency data.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(1): On or before July 1, 2022, each state facility shall submit to the division, or verify that the division already collects, the utility information for the state facility's utilities for each month, beginning with May 2021 and ending with May 2022.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2): (1) A state facility shall submit the utility information described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(a): in a format approved by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(b): for each location that the state facility uses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(c): for each of the following utilities that the state facility uses:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(c)(i): water;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(c)(ii): electric; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(2)(c)(iii): natural gas.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(3): The division shall use the information received in accordance with this section to identify opportunities for increased energy efficiency at each state facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1004(4): Once the division has identified an energy efficiency project for a state facility, the staff of the state facility shall assist the division in completing the identified project.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103 Making keys to buildings of state, political subdivisions, or colleges and universities without permission prohibited.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103(1)(a): "Applicable government entity" means a state agency, a political subdivision of the state, the Utah Board of Higher Education, or any college or university supported in whole or in part by the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103(1)(b): "Government facility" means a building, laboratory, facility, room, dormitory, hall, or other structure owned, licensed as a licensee, leased as a tenant, or lawfully occupied by an applicable government entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103(2): An individual may not knowingly make or cause to be made any key or duplicate key for a government facility without the prior written consent of the applicable government entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1103(3): A person who violates this section is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1105 Testing and inspection firm requirements.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
The director shall ensure that any person performing testing and inspection work governed by the American Society for Testing Materials Standard E-329 on a public building under the director's supervision:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1105(1): fully complies with the American Society for Testing Materials standard specifications for an agency engaged in the testing and inspection of materials known as ASTM E-329; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1105(2): carries a minimum of $1,000,000 of errors and omissions insurance.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109 Buildings and facilities to which chapter applies -- Standards available to interested parties -- Division of Facilities Construction and Management staff to advise, review, and approve plans when possible.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1)(a): The standards in this section apply to all buildings and facilities used by the public that are constructed or remodeled in whole or in part by the use of state funds, or the funds of any political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1)(b): All of those buildings and facilities constructed in Utah after May 12, 1981, shall conform to the standard prescribed in this section except buildings, facilities, or portions of them, not intended for public use, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1)(b)(i): caretaker dwellings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1)(b)(ii): service buildings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(1)(b)(iii): heating plants.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(2): This section applies to temporary or emergency construction as well as permanent buildings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(3)(a): The standards established in this section apply to the remodeling or alteration of any existing building or facility within the jurisdictions set forth in this section where the remodeling or alteration will affect an area of the building or facility in which there are architectural barriers for persons with a physical disability.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(3)(b): If the remodeling involves less than 50% of the space of the building or facility, only the areas being remodeled need comply with the standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(3)(c): If remodeling involves 50% or more of the space of the building or facility, the entire building or facility shall be brought into compliance with the standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(4)(a): All individuals and organizations are encouraged to apply the standards prescribed in this section to all buildings used by the public, but that are financed from other than public funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(4)(b): The Division of Facilities Construction and Management shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(4)(b)(i): make the standards established by this section available to interested individuals and organizations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(4)(b)(ii): upon request and to the extent possible, make available the services of the Division of Facilities Construction and Management staff to advise, review, and approve plans and specifications in order to comply with the standards of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(5)(a): This section is concerned with nonambulatory disabilities, semiambulatory disabilities, sight disabilities, hearing disabilities, disabilities of incoordination, and aging.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(5)(b): This section is intended to make all buildings and facilities covered by this section accessible to, and functional for, persons with a physical disability.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(6): The standards of this section are the current edition of planning and design criteria to prevent architectural barriers for the aged and persons with a physical disability, as promulgated by the Division of Facilities Construction and Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(7): The responsibility for adoption of the planning and design criteria referred to in this section, and enforcement of this section shall be as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(7)(a): where state school funds are utilized, the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(7)(b): where state funds are utilized, the Division of Facilities Construction and Management; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-5b-1109(7)(c): where funds of political subdivisions are utilized, the governing board of the county or municipality in which the building or facility is located.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-201 Creation.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-201(1): There is created the Division of Fleet Operations within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-201(2): The division of fleet operations is an internal service fund agency and its financial affairs shall be accounted for as an internal service fund.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-202 Director of division -- Appointment.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
The executive director of the department shall appoint the director of the Division of Fleet Operations with the approval of the governor.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-203 Director -- Duties.
---------------------------------------------------
The director shall establish and administer the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5 Vehicle fleet cost efficiency plans -- Requirements -- Contents -- Submission by agencies.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1): The division shall develop and coordinate the implementation of a statewide vehicle fleet cost efficiency plan to ensure continuing progress toward statewide overall cost reduction in government vehicle costs.  The plan shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(a): goals for vehicle fleet cost efficiency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(b): a summary of agency submitted plans, statistics, and progress;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(c): standard measures of cost including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(c)(i): vehicle cost per mile;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(c)(ii): total vehicles;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(c)(iii): total fuel used; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(c)(iv): miles per gallon of fuel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(d): goals for purchasing the most economically appropriate size and type of vehicle for the purposes and driving conditions for which the vehicle will be used;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e): cost reduction measures which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(i): reducing vehicle engine idle time;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(ii): driving fewer miles;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(iii): using car pools when possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(iv): avoiding rush hour traffic;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(v): reducing aggressive driving;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(vi): providing proper preventative maintenance including properly inflated tires; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(e)(vii): purchasing from state fuel sites and using the lowest octane fuel needed for the altitude;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(f): reducing inventories of underutilized vehicles; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(1)(g): education to inform drivers of their accountability on implementing cost reduction measures.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(2): The division shall assist agencies to develop and implement their own plans in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-401.5(3): 63A-9-402; (1) Each agency that owns or leases vehicles shall develop, implement, and submit to the division under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(a): On or before November 1 of each calendar year, the director of the division shall submit a state-owned vehicle report to the governor and to the legislative fiscal analyst.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b): The report shall contain a summary of vehicles owned or leased by each state agency including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(i): a description of each vehicle owned or leased by each agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(ii): the person or administrative unit within the agency to whom each vehicle is assigned; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(iii): standard measures of cost for the previous year, for each vehicle, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(iii)(A): vehicle cost per mile;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(iii)(B): total vehicles;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(iii)(C): total fuel used; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(2)(b)(iii)(D): miles per gallon of fuel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(3): The legislative fiscal analyst shall submit the information from the state-owned vehicle report about each agency's state-owned vehicles to the legislative appropriation subcommittee that has jurisdiction over that agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(4)(a): Vehicles used in official investigative work where secrecy is essential are exempt from the requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-402(4)(b): The report to the governor and legislative fiscal analyst shall include the total number of state vehicles used in official investigative work where secrecy is essential that are not otherwise accounted for in the report.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403 Clean emissions vehicles -- Alternative fuel vehicles.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No later than August 30, 2018, the division shall ensure that 50% or more of new or replacement division-owned state vehicles that are motor vehicles used for the transportation of passengers are motor vehicles with emissions that are equal to or cleaner than the standards established in bin 2 in Table S04-1, of 40 C.F.R. 86.1811-04(c)(6), or any vehicle propelled to a significant extent using one of the following alternative fuels:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403(1): electricity from an off-board source;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403(2): natural gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403(3): liquid petroleum gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403(4): hydrogen; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-403(5): biodiesel.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501 Complaints about misuse or illegal operation of state vehicles -- Disposition.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501(1): The division shall refer complaints from the public about misuse or illegal operation of state vehicles to the agency that is the owner or lessor of the vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; 63A-17-306 Each agency head or the agency head's designee shall investigate all complaints about misuse or illegal operation of state vehicles and shall discipline each employee that is found to have misused or illegally operated a vehicle by following the procedures described in the rules made by the Division of Human Resource Management, in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501(3)(a): Each agency shall report the findings of each investigation conducted as well as any action taken as a result of the investigation to the directors of the Divisions of Fleet Operations and Risk Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-501(3)(b): Misuse or illegal operation of state vehicles may result in suspension or revocation of state vehicle driving privileges as governed in rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702 Authority of public to purchase natural gas from the state fuel network -- Rulemaking authority.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(1): As used in this section, "private individual or entity" means any individual or entity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(1)(a): is not acting under the authority of a federal, state, or local government agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(1)(b): is not purchasing compressed natural gas from the state's fuel network for sale, resale, distribution, redistribution, trade, exchange, or in furtherance of a commercial enterprise.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(2): The division may allow a private individual or entity to purchase compressed natural gas from the state's fuel network if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(2)(a): there is no commercial fuel site that meets the geographical compressed natural gas distribution needs of private individuals or entities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(2)(b): there is no emergency that, as determined by the division, warrants the holding of compressed natural gas in reserve for use by state or emergency vehicles.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (3)(b); (2)(a); (b) In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(a): giving state and local agencies priority to dispense and receive compressed natural gas from the state's fuel network sites;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(b): designating state fuel network sites that may be made available to private individuals and entities for the purchase of compressed natural gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(c): (3)(b) defining the terms of operation for each site designated under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(d): unless otherwise prohibited by law, limiting the amount of compressed natural gas that may be purchased from the state's fuel network by any private individual or entity at any one time, or in the aggregate during any given period of time;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(e): providing conditions upon which a private individual or entity's authorization to purchase compressed natural gas from the state fuel network may be granted, revoked, or suspended under this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(f): (2)(a); (b) to establish or determine compliance with Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-9-702(3)(g): defining the term "geographical compressed natural gas needs of a private individual or entity."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-101 Division of Archives and Records Service created -- Duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-101(1): There is created the Division of Archives and Records Service within the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-101(2)(h): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act develop training programs to assist records officers and other interested officers and employees of governmental entities to administer this chapter and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-101(2)(i): provide access to public records deposited in the archives;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102 State archivist -- Duties.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(1)(a): With the approval of the governor, the executive director shall appoint the state archivist to serve as director of the state archives.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(1)(b): The state archivist shall be qualified by archival training, education, and experience.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2): 63A-12-102.5; 63A-12-102.5 The state archivist is charged with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(a): 63A-12-102.5 the custody and permanent retention and preservation of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(a)(i): the enrolled copy of the original 1895 Utah Constitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(a)(ii): Indian war records;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(a)(iii): oaths of office of all state officials, including legislative officials, required under Article IV, Section 10 of the Utah Constitution to take an oath of office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(a)(iv): 63A-12-102.5 all other records, excluding legislative records described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(2)(b): 63A-12-102.5 the retention and preservation of legislative records, as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(3)(a): The state archivist is the official custodian of all noncurrent records of permanent or historic value that are not required by law to remain in the custody of the originating governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102(3)(b): Upon the termination of any governmental entity, its records shall be transferred to the state archives.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5 Preservation of legislative records.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1): 63G-9-401 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(a): "Historical legislative record" means a permanent legislative record or a supplemental legislative record that a legislative office transmitted to the state archivist before March 3, 2023, for retention and preservation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(b): "Legislative office" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(b)(i): the Senate, the House of Representatives, or a staff office of the Legislature; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(b)(ii): as applicable, a body designated by the Legislative Management Committee to be responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(b)(ii)(A): the retention of a legislative record; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(b)(ii)(B): the transmission of a legislative record to the division, as provided in this section, if the body chooses to transmit the legislative record to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(c): "Legislative retention schedule" means the retention schedule attached as Appendix A to the Legislative Management Committee Policy L. Legislative Records.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d): 63G-9-401 "Permanent legislative record" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(i): a joint proclamation issued by the president of the Senate and the speaker of the House of Representatives convening a session of the Legislature under Article VI, Section 2 of the Utah Constitution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(ii): a session journal of the Senate or House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(iii): a recording of Senate or House of Representatives floor proceedings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(iv): a numbered bill or resolution of the Senate or House of Representatives, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(iv)(A): a public substitute or amendment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(iv)(B): a fiscal note or other information required to accompany a numbered bill or resolution; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(iv)(C): an enrolled bill or resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(v): an introduced article of impeachment or amendment to an article of impeachment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(vi): as prepared by the Legislature and provided to the public, a list of actions taken on legislation during a legislative session or descriptions of the status of legislation considered during a legislative session;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(vii): a notice, agenda, handout or other public meeting material, recording, or minutes of the Legislative Management Committee, Executive Appropriations Committee, standing and interim committees of the Legislature, appropriations subcommittees of the Legislature, audit subcommittees of the Legislature, and other legislative committees, task forces, or commissions, excluding a rules or sifting committee of the Legislature;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(viii): a statutorily required budget or appropriations report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(ix): an audit or review report of the Office of the Legislative Auditor General and a record that supports the conclusions and findings of the audit or review report;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(x): a version of the Utah Code after the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel prepares an updated Utah Code database incorporating any duly enacted legislation making changes to the Utah Code;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(xi): the Laws of Utah;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(xii): a biennial version of the Utah Constitution after the Office of Legislative Research and General Counsel incorporates into the Utah Constitution amendments that passed during the preceding regular general election; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(d)(xiii): 63G-9-401 a notice of appeal under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(1)(e): "Supplemental legislative record" means a legislative record that is not a permanent legislative record.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(2): A legislative office may, but is not required to, transmit a legislative record to the state archivist for retention and preservation as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(3)(a): A legislative office shall consult with the state archivist as the legislative office determines the method and timing of transmitting a legislative record that the legislative office chooses to transmit to the state archivist for the state archivist's retention and preservation as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(3)(b): The transmission of a digital copy of a legislative record is sufficient for purposes of the transmission of the legislative record to the state archivist.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(4)(a): A legislative record that a legislative office transmits to the state archivist for retention and preservation remains in the control and legal custody of the legislative office and, although retained and preserved by the state archivist, does not become subject to the control or legal custody of the state archivist.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(4)(b): The state archivist shall allow a legislative office full and continuing access to any legislative record transmitted to the state archivist for retention and preservation under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(5)(a): The state archivist may not disclose a supplemental legislative record without the prior written consent of the legislative office that transmitted the supplemental legislative record to the state archivist.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(5)(b): If the state archivist receives a subpoena or other request for a supplemental legislative record, the state archivist shall immediately provide written notice of the subpoena or other request to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(5)(b)(i): the legislative office that transmitted the supplemental legislative record to the state archivist; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(5)(b)(ii): legislative general counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(6): The state archivist shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(6)(a): permanently retain and preserve a historical legislative record;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(6)(b): permanently retain and preserve a permanent legislative record that a legislative office chooses to transmit to the state archivist after March 3, 2023; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-102.5(6)(c): retain and preserve, according to the legislative retention schedule, a supplemental legislative record that a legislative office chooses to transmit to the state archivist for retention and preservation after March 3, 2023.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-106 Certified and microphotographed copies.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-106(1): 63G-2-501 Upon demand, the state archives shall furnish certified copies of a record in the state archives's exclusive custody that is classified public or that is otherwise determined to be public under this chapter by the originating governmental entity, the State Records Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-106(2): The state archives may microphotograph records when the state archives determines that microphotography is an efficient and economical way to care, maintain, and preserve the record.  A transcript, exemplification, or certified copy of a microphotograph has the same legal force and effect as the original.  Upon review and approval of the microphotographed film by the state archivist, the source documents may be destroyed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-106(3): The state archives may allow another governmental entity to microphotograph records in accordance with standards set by the state archives.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-107 Right to replevin.
---------------------------------------------------
To secure the safety and preservation of records, the state archivist or the state archivist's representative may examine all records.  On behalf of the state archivist, the attorney general may replevin any records that are not adequately safeguarded.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-108(1)(b): for an executive branch agency, the privacy annotation of each record series.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-108(2): 63A-12-104(3) The department shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-113 Records Management Committee -- Duties.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-12-113(1): 63G-2-604 The Records Management Committee shall:

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63A - Chapter 13 - Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services
***********************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(1): "Abuse" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(1)(a): an action or practice that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(1)(a)(i): is inconsistent with sound fiscal, business, or medical practices; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(1)(a)(ii): results, or may result, in unnecessary Medicaid related costs; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(1)(b): reckless or negligent upcoding.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(2): "Claimant" means a person that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(2)(a): provides a service; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(2)(b): submits a claim for Medicaid reimbursement for the service.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(3): 26B-1-201 "Department" means the Department of Health and Human Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(4): 26B-3-102 "Division" means the Division of Integrated Healthcare, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(5): "Extrapolation" means a method of using a mathematical formula that takes the audit results from a small sample of Medicaid claims and projects those results over a much larger group of Medicaid claims.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(6): 26B-3-1102; 26B-3-1106 "Fraud" means an intentional or knowing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(6)(a): deception, misrepresentation, or upcoding in relation to Medicaid funds, costs, a claim, reimbursement, or services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(6)(b): 26B-3-1102; 26B-3-1106 violation of a provision of Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(7): "Fraud unit" means the Medicaid Fraud Control Unit of the attorney general's office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8): Title 58, Chapter 5a, Podiatric Physician Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 16a, Utah Optometry Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 17b, Pharmacy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 24b, Physical Therapy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 40, Recreational Therapy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 41, Speech-Language Pathology and Audiology Licensing Act; Title 58, Chapter 42a, Occupational Therapy Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 44a, Nurse Midwife Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 49, Dietitian Certification Act; Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 69, Dentist and Dental Hygienist Practice Act; Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act; Title 58, Chapter 73, Chiropractic Physician Practice Act "Health care professional" means a person licensed under:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(a): Title 58, Chapter 5a, Podiatric Physician Licensing Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(b): Title 58, Chapter 16a, Utah Optometry Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(c): Title 58, Chapter 17b, Pharmacy Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(d): Title 58, Chapter 24b, Physical Therapy Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(e): Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(i): Title 58, Chapter 44a, Nurse Midwife Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(j): Title 58, Chapter 49, Dietitian Certification Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(k): Title 58, Chapter 60, Mental Health Professional Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(l): Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(8)(p): Title 58, Chapter 73, Chiropractic Physician Practice Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(9): 63A-13-201 "Inspector general" means the inspector general of the office, appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(10): 63A-13-201 "Office" means the Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(11): "Provider" means a person that provides:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(11)(a): medical assistance, including supplies or services, in exchange, directly or indirectly, for Medicaid funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(11)(b): billing or recordkeeping services relating to Medicaid funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(12): "Upcoding" means assigning an inaccurate billing code for a service that is payable or reimbursable by Medicaid funds, if the correct billing code for the service, taking into account reasonable opinions derived from official published coding definitions, would result in a lower Medicaid payment or reimbursement.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(13): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(13)(a): "Waste" means the act of using or expending a resource carelessly, extravagantly, or to no purpose.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(13)(b): "Waste" includes an activity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(13)(b)(i): does not constitute abuse or necessarily involve a violation of law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-102(13)(b)(ii): relates primarily to mismanagement, an inappropriate action, or inadequate oversight.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201 Creation of office -- Inspector general -- Appointment -- Term.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(1): There is created an independent entity within the department known as the "Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services."
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(2): The governor shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(2)(a): appoint the inspector general of Medicaid services with the advice and consent of the Senate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(2)(b): establish the salary for the inspector general of Medicaid services based upon a recommendation from the Division of Human Resource Management which shall be based on a market salary survey conducted by the Division of Human Resource Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3): A person appointed as the inspector general shall have the following qualifications:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3)(a): a general knowledge of the type of methodology and controls necessary to audit, investigate, and identify fraud, waste, and abuse;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3)(b): strong management skills;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3)(c): extensive knowledge of performance audit methodology;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3)(d): the ability to oversee and execute an audit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(3)(e): strong interpersonal skills.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(4): The inspector general of Medicaid services:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(4)(a): shall serve a term of four years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(4)(b): may be removed by the governor, for cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(5): If the inspector general is removed for cause, a new inspector general shall be appointed, with the advice and consent of the Senate, to serve the remainder of the term of the inspector general of Medicaid services who was removed for cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(6): Title 51, Chapter 5, Funds Consolidation Act; Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act; Title 63A, Utah Government Operations Code; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code; Title 63J, Chapter 1, Budgetary Procedures Act; Title 63J, Chapter 2, Revenue Procedures and Control Act; Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act; Title 67, Chapter 16, Utah Public Officers' and Employees' Ethics Act; Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act; Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act; 63A-4-201 The Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(6)(a): is not under the supervision of, and does not take direction from, the executive director, except for administrative purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(6)(b): shall use the legal services of the state attorney general's office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(6)(c): shall submit a budget for the office directly to the department;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-201(6)(d): Title 51, Chapter 5, Funds Consolidation Act; Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act; Title 63A, Utah Government Operations Code; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code; Title 63J, Chapter 1, Budgetary Procedures Act; Title 63J, Chapter 2, Revenue Procedures and Control Act; Chapter 17, Utah State Personnel Management Act; Title 67, Chapter 16, Utah Public Officers' and Employees' Ethics Act; Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act; Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act; 63A-4-201 except as prohibited by federal law, is subject to:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202 Duties and powers of inspector general and office.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1): 63A-13-502 The inspector general of Medicaid services shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(a): administer, direct, and manage the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(b): inspect and monitor the following in relation to the state Medicaid program:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(b)(i): the use and expenditure of federal and state funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(b)(ii): the provision of health benefits and other services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(b)(iii): implementation of, and compliance with, state and federal requirements; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(b)(iv): records and recordkeeping procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(c): receive reports of potential fraud, waste, or abuse in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(d): investigate and identify potential or actual fraud, waste, or abuse in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(e): consult with the Centers for Medicaid and Medicare Services and other states to determine and implement best practices for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(e)(i): educating and communicating with health care professionals and providers about program and audit policies and procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(e)(ii): discovering and eliminating fraud, waste, and abuse of Medicaid funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(e)(iii): differentiating between honest mistakes and intentional errors, or fraud, waste, and abuse, if the office enters into settlement negotiations with the provider or health care professional;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(f): obtain, develop, and utilize computer algorithms to identify fraud, waste, or abuse in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(g): work closely with the fraud unit to identify and recover improperly or fraudulently expended Medicaid funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(h): audit, inspect, and evaluate the functioning of the division for the purpose of making recommendations to the Legislature and the department to ensure that the state Medicaid program is managed:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(h)(i): in the most efficient and cost-effective manner possible; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(h)(ii): in a manner that promotes adequate provider and health care professional participation and the provision of appropriate health benefits and services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(i): regularly advise the department and the division of an action that could be taken to ensure that the state Medicaid program is managed in the most efficient and cost-effective manner possible;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(j): refer potential criminal conduct, relating to Medicaid funds or the state Medicaid program, to the fraud unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(k): refer potential criminal conduct, including relevant data from the controlled substance database, relating to Medicaid fraud, to law enforcement in accordance with Title 58, Chapter 37f, Controlled Substance Database Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(l): determine ways to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(l)(i): identify, prevent, and reduce fraud, waste, and abuse in the state Medicaid program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(l)(ii): balance efforts to reduce costs and avoid or minimize increased costs of the state Medicaid program with the need to encourage robust health care professional and provider participation in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(m): recover improperly paid Medicaid funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(n): track recovery of Medicaid funds by the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(o): 63A-13-502 in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(o)(i): report on the actions and findings of the inspector general; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(o)(ii): make recommendations to the Legislature and the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(p): provide training to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(p)(i): agencies and employees on identifying potential fraud, waste, or abuse of Medicaid funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(p)(ii): health care professionals and providers on program and audit policies and compliance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(q): develop and implement principles and standards for the fulfillment of the duties of the inspector general, based on principles and standards used by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(q)(i): the Federal Offices of Inspector General;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(q)(ii): the Association of Inspectors General; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(1)(q)(iii): the United States Government Accountability Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2): 63A-13-301; 36-35-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(a): 63A-13-301 The office may, in fulfilling the duties under Subsection (1), conduct a performance or financial audit of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(a)(i): 63A-13-301 a state executive branch entity or a local government entity, including an entity described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(a)(i)(A): manages or oversees a state Medicaid program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(a)(i)(B): manages or oversees the use or expenditure of state or federal Medicaid funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(a)(ii): Medicaid funds received by a person by a grant from, or under contract with, a state executive branch entity or a local government entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(b): 36-35-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(b)(i): The office may not, in fulfilling the duties under Subsection (1), amend the state Medicaid program or change the policies and procedures of the state Medicaid program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(b)(ii): 36-35-102 The office shall identify conflicts between the state Medicaid plan, department administrative rules, Medicaid provider manuals, and Medicaid information bulletins and recommend that the department reconcile inconsistencies.  If the department does not reconcile the inconsistencies, the office shall report the inconsistencies to the Legislature's Rules Review and General Oversight Committee created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(b)(iii): Beginning July 1, 2013, the office shall review a Medicaid provider manual and a Medicaid information bulletin in accordance with Subsection (2)(b)(ii), prior to the department making the provider manual or Medicaid information bulletin available to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(2)(c): Beginning July 1, 2013, the Department of Health and Human Services shall submit a Medicaid provider manual and a Medicaid information bulletin to the office for the review required by Subsection (2)(b)(ii) prior to releasing the document to the public.  The department and the Office of Inspector General of Medicaid Services shall enter into a memorandum of understanding regarding the timing of the review process under Subsection (2)(b)(iii).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(3)(a): The office shall, in fulfilling the duties under this section to investigate, discover, and recover fraud, waste, and abuse in the Medicaid program, apply the state Medicaid plan, department administrative rules, Medicaid provider manuals, and Medicaid information bulletins in effect at the time the medical services were provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(3)(b): A health care provider may rely on the policy interpretation included in a current Medicaid provider manual or a current Medicaid information bulletin that is available to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-202(4): The inspector general of Medicaid services, or a designee of the inspector general of Medicaid services within the office, may take a sworn statement or administer an oath.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-203 Memorandum of understanding with fraud unit.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
The inspector general shall enter into a memorandum of understanding with the fraud unit to:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-203(1): formalize communication, cooperation, coordination of efforts, and the sharing of information, on a regular basis, between the office and the fraud unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-203(2): provide for reporting criminal activity discovered by the office to the fraud unit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-203(3): ensure that investigations and other actions by the office and the fraud unit do not conflict; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-203(4): provide for the sharing and classification of records between the office and the fraud unit under the Government Records Access and Management Act.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205 Placement of hold on claims for reimbursement -- Injunction.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(1): The inspector general or the inspector general's designee may, without prior notice, order a hold on the payment of a claim for reimbursement submitted by a claimant if there is reasonable cause to believe that the claim, or payment of the claim, constitutes fraud, waste, or abuse, or is otherwise inaccurate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(2): (1) The office shall, within seven days after the day on which a hold described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(3): The inspector general or the inspector general's designee may not maintain a hold longer than is necessary to determine whether the claim, or payment of the claim, constitutes fraud, waste, or abuse, or is otherwise inaccurate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(4): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act A claimant may, at any time during which a hold is in place, appeal the hold under
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(5): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act If a claim is approved or denied before a hearing is held under
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(6): The inspector general may request that the attorney general's office seek an injunction to prevent a person from disposing of an asset that is potentially subject to recovery by the state to recover funds due to a person's fraud or abuse.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-205(7): The department and the division shall fully comply with a hold ordered under this section.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301 Access to records -- Retention of designation under Government Records Access and Management Act.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1): 63A-13-202 In order to fulfill the duties described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(a): the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(b): state or federal Medicaid funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(c): the provision of Medicaid related services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(d): the regulation or management of any aspect of the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(e): the use or expenditure of state or federal Medicaid funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(f): suspected or proven fraud, waste, or abuse of state or federal Medicaid funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(g): Medicaid program policies, practices, and procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(h): monitoring of Medicaid services or funds; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(1)(i): a fatality review of a person who received Medicaid funded services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(2): The office shall have access to information in any database maintained by the state or a local government to verify identity, income, employment status, or other factors that affect eligibility for Medicaid services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(3): The records described in Subsections (1) and (2) include records held or maintained by the department, the division, the Department of Health and Human Services, the Department of Workforce Services, a local health department, a local mental health authority, or a school district.  The records described in Subsection (1) include records held or maintained by a provider.  When conducting an audit of a provider, the office shall, to the extent possible, limit the records accessed to the scope of the audit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4): A record, described in Subsection (1) or (2), that is accessed or copied by the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4)(a): may be reviewed or copied by the office during normal business hours, unless otherwise requested by the provider or health care professional under Subsection (4)(b);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4)(b): unless there is a credible allegation of fraud, shall be accessed, reviewed, and copied in a manner, on a day, and at a time that is minimally disruptive to the health care professional's or provider's care of patients, as requested by the health care professional or provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4)(c): may be submitted electronically;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4)(d): may be submitted together with other records for multiple claims; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(4)(e): if it is a government record, shall retain the classification made by the entity responsible for the record, under Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(5): Except as provided in Subsection (7), notwithstanding any provision of state law to the contrary, the office shall have the same access to all records, information, and databases to which the department or the division has access.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(6): The office shall comply with the requirements of federal law, including the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 and 42 C.F.R., Part 2, relating to the office's:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(6)(a): access, review, retention, and use of records; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(6)(b): use of information included in, or derived from, records.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(7): The office's access to data held by the Department of Health and Human Services under Title 26B, Chapter 8, Part 5, Utah Health Data Authority:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(7)(a): is not subject to this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-301(7)(b): is subject to Title 26B, Chapter 8, Part 5, Utah Health Data Authority.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-303 Cooperation and support.
---------------------------------------------------------
The department, the division, each consultant or contractor of the department or division, and each provider shall provide its full cooperation and support to the inspector general and the office in fulfilling the duties of the inspector general and the office.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-304 Interference with an investigation or audit prohibited.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No person may:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-304(1): interfere with or impede an investigation or audit of the office or fraud unit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-304(2): interfere with the office relative to the content of a report, the conclusions reached in a report, or the manner of disclosing the results and findings of the office.
