Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(iv): the recovery of fraudulent or improper use of state and federal Medicaid funds, including total dollars recovered through cash recovery, credit adjustments, and rebilled claims;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(v): measures taken by the state to discover and reduce fraud, waste, and abuse in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(vi): audits conducted by the office, including performance and financial audits;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(vii): investigations conducted by the office and the results of those investigations, including preliminary investigations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(viii): administrative and educational efforts made by the office and the division to improve compliance with Medicaid program policies and requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(ix): total cost avoidance attributed to an office policy or action;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(x): the number of complaints against Medicaid recipients received and disposition of those complaints;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(xi): the number of educational activities that the office provided to a provider or a state agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(xii): 63A-13-501 the number of credible allegations of fraud referred to the Medicaid fraud control unit under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(a)(xiii): the number of data pulls performed and general results of those pulls;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(b): recommendations on action that should be taken by the Legislature or the governor to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(b)(i): improve the discovery and reduction of fraud, waste, and abuse in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(b)(ii): improve the recovery of fraudulently or improperly used Medicaid funds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(b)(iii): reduce costs and avoid or minimize increased costs in the state Medicaid program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(c): recommendations relating to rules, policies, or procedures of a state or local government entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-13-502(2)(d): services provided by the state Medicaid program that exceed industry standards.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63A - Chapter 14 - Review of Executive Branch Ethics Complaints
*******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-101(1): This chapter is known as "Review of Executive Branch Ethics Complaints."
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-101(2): This part is known as "General Provisions."


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(1): 63A-14-202 "Commission" means the Independent Executive Branch Ethics Commission, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(2): 63A-14-402(1)(a) "Complainant" means an individual who files a complaint under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3): "Executive branch elected official" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3)(a): the governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3)(b): the lieutenant governor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3)(c): the state auditor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3)(d): the state treasurer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(3)(e): the attorney general.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(4): "Improper purpose" includes harassing a respondent, causing unwarranted harm to a respondent's reputation, or causing unnecessary expenditure of public funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(5): "Malfeasance in office" means an intentional act or omission relating to the duties of an executive branch elected official that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(5)(a): constitutes a crime; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(5)(b)(i): constitutes a substantial breach of the trust imposed upon the executive branch elected official by the nature of the official's office; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(5)(b)(ii): is against commonly accepted standards of honesty and morality.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(6): 63A-14-402 "Respondent" means the executive branch elected official against whom an ethics complaint described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-102(7): "Violation" means a high crime, a misdemeanor, or malfeasance in office.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-201 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "Independent Executive Branch Ethics Commission."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202 Independent Executive Branch Ethics Commission -- Membership.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1): (1)(a); (1)(b)(i); (1)(b)(i); (1)(b)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a): There is created the Independent Executive Branch Ethics Commission, consisting of the following five members appointed by the governor, each of whom shall be registered to vote in the state at the time of appointment:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(i): two members who served:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(i)(A): as elected officials in state government no more recently than four years before the day on which the member is appointed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(i)(B): in a management position in the state executive branch no more recently than four years before the day on which the member is appointed;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(ii): one member who:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(ii)(A): has served, but no longer actively serves, as a judge of a court in the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(ii)(B): is a licensed attorney in the state and is not, and has not been, a judge; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(a)(iii): two citizen members.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b): (1)(a); (1)(b)(i); (1)(b)(i); (1)(b)(ii) The governor shall make appointments to the commission as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b)(i): (1)(a) each executive branch elected official, other than the governor, shall select, and provide to the governor, at least two names for potential appointment to one of the membership positions described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b)(ii): (1)(b)(i) the governor shall determine which of the executive branch elected officials described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b)(iii): (1)(b)(i) the governor shall appoint to the commission one of the names provided by each executive branch elected official described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b)(iv): the governor shall directly appoint the remaining member of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(1)(b)(v): (1)(b)(ii) if an executive branch elected official fails to submit names to the governor within 15 days after the day on which the governor makes the determination described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(2): 20A-11-101; 67-16-3; 36-11-102; 36-11-102 A member of the commission may not, during the member's term of office on the commission, act or serve as:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(2)(a): 20A-11-101 an officeholder as defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(2)(e): an employee of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3): (3)(b); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(a): (3)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(b): The governor shall set the first term of two of the members of the commission at two years, so that approximately half of the commission is appointed, or reappointed, every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(c): (1) When a vacancy occurs in the commission's membership for any reason, the governor shall appoint a replacement member for the unexpired term of the vacating member, in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(d): The governor may not appoint a member to serve more than two full terms, whether those terms are two or four years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(e)(i): The governor, or a majority of the commission, may remove a member from the commission only for cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(e)(ii): The governor may not remove a member from the commission during any period of time when the commission is investigating or considering a complaint alleging an ethics violation against the governor or lieutenant governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(3)(f): If a commission member determines that the commission member has a conflict of interest in relation to a complaint, the remaining members of the commission shall appoint an individual to serve in that member's place for the purpose of reviewing that complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(4): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(4)(a): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member of the commission may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and expenses incurred in the performance of the member's official duties at the rates established by the Division of Finance under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(4)(b): A member may decline to receive per diem and expenses for the member's service.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(5)(a): The commission members shall convene a meeting annually each January and elect, by majority vote, a chair from among the commission members.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(5)(b): An individual may not serve as chair for more than two consecutive years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(6): The commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(6)(a): is an independent entity established within the department for budgetary and general administrative purposes only; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-202(6)(b): is not under the direction or control of the department, the executive director, or any other officer or employee of the department.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203 Independent Executive Branch Ethics Commission -- Meetings -- Annual summary report -- Staff -- Legal counsel -- Supplemental appropriations.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(1): The commission shall meet for the purpose of reviewing an ethics complaint when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(1)(a): except as otherwise expressly provided in this chapter, called to meet at the discretion of the chair; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(1)(b): called to meet by a majority vote of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(2)(a): A majority of the commission is a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(2)(b): A majority vote of a quorum present constitutes the action of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a): The commission shall prepare an annual summary data report that contains:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a)(i): a general description of the activities of the commission during the past year;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a)(ii): the number of ethics complaints filed with the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a)(iii): the number of ethics complaints reviewed by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a)(iv): a summary description of ethics complaints that formed the basis for a commission finding that an allegation in a complaint has merit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(a)(v): an accounting of the commission's budget and expenditures.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(b): The commission shall submit the summary data report to the governor before December 1 each year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(3)(c): The summary data report is a public record.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(4): The commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(4)(a): shall employ a director to provide administrative support to the commission and to assist the commission in fulfilling the commission's duties;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(4)(b): may employ additional staff, to work under the direction of the director;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(4)(c): shall contract with private legal counsel to provide legal services to the commission, as needed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(4)(d): may, in consultation with the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst, request supplemental appropriations to pay the costs of legal fees and other staffing needs that exceed the commission's budget due to the number or complexity of the ethics complaints filed with or considered by the commission in a fiscal year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(5): (5)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(5)(a): (5)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(5)(b): A person employed as staff for the commission may be the same person employed as staff for the Independent Legislative Ethics Commission, if the staff ensures that proper protections are in place to preserve the confidentiality to both bodies and to avoid a conflict of interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-203(6): Except as expressly otherwise provided in this chapter, all meetings held under this chapter are closed to the public.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-301 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "General Powers and Procedures."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302 Authority to review complaint -- Grounds for complaint -- Limitations on filings.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(1): Subject to the requirements of this chapter, the commission may review an ethics complaint against an executive branch elected official if the complaint alleges that the executive branch elected official has committed a violation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(2): The commission may not review an ethics complaint filed against an executive branch elected official unless the complaint alleges conduct that, if true, would constitute grounds for impeachment under the Utah Constitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3): A complaint against an executive branch elected official may not allege a violation by the executive branch elected official for an act by an individual under the authority of the executive branch elected official, unless the complaint evidences that the executive branch elected official:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(b)(i): before the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to engage in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(c)(i): while the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was engaging in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to stop the act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(d)(i): after the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual engaged in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(3)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4): A complaint against an executive branch elected official may not allege a violation by the executive branch elected official for an individual under the authority of the executive branch elected official failing to act, unless the complaint evidences that the executive branch elected official:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(b)(i): before the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to fail to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(c)(i): while the individual was failing to act, knew or should have known that the individual was failing to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(d)(i): after the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual failed to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(4)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the failure to act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(5): Individuals who file a complaint for an alleged violation shall file the complaint within two years after the later of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(5)(a): the day on which the action or omission that forms the basis for the alleged violation occurs or would have been discovered by a reasonable person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(5)(b): the day on which a plea or conviction that forms the basis for the allegation is entered.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(6): (6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(6)(a): A complaint may not contain an allegation that was previously reviewed by the commission, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(6)(a)(i): the allegation is accompanied by material facts or circumstances supporting the allegation that were not raised or pled to the commission when the allegation was previously reviewed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(6)(a)(ii): the allegation and the general facts and circumstances supporting the allegation were only reviewed by the commission on one previous occasion.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(6)(b): (6)(a) If an allegation in a complaint does not comply with the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(7): Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures; Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures; (7)(a); (7)(a); Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures; Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures; 67-19a-201
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-302(7)(a): Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures; Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures An individual may not file a complaint under this chapter that alleges the same conduct alleged in a grievance filed under

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303 General powers -- Jurisdiction.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(1): The commission has jurisdiction only over an individual who is currently serving as an executive branch elected official.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(2): The commission or the chair shall dismiss an ethics complaint if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(2)(a): the respondent resigns from the respondent's position as an executive branch elected official; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(2)(b): the House of Representatives convenes to consider impeachment of the executive branch elected official.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(3)(a): The commission may suspend commission proceedings during a period of time when a criminal investigation or prosecution, based in whole or in part on an allegation in the complaint, is pending.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(3)(b): (3)(a) The time periods and deadlines described in this chapter are tolled during a suspension described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-303(4): The commission does not have jurisdiction over a violation that occurs before March 14, 2013.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-401 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "Ethics Complaints."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402 Ethics complaints -- Filing -- Form.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1): 63A-14-302; (1)(b); (1)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(a): 63A-14-302; (1)(b); (1)(a)(i) The following individuals may file an ethics complaint against an executive branch elected official if the complaint meets the requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(a)(i): two or more executive branch elected officials, deputies of elected officials, executive directors of departments in the executive branch, or directors of divisions in the executive branch, if the complaint contains evidence or sworn testimony that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(a)(i)(A): describes the facts and circumstances supporting the alleged violation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(a)(i)(B): is generally admissible under the Utah Rules of Evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(a)(ii): (1)(a)(i) two or more registered voters who currently reside in Utah and are not individuals described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(1)(b): Complainants may file a complaint only against an individual who is serving as an executive branch elected official on the date that the complaint is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2): (2)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2)(a): The commission shall post, on the state's website, a conspicuous and clearly identified link to the name and address of a person authorized to accept a complaint on behalf of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2)(b): (2)(a) Complainants shall file a complaint with the person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2)(c): An individual may not file a complaint during the 60 calendar days immediately preceding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2)(c)(i): a regular primary election in which the accused executive branch elected official is a candidate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(2)(c)(ii): a regular general election in which the accused executive branch elected official is a candidate, unless the accused executive branch elected official is unopposed in the election.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3): (4) The complainants shall ensure that each complaint filed under this rule is in writing and contains the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(a): the name and position or title of the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(b): the name, address, and telephone number of each individual who is filing the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c): (4) a description of each alleged violation, including for each alleged violation:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(i): a reference to any criminal provision that the respondent is alleged to have violated;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(ii): a reference to any other provision of law that the respondent is alleged to have violated or failed to comply with;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(iii): the name of the complainant or complainants who have personal knowledge of the supporting facts and circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(iv): (4) the facts and circumstances supporting the allegation, which shall be provided by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(iv)(A): copies of official records or documentary evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-402(3)(c)(iv)(B): (4) one or more affidavits, each of which shall comply with the format described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-405 Motion to disqualify commission member for conflict of interest.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-405(1): A complainant may file a motion to disqualify one or more members of the commission from participating in proceedings relating to the complaint if the individual files the motion within 20 days after the later of:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-405(1)(b): the day on which the individual knew or should have known of the grounds upon which the motion is based.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-405(4)(b): (3)(c); (4)(a) is accompanied by a statement, included in the affidavit or declaration described in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-601 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "Ethics Proceedings."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602 Review of ethics complaint by commission.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(1): The scope of the commission's review of a complaint is limited to the alleged violations stated in the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(2): Before holding a meeting for review of a complaint, the chair may schedule a separate meeting of the commission to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(2)(a): review a complaint, with or without the attendance of the parties, to determine if the complaint should be dismissed in whole or in part, by means of a majority vote of the commission, because the complaint pleads facts or circumstances against an executive branch elected official that have already been reviewed by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(2)(b): hear motions or arguments from the parties, including hearing motions or arguments relating to dismissal of a complaint, admission of evidence, or procedures; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(2)(c): hold a vote of the commission, with or without the attendance of the parties, on procedural or commission business matters relating to a complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(3): 63A-14-703
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(3)(a): The commission shall comply with the Utah Rules of Evidence except where the commission determines, by majority vote, that a rule is not compatible with the requirements of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(3)(b): 63A-14-703 The chair shall make rulings on admissibility of evidence consistent with the provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4): 63A-14-703
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a): The following individuals may be present during the presentation of testimony and evidence to the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(i): the complainants, except that no more than three complainants may be present at one time;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(ii): the complainants' counsel, if applicable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(iii): the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(iv): the respondent's counsel, if applicable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(v): members of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(vi): staff to the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(vii): a witness, while testifying before the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(a)(viii): necessary security personnel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(b): 63A-14-703 The complainants, respondent, and counsel for a complainant or respondent may be excluded from a portion of the meeting when the commission discusses administrative, procedural, legal, or evidentiary issues by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(b)(i): 63A-14-703 the order of the chair, subject to override as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(b)(ii): a majority vote of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(4)(c): When the commission deliberates at the conclusion of presentation of testimony and evidence, the commission shall ensure that those deliberations are closed to all persons except for the members of the commission and commission staff.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(5): If a majority of the commission determines that a continuance is necessary to obtain further evidence and testimony, accommodate administrative needs, or accommodate the attendance of commission members, witnesses, or a party, the commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(5)(a): after notice to the parties, adjourn and continue the meeting to a future date and time; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-602(5)(b): establish that future date and time by majority vote.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604 Process for making a decision -- Deliberations.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(1)(a): After each party presents a closing argument, the commission shall, at the direction of the chair, begin private deliberations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(1)(b): (1)(a) The deliberations described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(1)(b)(i): immediately after conclusion of the closing arguments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(1)(b)(ii): at a future meeting of the commission, on a date and time determined by a majority of the members of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(2)(a): The chair shall conduct the deliberations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(2)(b): Upon a motion made by a commission member, the commission may exclude commission staff from all or a portion of the deliberations by a majority vote of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(3)(a): During deliberations, for each allegation reviewed by the commission, each member shall determine and cast a vote stating whether the allegation is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(3)(a)(i): proved, by clear and convincing evidence, to have merit; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(3)(a)(ii): not proved to have merit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(3)(b): A verbal roll call vote shall be taken on each allegation and each member's vote shall be recorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(4)(a): An allegation is determined to not have merit unless four of the five members of the commission vote that the allegation has merit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(4)(b): An allegation that is not determined to have merit is dismissed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(5): 63A-14-605
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(5)(a): 63A-14-605 Before issuing an order or a finding under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(5)(b): A motion to reconsider a vote may only be made by a member of the commission who voted in favor of the vote to be reconsidered.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(6): 63A-14-605 At the conclusion of deliberations, the commission shall prepare an order or a finding in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7): The commission may not find that an allegation has merit if the allegation is based on an act by an individual under the authority of the executive branch elected official, unless the commission finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the executive branch elected official:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(b)(i): before the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to engage in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(c)(i): while the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was engaging in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to stop the act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(d)(i): after the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual engaged in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(7)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8): The commission may not find that an allegation has merit if the allegation is based on the failure of an individual under the authority of the executive branch elected official to act, unless the commission finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the executive branch elected official:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(b)(i): before the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to fail to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(c)(i): while the individual was failing to act, knew or should have known that the individual was failing to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(d)(i): after the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual failed to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-604(8)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the failure to act.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605 Order or finding of merit by the commission.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1): 63G-2-302; (1)(c); 63A-14-403 If the commission determines that all allegations in the complaint are without merit, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(a): issue and enter into the record an order that the complaint is dismissed because no allegations in the complaint were found to have merit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(b): 63G-2-302 classify all recordings, testimony, evidence, orders, findings, and other records directly relating to the meetings authorized by this part as private records under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(c): provide notice of the determination, in a manner determined by a majority vote of the commission, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(c)(i): the respondent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(c)(ii): the first complainant named on the complaint; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(1)(d): (1)(c); 63A-14-403 provide notice to each person named in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(2): (3); (3); 63G-2-302 If the commission determines that one or more of the allegations in the complaint have merit, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(2)(a): if one or more allegations were not found to have merit, enter into the record an order dismissing the allegations that were found not to have merit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-605(2)(b): (3); (3) within 30 business days after the day on which the commission makes the determination, prepare a written finding, for submission to the Legislature, that:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-701 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as "General Provisions Governing Hearings on Ethics Complaints."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702 General procedures for conducting a hearing on an ethics complaint.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1): In conducting a hearing on a complaint, the commission shall comply with the following process in the order specified:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(a): introduction and instructions for procedure and process, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(b): procedural motions, adoption of evidentiary standards, or other general matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(c): complainants' opening argument, to be presented by a complainant or complainants' counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(d): complainants' presentation of evidence and witnesses in support of allegations in the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(e): consideration of motions to dismiss the complaint or motions for a directed verdict, as applicable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(f): respondent's opening argument, to be presented by the respondent or respondent's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(g): respondent's presentation of evidence and witnesses refuting the allegations in the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(h): presentation of rebuttal evidence and witnesses by the complainants, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(i): presentation of rebuttal evidence and witnesses by the respondent, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(j): complainants' closing argument, to be presented by a complainant or complainants' counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(k): respondent's closing argument, to be presented by the respondent or respondent's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(l): deliberations by the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(1)(m): adoption of the commission's findings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(2): (1) The commission may, in extraordinary circumstances, and consistent with due process considerations, vary the order described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-702(3): In addition to witnesses or evidence subpoenaed at the request of a complainant or a respondent, the chair or the commission may, consistent with due process considerations, subpoena and schedule the examination of witnesses or evidence that the chair or the commission determines will assist the commission in making a determination on the merits of the complaint.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703 Chair as presiding judge.
----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(1): Except as expressly provided otherwise in this chapter, the chair is vested with the power to direct the commission during meetings authorized by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(2): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the commission may overrule a decision of the chair if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(2)(a): a member of the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(2)(a)(i): states that the member desires to overrule the decision of the chair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(2)(a)(ii): states the basis for the member's objection to the decision of the chair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(2)(b): a majority of the commission votes to overrule the decision of the chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-703(3): The chair may set time limitations on any part of a meeting authorized by this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704 Subpoena powers.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(1): For all proceedings authorized by this chapter, the commission may issue a subpoena to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(1)(a): require the attendance of a witness; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(1)(b): direct the production of evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(2): 63A-14-706 The commission shall issue a subpoena under this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(2)(a): 63A-14-706 as required under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(2)(b): at the direction of the chair, if the chair determines that the testimony or evidence is relevant to the review of a complaint; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-704(2)(c): upon a vote of a majority of the commission members.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706 Testimony and examination of witnesses -- Oath -- Procedure -- Contempt.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(1): The chair shall ensure that each witness listed in a complaint and response is subpoenaed for appearance at the hearing unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(1)(a): the witness is unable to be properly identified or located; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(1)(b): service is otherwise determined to be impracticable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(2): The chair shall determine the scheduling and order of witnesses and presentation of evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(3): (1); (2); 63A-14-704 The commission may, by majority vote:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(3)(a): (1) overrule the chair's decision not to subpoena a witness under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(3)(d): decline to review or consider evidence submitted in relation to an ethics complaint; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(3)(e): 63A-14-704 request and subpoena witnesses or evidence according to the procedures of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(4)(a): Each witness shall testify under oath.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(4)(b): The chair or the chair's designee shall administer the oath to each witness.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5): After the oath is administered to a witness, the chair shall direct testimony as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5)(a): allow the party that called the witness, or that party's counsel, to question the witness;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5)(b): allow the opposing party, or the opposing party's counsel, to cross-examine the witness;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5)(c): allow additional questioning by a party or a party's counsel as appropriate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5)(d): give commission members the opportunity to question the witness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(5)(e): as appropriate, allow further examination of the witness by the commission, or the parties or their counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(6): 63A-14-705
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(6)(a): If a witness, a party, or a party's counsel objects to a question, the chair shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(6)(a)(i): direct the witness to answer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(6)(a)(ii): rule that the witness is not required to answer the question.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-706(6)(b): 63A-14-705 If a witness declines to answer a question after the chair or a majority of the commission determines that the witness is required to answer the question, the witness may be held in contempt in accordance with the provisions of Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707 Communications of commission members.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(1): As used in this section, "third party" means a person who is not a member of the commission or staff to the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(2): While a complaint is under review by the commission, a member of the commission may not initiate, engage in, or consider any communications concerning the complaint with a third party unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(2)(a): the communication is expressly permitted under the procedures established by this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(2)(b): the communication is made by the third party, in writing, simultaneously to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(2)(b)(i): all members of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(2)(b)(ii): a staff member of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-707(3): While the commission is reviewing a complaint under this chapter, a commission member may communicate outside of the meetings or deliberations with another member of, or staff to, the commission, if the member's communication does not materially compromise the member's responsibility to independently review and make decisions in relation to the complaint.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-708(3)(b): (3)(a); (3)(a) If the Executive Appropriations Committee of the Legislature receives a request described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-14-708(4): An attorney who participates in a hearing before the commission shall comply with:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201 Commission established -- Membership.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(1): There is established a Political Subdivisions Ethics Review Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2): The commission is composed of seven individuals, each of whom is registered to vote in this state and appointed by the governor with the advice and consent of the Senate, as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(a): one member who has served, but no longer serves, as a judge of a court of record in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(b): one member who has served as a mayor or municipal council member no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(c): one member who has served as a member of a local board of education no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(d): two members who are lay persons; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e): two members, each of whom is one of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(i): a municipal mayor no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(ii): a municipal council member no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(iii): a county mayor no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(iv): a county commissioner no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(v): a special service district administrative control board member no more recently than four years before the date of appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(vi): a special district board of trustees member no more recently than four years before the date of appointment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(2)(e)(vii): a judge who has served, but no longer serves, as a judge of a court of record in this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(3): 67-16-3; 36-11-102; 36-11-102; 63A-15-303
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(3)(a): 67-16-3; 36-11-102; 36-11-102 A member of the commission may not, during the member's term of office on the commission, act or serve as:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(3)(a)(i): a political subdivision officer;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(b)(i): When a vacancy occurs in the commission's membership for any reason, a replacement member shall be appointed for the unexpired term of the vacating member using the procedures and requirements described in Subsection (2) or (3)(b), as applicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(b)(ii): For the purposes of this section, an appointment for an unexpired term of a vacating member is not considered a full term.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(c): A member may not be appointed to serve for more than two full terms, whether those terms are two or four years.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(d): A member of the commission may resign from the commission by giving one month's written notice of the resignation to the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(e): The governor shall remove a member from the commission if the member:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(e)(iii): fails to meet the qualifications of office as provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i): If a commission member is accused of wrongdoing in a complaint, or if a commission member has a conflict of interest in relation to a matter before the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(A): the alternate member described in Subsection (3)(b) shall serve in the member's place for the purposes of reviewing the complaint; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(B): if the alternate member has already taken the place of another commission member or is otherwise not available, the commission shall appoint another individual to temporarily serve in the member's place for the purposes of reviewing the complaint.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(ii)(A): is not required to be confirmed by the Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(ii)(B): may be a lay person;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-201(4)(f)(ii)(D): shall comply with Subsection (3)(a).

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-202(6)(c): shall employ a director to provide administrative support to the commission and to assist the commission in fulfilling the commission's duties;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-202(6)(f): may, in consultation with the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst, request supplemental appropriations to pay the costs of legal fees and other staffing needs that exceed the commission's budget due to the number or complexity of the ethics complaints filed with or considered by the commission in a fiscal year.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303 Motion to disqualify commission member for conflict of interest.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303(1): A complainant may file a motion to disqualify one or more members of the commission from participating in proceedings relating to the complaint if the individual files the motion within 20 days after the later of:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303(1)(b): the day on which the individual knew or should have known of the grounds upon which the motion is based.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303(2)(b): the day on which the respondent knew or should have known of the grounds upon which the motion is based.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303(4)(b): (3)(c); (4)(a) is accompanied by a statement, included in the affidavit or declaration described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-303(5): The commission shall dismiss a motion filed under this section, with prejudice, if the motion:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401 Hearing on ethics complaint -- General procedures.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1): Part 7, Commission Review of Ethics Violation In conducting a hearing on a complaint in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(a): introduction and instructions for procedure and process, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(b): complainant's opening argument, to be presented by a complainant or complainant's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(c): complainant's presentation of evidence and witnesses in support of allegations in the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(d): consideration of motions to dismiss the complaint or motions for a finding of no cause, as applicable;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(e): respondent's opening argument, to be presented by the respondent or respondent's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(f): respondent's presentation of evidence and witnesses refuting allegations in the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(g): presentation of rebuttal evidence and witnesses by the complainant, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(h): presentation of rebuttal evidence and witnesses by the respondent, at the discretion of the chair;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(i): complainant's closing argument, to be presented by a complainant or complainant's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(j): respondent's closing argument, to be presented by the respondent or respondent's counsel;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(k): deliberations by the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(1)(l): adoption of the commission's findings.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(2): (1) The commission may, in extraordinary circumstances, vary the order contained in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-401(3): 63A-15-403 The chair may schedule the examination of a witness or evidence subpoenaed at the request of the chair or the commission under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-402 Chair as presiding officer.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-402(1): Except as expressly provided otherwise in this chapter, the chair of the commission is vested with the power to direct the commission during meetings authorized by this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-402(2): (2)(a) Unless expressly prohibited from doing so under this chapter, the commission may overrule a decision of the chair by using the following procedure:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-402(2)(a): If a member objects to a decision of the chair, that member may appeal the decision by stating:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404 Contempt of the commission.
------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(ii): 63A-15-402 failure, without legal justification, to answer a question during a hearing when directed to do so by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(ii)(A): 63A-15-402 the commission chair, unless the direction is overridden by the commission in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(ii)(B): a majority of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(iii): failure to comply with a subpoena or other order issued under authority of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(iv): 63A-15-502 violation of privacy provisions established by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(v): 63A-15-407 violation of the communication provisions established by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(vi): violation of a request to comply with a provision of this chapter by a chair or a majority of the members of the commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(a)(vii): any other ground that is specified in statute or recognized by common law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-404(1)(b): Because the purpose of the Fifth Amendment privilege not to incriminate oneself is to prevent prosecution for criminal action, it is improper for a witness to invoke the Fifth Amendment privilege if the witness cannot be prosecuted for the crime to which the witness's testimony relates.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407 Communications of commission members.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(1): As used in this section, "third party" means a person who is not a member of the commission or staff to the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(2): While a complaint is under review by the commission, a member of the commission may not initiate or consider any communications concerning the complaint with a third party unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(2)(a): the communication is expressly permitted under the procedures established by this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(2)(b): the communication is made by the third party, in writing, simultaneously to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(2)(b)(i): all members of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(2)(b)(ii): a staff member of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-407(3): While the commission is reviewing a complaint under this chapter, a commission member may communicate outside of a meeting, hearing, or deliberation with another member of, or staff to, the commission, only if the member's communication does not materially compromise the member's responsibility to independently review and make decisions in relation to the complaint.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604 Response to ethics complaint -- Filing -- Form.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(1): 63A-15-602(7) The political subdivision officer or employee who is the subject of the complaint may file a response to the complaint no later than 30 days after the day on which the officer or employee receives delivery of an order issued by the commission under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2): (4); (4) The respondent shall file the response with the commission and ensure that the response is in writing and contains the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(a): the name, address, and telephone number of the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(b): (4); (4) for each alleged ethics violation in the complaint:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(b)(i): (4) each affirmative defense asserted in response to the allegation, including a general description of each affirmative defense and the facts and circumstances supporting the defense to be provided by one or more affidavits, each of which shall comply with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(b)(ii): (4) the facts and circumstances refuting the allegation, which shall be provided by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(b)(ii)(A): copies of official records or documentary evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(b)(ii)(B): (4) one or more affidavits, each of which shall comply with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(c): a list of the witnesses that the respondent wishes to have called, including for each witness:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(c)(i): the name, address, and, if available, telephone number of the witness;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(c)(ii): a brief summary of the testimony to be provided by the witness; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(c)(iii): a specific description of any documents or evidence the respondent desires the witness to produce;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(d): a statement that the respondent:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(d)(i): has reviewed the allegations contained in the complaint and the sworn statements and documents attached to the response; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(d)(ii): believes the contents of the response to be true and accurate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(2)(e): the signature of the respondent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(3): Promptly after receiving the response, the commission shall provide copies of the response to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(3)(a): each member of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(3)(b): the first named complainant on the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4): (2)(b)(i); (2)(b)(ii)(B) An affidavit described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4)(a): the name, address, and telephone number of the signer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4)(b): a statement that the signer has actual knowledge of the facts and circumstances alleged in the affidavit;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4)(c): the facts and circumstances testified to by the signer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4)(d): a statement that the affidavit is believed to be true and correct and that false statements are subject to penalties of perjury; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-604(4)(e): the signature of the signer.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703 Commission deliberations -- Standard of proof.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(1): After each party has presented a closing argument, the commission shall, at the direction of the chair, begin its deliberations:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(1)(a): immediately after conclusion of the closing arguments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(1)(b): at a future meeting of the commission, on a date and time determined by a majority of the members of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(2): 52-4-204
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(2)(a): The chair of the commission shall conduct the deliberations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(2)(b): 52-4-204 Upon a motion made by a commission member, the commission may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(2)(b)(i): exclude commission staff from all or a portion of the deliberations by a majority vote of the commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(2)(b)(ii): 52-4-204 close the meeting in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3): (3)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a): During deliberations, for each allegation reviewed by the commission, each member shall determine and cast a vote stating:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(i): whether the allegation is:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(i)(A): proven by clear and convincing evidence; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(i)(B): not proven; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii): for each allegation proven, whether the commission would recommend to the appropriate political subdivision governing body to take one or more of the following actions:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii)(A): censure;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii)(B): in the case of a political subdivision employee, termination;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii)(C): in the case of a political subdivision officer, removal from office; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii)(D): any other action or reprimand that the commission determines is appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(b): (3)(a)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(b)(i): (3)(a)(ii) A verbal roll call vote shall be taken on each allegation, and each recommended action described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(3)(b)(ii): Each member's vote shall be recorded.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4): (4)(a); 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(A); 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(B); 63A-15-704
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(a): An allegation is not considered to be proven unless six of the seven members of the commission vote that the allegation is proven.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(b): (4)(a); 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(A); 63A-15-201(4)(f)(i)(B) The seven members of the commission described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(c): An allegation that is not considered to be proven is dismissed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(d): 63A-15-704
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(d)(i): 63A-15-704 Before the commission issues its recommendation in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(4)(d)(ii): A motion to reconsider a vote may only be made by a member of the commission who voted that the allegation was not proved.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5): The commission may not find that an allegation is proven if the allegation is based on an act by an individual under the authority of the political subdivision officer or employee, unless the commission finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the political subdivision officer or employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(b)(i): before the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to engage in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(c)(i): while the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual was engaging in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to stop the act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(d)(i): after the individual engaged in the act, knew or should have known that the individual engaged in the act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(5)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6): The commission may not find that an allegation is proven if the allegation is based on the failure of an individual under the authority of the political subdivision officer or employee to act, unless the commission finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the political subdivision officer or employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(a): encouraged, condoned, or ordered the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(b)(i): before the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual was likely to fail to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(b)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(c)(i): while the individual was failing to act, knew or should have known that the individual was failing to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(c)(ii): failed to take appropriate action to prevent the failure to act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(d)(i): after the individual failed to act, knew or should have known that the individual failed to act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(6)(d)(ii): failed to take appropriate action in response to the failure to act.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-703(7): 63A-15-704; 63A-15-705 At the conclusion of deliberations, the commission shall prepare the commission's recommendations as provided in Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704 Recommendations of commission.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a): If the commission determines that no allegations in the complaint were proved, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(i): issue and enter into the record an order that the complaint is dismissed because no allegations in the complaint were found to have been proved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(ii): provide notice of the determination at a public meeting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(iii): provide written notice of the determination to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(iii)(A): the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(iii)(B): the first complainant named on the complaint; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(1)(a)(iii)(C): the appropriate political subdivision.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2): 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii) If the commission determines that one or more of the allegations in the complaint were proved, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(a): if one or more allegations were not found to have been proven, enter into the record an order dismissing those unproven allegations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b): 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii) prepare a written recommendation to the applicable political subdivision governing body that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(i): lists the name of each complainant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(ii): lists the name of the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iii): states the date of the recommendation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iv): for each allegation that was found to be proven:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iv)(A): provides a reference to the statute or criminal provision allegedly violated;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iv)(B): states the number and names of commission members voting that the allegation was proved and the number and names of commission members voting that the allegation was not proved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iv)(C): at the option of those members voting that the allegation was proved, includes a statement by one or all of those members stating the reasons for voting that the allegation was proved; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(iv)(D): at the option of those members voting that the allegation was not proved, includes a statement by one or all of those members stating the reasons for voting that the allegation was not proved;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(v): contains any general statement that is adopted for inclusion in the recommendation by a majority of the members of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(vi): contains a statement referring the allegations found to have been proved to the appropriate political subdivision governing body for review and, if necessary, further action;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(vii): 63A-15-703(3)(a)(ii) contains a statement referring to each allegation proven the commission's recommendation under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(viii): states the name of each member of the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(2)(b)(ix): is signed by each commission member.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3): (4) The commission shall provide notice of the determination:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3)(a): at a public meeting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3)(b): (4) in writing to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3)(b)(i): the respondent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3)(b)(ii): the first complainant named on the complaint; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(3)(b)(iii): (4) in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(4): (3) The commission shall ensure that, within 10 business days of the date of public issuance of the determination in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(4)(a): a cover letter referring the proven allegations contained in the complaint to the political subdivision governing body for review;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(4)(b): a copy of the complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(4)(c): a copy of the response; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-15-704(4)(d): a copy of the commission's recommendation.
