Utah Code Annotated - Title 63A - Chapter 16 - Utah Technology Governance Act
*****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah Technology Governance Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(1): 63A-16-201 "Chief information officer" means the chief information officer appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(2): "Data center" means a centralized repository for the storage, management, and dissemination of data.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(3): "Division" means the Division of Technology Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4): "Enterprise architecture" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a): information technology assets and functions that can be applied across state government, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(i): mainframes, servers, desktop devices, peripherals, and other computing devices;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(ii): networks;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(iii): enterprise-wide applications;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(iv): maintenance and help desk functions for common hardware and applications;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(v): standards for other computing devices, operating systems, common applications, and software; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(a)(vi): master contracts that are available for use by agencies for various systems, including operating systems, databases, enterprise resource planning and customer relationship management software, application development services, and enterprise integration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(b): support for information technology that can be applied across state government, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(b)(i): technical support;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(b)(ii): master software licenses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(4)(b)(iii): hardware and software standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5): 63E-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(a): "Executive branch agency" means an agency or administrative subunit of state government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b): 63E-1-102 "Executive branch agency" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(i): the legislative branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(ii): the judicial branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(iii): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(iv): the Utah Board of Higher Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(v): institutions of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(vi): 63E-1-102 independent entities as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(vii): the following elective constitutional offices of the executive department:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(vii)(A): the state auditor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(vii)(B): the state treasurer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(5)(b)(vii)(C): the attorney general.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(6): 63A-16-202 "Executive branch strategic plan" means the executive branch strategic plan created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(7): "Individual with a disability" means an individual with a condition that meets the definition of "disability" in 42 U.S.C. Sec. 12102.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8): "Information technology" means all computerized and auxiliary automated information handling, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(a): systems design and analysis;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(b): acquisition, storage, and conversion of data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(c): computer programming;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(d): information storage and retrieval;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(e): voice, video, and data communications;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(f): requisite systems controls;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(g): simulation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(8)(h): all related interactions between people and machines.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-102(9): "State information architecture" means a logically consistent set of principles, policies, and standards that guide the engineering of state government's information technology and infrastructure in a way that ensures alignment with state government's business and service needs.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-103 Division of Technology Services.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-103(1): There is created within the department the Division of Technology Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-103(2): 63J-1-410 The division has authority to operate as an internal service fund agency as provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104 Duties of division.
----------------------------------------------------
The division shall:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1): lead state executive branch agency efforts to establish and reengineer the state's information technology architecture with the goal of coordinating central and individual agency information technology in a manner that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1)(a): ensures compliance with the executive branch agency strategic plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1)(b): ensures that cost-effective, efficient information and communication systems and resources are being used by agencies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1)(b)(i): reduce data, hardware, and software redundancy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1)(b)(ii): improve system interoperability and data accessibility between agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(1)(b)(iii): meet the agency's and user's business and service needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(2): coordinate an executive branch strategic plan for all agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(3): develop and implement processes to replicate information technology best practices and standards throughout the executive branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(4): once every three years:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(4)(a): conduct an information technology security assessment via an independent third party:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(4)(a)(i): to evaluate the adequacy of the division's and the executive branch agencies' data and information technology system security standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(4)(a)(ii): that will be completed over a period that does not exceed two years; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(4)(b): communicate the results of the assessment described in Subsection (4)(a) to the appropriate executive branch agencies and to the president of the Senate and the speaker of the House of Representatives;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(5): 63G-6a-109.5; 63G-6a-109.5 subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(5)(a): advise executive branch agencies on project and contract management principles as they relate to information technology projects within the executive branch; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(5)(b): 63G-6a-109.5 approve the acquisition of technology services and products by executive branch agencies as required under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(6): work toward building stronger partnering relationships with providers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(7): develop service level agreements with executive branch departments and agencies to ensure quality products and services are delivered on schedule and within budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(8): develop standards for application development including a standard methodology and cost-benefit analysis that all agencies shall utilize for application development activities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(9): determine and implement statewide efforts to standardize data elements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10): 63A-16-209 coordinate with executive branch agencies to provide basic website standards for agencies that address common design standards and navigation standards, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(a): 63A-16-209 accessibility for individuals with disabilities in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(a)(i): the standards of 29 U.S.C. Sec. 794d; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(a)(ii): 63A-16-209 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(b): consistency with standardized government security standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(c): designing around user needs with data-driven analysis influencing management and development decisions, using qualitative and quantitative data to determine user goals, needs, and behaviors, and continual testing of the website, web-based form, web-based application, or digital service to ensure that user needs are addressed;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(d): providing users of the website, web-based form, web-based application, or digital service with the option for a more customized digital experience that allows users to complete digital transactions in an efficient and accurate manner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(10)(e): full functionality and usability on common mobile devices;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(11): consider, when making a purchase for an information system, cloud computing options, including any security benefits, privacy, data retention risks, and cost savings associated with cloud computing options;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(12): 63A-16-201 develop systems and methodologies to review, evaluate, and prioritize existing information technology projects within the executive branch and report to the governor and the Government Operations Interim Committee in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(13): assist the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget with the development of information technology budgets for agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(14): 63G-22-102 ensure that any training or certification required of a public official or public employee, as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(14)(a): under this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(14)(b): by the department; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(14)(c): by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(15): provide support to executive branch agencies for the information technology assets and functions that are unique to the agency and are mission critical functions of the agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(16): provide in-house information technology staff support to executive branch agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(17): establish a committee composed of agency user groups to coordinate division services with agency needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(18): assist executive branch agencies in complying with the requirements of any rule made by the chief information officer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(19): develop and implement an effective enterprise architecture governance model for the executive branch;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(20): provide oversight of information technology projects that impact statewide information technology services, assets, or functions of state government to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(20)(a): control costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(20)(b): ensure business value to a project;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(20)(c): maximize resources;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(20)(e): avoid duplication of resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(21): develop a method of accountability to agencies for services provided by the department through service agreements with the agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(22): serve as a project manager for enterprise architecture, including management of applications, standards, and procurement of enterprise architecture;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-104(23): coordinate the development and implementation of advanced state telecommunication systems;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108 Digital verifiable credential and records.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1): 67-1-17; 63A-12-102; 67-3-13; 26B-8-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(a): "Blockchain" means a distributed ledger of ordered electronic records that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(a)(i): is distributed across a network of computers;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(a)(ii): utilizes technology to prevent the unauthorized alteration of electronic records; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(a)(iii): is mathematically verified.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(b): "Digital record schema" means a description of the data fields and tamper-evident technologies required to create a digital verifiable credential or digital verifiable record that can be registered on a distributed ledger technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(c): "Digital signature" means a tamper-evident, immutable, electronic seal that is equivalent in function and status to a notary seal issued by a government entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(d): "Digital verifiable credential" means a digital document that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(d)(i): attests to a fact;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(d)(ii): is issued by a government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(d)(iii): can be mathematically verified; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(d)(iv): conveys rights, privileges, and legal enforceability equivalent to the possession of a physical credential of the same type.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(e): "Digital verifiable record" means a digital record that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(e)(i): is issued by a government entity or has been digitally signed by a government entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(e)(ii): has a digital signature;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(e)(iii): can be mathematically verified; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(e)(iv): conveys rights, privileges, and legal enforceability equivalent to the possession of a physical record of the same type.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(f): "Distributed ledger" means a decentralized database that is maintained by the consensus of replicated, shared, and synchronized digital data.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(g): "Government entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(g)(i): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(g)(ii): a state agency; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(g)(iii): a political subdivision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(h): 67-1-17 "Government operations privacy officer" means the government operations privacy officer described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(i): 63A-12-102 "State archivist" means the state archivist appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(j): 67-3-13 "State privacy officer" means the state privacy officer described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(1)(k): 26B-8-102 "State registrar" means the state registrar of vital records appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2): (2)(a); (b) The Division of Technology Services shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(a): provide recommendations to government entities regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(a)(i): appropriate digital record schemas that allow a government to issue a digital verifiable credential or record;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(a)(ii): policies and procedures to protect the privacy of personal identifying information maintained within distributed ledger programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(a)(iii): the manner and format in which an issuer may certify a document through blockchain; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(a)(iv): processes and procedures for the preservation, auditability, integrity, security, and confidentiality of digital verifiable credentials and records;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(b): create a pilot program for the implementation of digital verifiable credentials by governmental entities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(2)(c): (2)(a); (b) report to Public Utilities, Energy, and Technology Interim Committee by October 31, 2023, on the duties described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(3): (2)(a); (b) In performing the duties described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(3)(a): the state archivist;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(3)(b): the state privacy officer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-108(3)(c): the government operations privacy officer;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109 Removal of state elected official or employee personal identifying information.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(a): "Open web" means the Internet used for everyday activities like browsing, searching, reading media, online shopping, or other website or online applications.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(b): "Personal identifying information" means the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(b)(i): physical home address and personal email address;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(b)(ii): home telephone number and personal mobile telephone number;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(b)(iii): driver license or other government-issued identification; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(b)(iv): social security number.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(c)(i): "State elected official" means a person who holds an office in state government that is required by law to be filled by an election, including the offices of governor, lieutenant governor, attorney general, state auditor, state treasurer, and legislator.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(c)(ii): "State elected official" does not include a judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(d): "State employee who has been threatened" means an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(d)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(d)(i)(A): who is a cabinet level official or senior staff of the governor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(d)(i)(B): who is an employee of the state executive branch and meets selective criteria implemented by the division that are established by rule made under Subsection (4); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(1)(d)(ii): whose life or safety has been threatened in the course of performing the individual's state duties through a text, phone call, email, postal delivery, face-to-face encounter, or website or online application.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(2): At the written request of a state elected official or a state employee who has been threatened, the division shall within 30 days of receipt of the request:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(2)(a): search the open web for personal identifying information that is about the state elected official or state employee who has been threatened;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(2)(b): when possible, remove the personal identifying information found under Subsection (2)(a) from the open web; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(2)(c): conduct continuous monthly removal when possible of personal identifying information from the open web.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(3): The chief information officer may contract, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 6a, Utah Procurement Code, with a third party to provide the services described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(4): The chief information officer may by rule made in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, establish requirements related to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(4)(a): what information the state elected official or state employee who has been threatened shall provide the division as part of the request described in Subsection (2);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(4)(b): procedures for submitting the written request to the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(4)(c): establishing the selective criteria used to determine whether a state employee may receive the services described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(5): The division may not charge a rate for the services provided under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(6)(a): In addition to the governmental immunity granted in Title 63G, Chapter 7, Governmental Immunity Act of Utah, the division is not liable for actions performed under this section except as a result of intentional misconduct or gross negligence including reckless, willful, or wanton misconduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(6)(b): This section does not create a special duty of care.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-109(7): A federal, state, or local government record is not subject to this section, even if the government record contains personal identifying information.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(2): The chief information officer may delegate a function of the division only when the delegation results in net cost savings or improved service delivery to the state as a whole or to the unique mission critical function of the executive branch agency.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(3)(b)(iii): a provision for periodic administrative audits by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(3)(b)(iv): a date on which the agreement shall terminate if the agreement has not been previously terminated or renewed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(3)(b)(v): any delegation of division staff to the agency to support the function in-house with the agency and rates to be charged for the delegated staff; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(3)(c): include a cost-benefit analysis justifying the delegation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-207(4): An agreement to delegate functions to an executive branch agency or an institution of higher education may be terminated by the division if the results of an administrative audit conducted by the division reveals a lack of compliance with the terms of the agreement by the executive branch agency or institution of higher education.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214 Zero trust architectures -- Implementation -- Requirements -- Reporting.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(a): "Endpoint detection and response" means a cybersecurity solution that continuously monitors end-user devices to detect and respond to cyber threats.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(b): "Governmental entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(b)(i): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(b)(ii): a political subdivision of the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(b)(iii): an entity created by the state or a political subdivision of the state, including an agency, board, bureau, commission, committee, department, division, institution, instrumentality, or office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(c): "Multi-factor authentication" means using two or more different types of identification factors to authenticate a user's identity for the purpose of accessing systems and data, which may include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(c)(i): knowledge-based factors, which require the user to provide information that only the user knows, such as a password or personal identification number;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(c)(ii): possession-based factors, which require the user to have a physical item that only the user possesses, such as a security token, key fob, subscriber identity module card, or smart phone application; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(c)(iii): inherence-based credentials, which require the user to demonstrate specific known biological traits attributable only to the user, such as fingerprints or facial recognition.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(1)(d): "Zero trust architecture" means a security model, a set of system design principles, and a coordinated cybersecurity and system management strategy that employs continuous monitoring, risk-based access controls, secure identity and access management practices, and system security automation techniques to address the cybersecurity risk from threats inside and outside traditional network boundaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(2): This section applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(2)(a): all systems and data owned, managed, maintained, or utilized by or on behalf of an executive branch agency to access state systems or data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(2)(b): all hardware, software, internal systems, and essential third-party software, including for on-premises, cloud, and hybrid environments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3)(a): On or before November 1, 2023, the chief information officer shall develop uniform technology policies, standards, and procedures for use by executive branch agencies in implementing zero trust architecture and multi-factor authentication on all systems in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3)(b): On or before July 1, 2024, the division shall consider adopting the enterprise security practices described in this section and consider implementing zero trust architecture and robust identity management practices, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3)(b)(i): multi-factor authentication;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3)(b)(ii): cloud-based enterprise endpoint detection and response solutions to promote real-time detection, and rapid investigation and remediation capabilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(3)(b)(iii): robust logging practices to provide adequate data to support security investigations and proactive threat hunting.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4)(a): If implementing a zero trust architecture and multi-factor authentication, the division shall consider prioritizing the use of third-party cloud computing solutions that meet or exceed industry standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4)(b): The division shall consider giving preference to zero trust architecture solutions that comply with, are authorized by, or align to applicable federal guidelines, programs, and frameworks, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4)(b)(i): the Federal Risk and Authorization Management Program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4)(b)(ii): the Continuous Diagnostics and Mitigation Program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(4)(b)(iii): guidance and frameworks from the National Institute of Standards and Technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(a): In procuring third-party cloud computing solutions, the division may utilize established purchasing vehicles, including cooperative purchasing contracts and federal supply contracts, to facilitate efficient purchasing.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(b): The chief information officer shall establish a list of approved vendors that are authorized to provide zero trust architecture to governmental entities in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(c): If an executive branch agency determines that procurement of a third-party cloud computing solution is not feasible, the executive branch agency shall provide a written explanation to the division of the reasons that a cloud computing solution is not feasible, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(c)(i): the reasons why the executive branch agency determined that a third-party cloud computing solution is not feasible;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(c)(ii): specific challenges or difficulties of migrating existing solutions to a cloud environment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(5)(c)(iii): the total expected cost of ownership of existing or alternative solutions compared to a cloud computing solution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6): 63C-25-201; (6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(a): 63C-25-201 On or before November 30 of each year, the chief information officer shall report on the progress of implementing zero trust architecture and multi-factor authentication to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(a)(i): the Public Utilities, Energy, and Technology Interim Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(a)(ii): 63C-25-201 the Cybersecurity Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b): (6)(a) The report described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(i): applicable guidance issued by the United States Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii): the progress of the division, executive branch agencies, and governmental entities with respect to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii)(A): shifting away from a paradigm of trusted networks toward implementation of security controls based on a presumption of compromise;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii)(B): implementing principles of least privilege in administering information security programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii)(C): limiting the ability of entities that cause incidents to move laterally through or between agency systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii)(D): identifying incidents quickly; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-214(6)(b)(ii)(E): isolating and removing unauthorized entities from agency systems as quickly as practicable, accounting for cyber threat intelligence or law enforcement purposes.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508 Statewide Global Positioning Reference Network created -- Rulemaking authority.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(1)(a): There is created the Statewide Global Positioning Reference Network to improve the quality of geographic information system data and the productivity, efficiency, and cost-effectiveness of government services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(1)(b): The network shall provide a system of permanently mounted, fully networked, global positioning system base stations that will provide real time radio navigation and establish a standard statewide coordinate reference system.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(1)(c): The center shall administer the network.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2)(b): When making rules under this section, the chief information officer shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2)(b)(i): network development that serves a public purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2)(b)(ii): increased productivity and efficiency for state agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-508(2)(b)(iii): costs and longevity of the network.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901(1): "Executive branch agency" means a department, division, or other agency within the executive branch of state government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901(2): 63J-4-201 "Governor's budget office" means the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901(3): "Review board" means the Architecture Review Board established within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901(4): "Technology innovation" means a new information technology not previously in use or a substantial adaptation or modification of an existing information technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-901(5): "Technology proposal" means a proposal to implement a technology innovation designed to result in a greater efficiency in a government process or a cost saving in the delivery of a government service, or both.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902 Submitting a technology proposal -- Review process.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(1): Multiple executive branch agencies may jointly submit to the chief information officer a technology proposal, on a form or in a format specified by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(2): The chief information officer shall transmit to the review board each technology proposal the chief information officer determines meets the form or format requirements of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3): The review board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3)(a): conduct a technical review of a technology proposal transmitted by the chief information officer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3)(b): determine whether the technology proposal merits further review and consideration by the chief information officer, based on the technology proposal's likelihood to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3)(b)(i): be capable of being implemented effectively; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3)(b)(ii): result in greater efficiency in a government process or a cost saving in the delivery of a government service, or both; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-902(3)(c): transmit a technology proposal to the chief information officer and to the governor's budget office, if the review board determines that the technology proposal merits further review and consideration by the chief information officer.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903 Chief information officer review and approval of technology proposals.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(1): The chief information officer shall review and evaluate each technology proposal that the review board transmits to the chief information officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(2): The chief information officer may approve and recommend that the division provide funding from legislative appropriations for a technology proposal if, after the chief information officer's review and evaluation of the technology proposal:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(2)(a): the chief information officer determines that there is a reasonably good likelihood that the technology proposal:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(2)(a)(i): is capable of being implemented effectively; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(2)(a)(ii): will result in greater efficiency in a government process or a cost saving in the delivery of a government service, or both; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(2)(b): the chief information officer receives approval from the governor's budget office for the technology proposal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(3): (2); (3)(a) The chief information officer may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(3)(a): (2) prioritize multiple approved technology proposals based on their relative likelihood of achieving the goals described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(3)(b): (3)(a) recommend funding based on the chief information officer's prioritization under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4)(a): track the implementation and success of a technology proposal approved by the chief information officer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4)(b): evaluate the level of the technology proposal's implementation effectiveness and whether the implementation results in greater efficiency in a government process or a cost saving in the delivery of a government service, or both; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4)(c): report the results of the division's tracking and evaluation:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4)(c)(i): to the chief information officer, as frequently as the chief information officer requests; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(4)(c)(ii): at least annually to the Government Operations Interim Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-903(5): The division may expend money appropriated by the Legislature to pay for expenses incurred by executive branch agencies in implementing a technology proposal that the chief information officer has approved.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1001(2): "Criminal justice agency" means an agency or institution directly involved in the apprehension, prosecution, and incarceration of an individual involved in criminal activity, including law enforcement, correctional facilities, jails, courts, probation, and parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1001(3): 63A-16-103 "Division" means the Division of Technology Services created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002 Public safety portal.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(1): The commission shall oversee the creation and management of a public safety portal for information and data required to be reported to the commission and accessible to all criminal justice agencies in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(2): The division shall assist with the development and management of the public safety portal.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3): The division, in collaboration with the commission, shall create:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3)(a): master standards and formats for information submitted to the public safety portal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3)(b): a gateway, bridge, website, or other method for reporting entities to provide the information;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3)(c): a master data management index or system to assist in the retrieval of information from the public safety portal;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3)(d): a protocol for accessing information in the public safety portal that complies with state privacy regulations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1002(3)(e): a protocol for real-time audit capability of all data accessed from the public safety portal by participating data source, data use entities, and regulators.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101 Definitions.
----------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(1): 63A-16-1102 "Cyber Center" means the Utah Cyber Center created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(2): "Data breach" means the unauthorized access, acquisition, disclosure, loss of access, or destruction of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(2)(a): personal data affecting 500 or more individuals; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(2)(b): data that compromises the security, confidentiality, availability, or integrity of the computer systems used or information maintained by the governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(3): 63G-2-103 "Governmental entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-16-1101(4): "Personal data" means information that is linked or can be reasonably linked to an identified individual or an identifiable individual.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63A - Chapter 17 - Utah State Personnel Management Act
**********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utah State Personnel Management Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(1): "Agency" means any department or unit of Utah state government with authority to employ personnel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(2): 63A-17-301 "Career service" means positions under schedule B as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(3): "Career service employee" means an employee who has successfully completed a probationary period of service in a position covered by the career service.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(4): "Career service status" means status granted to employees who successfully complete probationary periods for competitive career service positions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(5): 63A-17-307 "Classified service" means those positions subject to the classification and compensation provisions of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(6): 58-37-2 "Controlled substance" means controlled substance as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(7): 63A-17-307
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(7)(a): "Demotion" means a disciplinary action resulting in a reduction of an employee's current actual wage.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(7)(b): 63A-17-307 "Demotion" does not mean:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(7)(b)(i): a nondisciplinary movement of an employee to another position without a reduction in the current actual wage; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(7)(b)(ii): 63A-17-307 a reclassification of an employee's position under the provisions of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(8): "Director" means the director of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(9): "Disability" means a physical or mental disability as defined and protected under the Americans with Disabilities Act, 42 U.S.C. Section 12101 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(10): 63A-17-105 "Division" means the Division of Human Resource Management, created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(11): "Employee" means any individual in a paid status covered by the career service or classified service provisions of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(12): "Examining instruments" means written or other types of proficiency tests.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(13): 63A-17-106 "Human resource function" means those duties and responsibilities specified:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(13)(a): 63A-17-106 under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(13)(b): under rules of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(13)(c): under other state or federal statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(14): "Market comparability adjustment" means a salary range adjustment determined necessary through a market survey of salary data and other relevant information.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(15): "Probationary employee" means an employee serving a probationary period in a career service position but who does not have career service status.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(16): "Probationary period" means that period of time determined by the division that an employee serves in a career service position as part of the hiring process before career service status is granted to the employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(17): "Probationary status" means the status of an employee between the employee's hiring and the granting of career service status.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(18): "Structure adjustment" means a division modification of salary ranges.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(19): 63A-17-301 "Temporary employee" means a career service exempt employee described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-102(20): "Total compensation" means salaries and wages, bonuses, paid leave, group insurance plans, retirement, and all other benefits offered to state employees as inducements to work for the state.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103 Principles guiding interpretation of chapter and adoption of rules -- Merit principles.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1): The division shall establish a career service system designed in a manner that will provide for the effective implementation of the following merit principles:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(a): recruiting, selecting, and advancing employees on the basis of their relative ability, knowledge, and skills, including open consideration of qualified applicants for initial appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(b): providing for equitable and competitive compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(c): training employees as needed to assure high-quality performance;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(d): retaining employees on the basis of the adequacy of their performance and separating employees whose inadequate performance cannot be corrected;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(e): fair treatment of applicants and employees in all aspects of human resource administration without regard to race, color, religion, sex, national origin, political affiliation, age, or disability, and with proper regard for their privacy and constitutional rights as citizens;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(f): providing information to employees regarding their political rights and the prohibited practices under the Hatch Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(g): providing a formal procedure for advancing grievances of employees:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(g)(i): without discrimination, coercion, restraint, or reprisal; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(1)(g)(ii): in a manner that is fair, expeditious, and inexpensive for the employee and the agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(2): (1) The career service system described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(3): (1) As part of the career service system described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(3)(a): consider comparable experience or ability as equal to education in determining a candidate's satisfaction of minimum qualifications, except when a minimum educational qualification is legally required to perform the duties of the position; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(3)(b): ensure that position descriptions and job postings published by agencies for career service positions are based on the specific skills and competencies required to perform those jobs.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(4): (2); (3) Within existing resources, the department shall create supporting materials that may be used by a political subdivision that chooses to implement competency-based hiring principles that are the same as or similar to those principles described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-103(5): (1); (3) The principles in Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105 Division of Human Resource Management created -- Director -- Chief Human Resources Officer -- Staff.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(1): There is created within the department, the Division of Human Resource Management.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(2): The division shall be administered by a director appointed by the executive director, with the approval of the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(3): The director shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(3)(a): be a person with experience in human resource management;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(3)(b): be accountable to the executive director for the director's performance in office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(3)(c): serve as the chief human resource officer for the state executive branch; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-105(3)(d): advise the governor on human resource matters and policies.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-108 Severability of provisions -- Compliance with requirements for federally aided programs.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-108(1): If any provision of this chapter or of any regulation or order issued thereunder or the application of any provision of this chapter to any person or circumstance is held invalid, the remainder of this chapter and the application of provision of this chapter or regulation or orders issued under it to persons or circumstances other than those to which it is held invalid shall still be regarded as having the force and effect of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-108(2): If any part of this chapter is found to be in conflict with federal requirements which are a condition precedent to the allocation of federal funds to the state, the conflicting part of this chapter shall be inoperative solely to the extent of the conflict and with respect to the agencies directly affected, and such findings shall not affect the operation of the remainder of this chapter in its application to the agencies concerned.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-108(3): Notwithstanding any provisions in this chapter to the contrary, no regulation shall be adopted which would deprive the state or any of its departments or institutions of federal grants or other forms of financial assistance, and the rules and regulations promulgated hereunder shall include standards, provisions, terms, and conditions for personnel engaged in the administration of federally aided programs, which shall, in all respects, comply with the necessary requirements for a qualified human resource system under the standards applicable to personnel engaged in the administration of federally aided programs.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-109 Study of wildland fire related pay plans.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
By no later than June 30, 2021, the division shall complete a comprehensive comparison of federal, state, and municipal wildland fire agencies or departments to recommend whether salary ranges should be adjusted for state employed wildland firefighters.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111 Teleworking progress report.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1)(a): "Mandatory action day" means a day where notice has been issued at least 48 hours in advance by the director of the Division of Air Quality that the concentration of air pollutants measured in a county are predicted to reach or exceed levels of air pollution that are unhealthy for sensitive groups.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1)(b): "Special circumstance day" means a day where predicted heavy snowfall or other situations pose a risk to employee safety or employee health as determined by the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget or a designee of the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1)(c): "Surge telework eligible" means all employment positions identified as telework eligible and employment positions identified as able to telework temporarily for mandatory action days or special circumstance days.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1)(d): "Surge teleworking" means an employee who temporarily teleworks on a mandatory action day or a special circumstance day.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(1)(e): "Telework" or "Teleworking" means an employee working from home, or from an approved worksite other than the location from which the employee would otherwise work, through the use of a computer, the Internet, a telephone, or other technology to complete work-related duties and maintain contact with colleagues, clients, or a central office as needed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(2)(a): The division shall assist each state agency with identifying positions that are surge telework eligible.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(2)(b): The division may identify and distribute to each state agency strategies and best practices to increase the use of teleworking by the agency's employees during mandatory action days and special circumstance days.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(3): The Governor's Office of Planning and Budget or a designee of the Governor's Office of Planning and Budget shall inform each state agency in a timely manner of mandatory action days and special circumstance days.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(4): On or before October 1 of each year, the division shall provide a written report to the Economic Development and Workforce Services Interim Committee describing:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(4)(a): the number of employees and the percentage of employees from each agency that are identified as telework eligible and surge telework eligible;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(4)(b): except for the initial written report on or before October 1, 2021, the number of employees and the percentage of employees from each agency that have teleworked during mandatory action days and special circumstance days during the previous fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(4)(c): for each agency that has not met the target goal of 90% of surge telework eligible employees teleworking on mandatory action days or special circumstance days, impediments to achieving the target goals and recommended strategies to achieve the target goals in the future; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-111(4)(d): for each agency, recommendations for any actions by the Legislature to increase the number and percentage of surge telework eligible employees.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112 Pay for performance management system -- Employees paid for performance.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1): 63A-17-102; 63E-1-102; 63A-17-301 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(a): 63A-17-102; 63E-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(a)(i): 63A-17-102 "Agency" means, except as provided in Subsection (1)(a)(ii), the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(a)(ii): 63E-1-102 "Agency" does not include the State Board of Education, the Office of the State Treasurer, Office of the State Auditor, Office of the State Attorney General, Utah System of Higher Education, the Legislature, the judiciary, or, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b): 63A-17-301
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b)(i): "Employee" means an employee of an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b)(ii): 63A-17-301 "Employee" does not include :
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b)(ii)(A): 63A-17-301 an individual in a schedule AB position, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b)(ii)(B): an individual in a position that is not eligible to receive a retirement benefit under Title 49, Utah State Retirement and Insurance Benefit Act; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(b)(ii)(C): an individual that an agency hires for a time-limited position that will last fewer than 12 consecutive months.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(c): "Pay for performance" means a plan for incentivizing an employee to meet or exceed production or performance goals, in which the plan is well-defined before work begins, specific goals and targets for the employee are determined, and measurement procedures are in place.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(1)(d): "Pay for performance management system" means the system described in Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(2): The division shall establish and, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, make rules for the administration of a pay for performance management system.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3): The pay for performance management system shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3)(a): guidelines and criteria for an agency to adopt pay for performance policies and administer pay based on an employee's performance in furtherance of the agency's mission;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3)(b): employee performance ratings;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3)(c): requirements for written employee performance standards and expectations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3)(d): supervisor verbal and written feedback based on the standards of performance and behavior outlined in an employee's performance plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(3)(e): quarterly written evaluation of an employee's performance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4): In consultation with the division, no later than July 1, 2023, each agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(a): adopt pay for performance policies based on the performance management system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(b): subject to available funds and as necessary, adjust an employee's wage to reflect:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(b)(i): subject to Subsection (5), for a classified service employee, the salary range of the position classified plan for the employee's position; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(b)(ii): an increase, decrease, or no change in the employee's wage:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(b)(ii)(A): commensurate to an employee's performance as reflected by the employee's evaluation conducted in accordance with the pay for performance management system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(4)(b)(ii)(B): in an amount that is in accordance with the guidelines and criteria established for a wage change in the pay for performance management system.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-112(5): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the division shall make rules authorizing a classified service employee to receive a wage that exceeds the salary range of the classified service employee's position classified plan if warranted based on the classified employee's performance rating.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201 Division field offices.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(1): The director may establish a field office in an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(2): The director may assign an employee of the division to act as field office staff.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(3): The director and agency head shall sign an agreement, to be reviewed annually, that specifies:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(3)(a): the services to be provided by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(3)(b): the use of agency facilities and equipment by the field office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(3)(c): protocols to resolve discrepancies between agency practice and division policy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(3)(d): any other issue necessary for the proper functioning of the field office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(4): Unless otherwise provided for in the field office agreement, the agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(4)(a): assign responsibilities and duties to its employees;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(4)(b): conduct performance appraisals;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(4)(c): discipline the agency's employees in consultation with the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-201(4)(d): maintain individual personnel records.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304 Promotion -- Reclassification -- Market adjustment.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(1)(a): If an employee is promoted or the employee's position is reclassified to a higher salary range maximum, the agency shall place the employee's salary within the new range of the position.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(1)(b): An agency may not set an employee's salary:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(1)(b)(i): higher than the maximum in the new salary range; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(1)(b)(ii): lower than the minimum in the new salary range of the position.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(2): 63A-17-307 An agency shall adjust the salary range for an employee whose salary range is approved by the Legislature for a market comparability adjustment consistent with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(2)(a): at the beginning of the next fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(2)(b): consistent with appropriations made by the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(3): Division-initiated revisions in the state classification system that result in consolidation or reduction of class titles or broadening of pay ranges:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(3)(a): may not be regarded as a reclassification of the position or promotion of the employee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-304(3)(b): are exempt from the provisions of Subsection (1).


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305 Appointments to Schedule B positions -- Examinations -- Hiring lists -- Probationary service -- Dismissal.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(1): Each appointment to a position under Schedule B shall be made from hiring lists of applicants who have been selected by competitive procedures as defined by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(2): The director shall publicly announce information regarding career service positions:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(2)(a): for periods of time to be determined by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(2)(b): in a manner designed to attract the highest number of qualified applicants.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(3): The director shall make rules establishing standards for the development, approval, and implementation of examining processes, including establishing a department approved on the job examination to appoint a qualified person with a disability.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(4): Applicants for employment to Schedule B positions shall be eligible for appointment based upon rules established by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(5)(a): The agency head shall make appointments to fill vacancies from hiring lists for probationary periods as defined by rule.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(5)(b): The director shall make rules establishing probationary periods.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(6): Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures A person serving a probationary period may not use the grievance procedures provided in this chapter and in
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-305(7): Career service status shall be granted upon the successful completion of the probationary period.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306 Dismissals and demotions -- Grounds -- Disciplinary action -- Procedure -- Reductions in force.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(1): A career service employee may be dismissed or demoted:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(1)(a): to advance the good of the public service; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(1)(b): for just cause, including inefficiency, incompetency, failure to maintain skills or adequate performance levels, insubordination, disloyalty to the orders of a superior, misfeasance, malfeasance, or nonfeasance in office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(2): An employee may not be dismissed because of race, sex, age, disability, national origin, religion, political affiliation, or other nonmerit factor including the exercise of rights under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(3): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the director shall make rules governing the procedural and documentary requirements of disciplinary dismissals and demotions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(4): If an agency head finds that a career service employee is charged with aggravated misconduct or that retention of a career service employee would endanger the peace and safety of others or pose a grave threat to the public interest, the employee may be suspended pending the administrative appeal to the department head as provided in Subsection (5).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(5): An agency head may not demote or dismiss a career service employee unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(5)(a): the agency head or the designated representative of the agency head notifies the employee in writing of the reason for the dismissal or demotion;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(5)(b): the employee is given five working days to submit a written reply to the agency head and to have the reply considered by the agency head;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(5)(c): the employee is given an opportunity to be heard by the agency head or the designated representativeof the agency head; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(5)(d): after completing the procedural requirements described in Subsections (5)(a) through (c), the agency head finds adequate cause or reasonto demote or dismiss the employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(a): Reductions in force required by inadequate funds, change of workload, or lack of work are governed by retention points established by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b): Under those circumstances:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b)(i): The agency head shall designate the category of work to be eliminated, subject to review by the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b)(ii): Temporary and probationary employees shall be separated before any career service employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b)(iii)(A): When more than one career service employee is affected, the employees shall be separated in the order of their retention points, the employee with the lowest points to be discharged first.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(b)(iii)(B): Retention points for each career service employee shall be computed according to rules established by the director, allowing appropriate consideration for proficiency and seniority in state government, including any active duty military service fulfilled subsequent to original state appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(c)(i): A career service employee who is separated in a reduction in force under this section shall be given preferential consideration when applying for a career service position.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(c)(ii): Preferential consideration under Subsection (6)(c)(i) applies only until the former career service employee accepts a career service position.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(c)(iii): The director shall make rules in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, concerning the manner of granting preferential consideration under Subsection (6)(c)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(d)(i): An employee separated due to a reduction in force may appeal to the department head for an administrative review.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(d)(ii): The notice of appeal must be submitted within 20 working days after the employee's receipt of written notification of separation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-306(6)(d)(iii): The employee may appeal the decision of the department head according to the grievance and appeals procedure of this chapter and Title 67, Chapter 19a, Grievance Procedures.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-401 Examination of payrolls and certification of employee eligibility by the director.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-401(1): The director may examine payrolls at any time to determine conformity with this chapter and administrative rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-401(2): No new employee shall be hired in a position covered by this chapter, and no employee shall be changed in pay, title or status, nor shall any employee be paid unless certified by the director as eligible under the provisions of or rules made pursuant to this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402 Division provides payroll services to executive branch agencies -- Report.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(i): "Executive branch entity" means a department, division, agency, board, or office within the executive branch of state government that employs a person who is paid through the central payroll system developed by the Division of Finance as of December 31, 2011.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii): "Executive branch entity" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(A): the Office of the Attorney General;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(B): the Office of the State Treasurer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(C): the Office of the State Auditor;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(D): the Department of Transportation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(E): the Division of Technology Services;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(F): the Department of Public Safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(G): the Department of Natural Resources; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(a)(ii)(H): the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(i): "Payroll services" means using the central payroll system as directed by the Division of Finance to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(i)(A): enter and validate payroll reimbursements, which include reimbursements for mileage, a service award, and other wage types;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(i)(B): calculate, process, and validate a retirement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(i)(C): enter a leave adjustment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(i)(D): certify payroll by ensuring an entry complies with a rule or policy adopted by the department or the Division of Finance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(ii): "Payroll services" does not mean:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(ii)(A): a function related to payroll that is performed by an employee of the Division of Finance;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(ii)(B): a function related to payroll that is performed by an executive branch agency on behalf of a person who is not an employee of the executive branch agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(ii)(C): the entry of time worked by an executive branch agency employee into the central payroll system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(1)(b)(ii)(D): approval or verification by a supervisor or designee of the entry of time worked.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(2): The division shall provide payroll services to all executive branch entities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-402(3): After September 19, 2012, an executive branch entity, other than the division or the Division of Finance, may not create a full-time equivalent position or part-time position, or request an appropriation to fund a full-time equivalent position or part-time position for the purpose of providing payroll services to the entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-403 Employee cost disclosure.
----------------------------------------------------------
The Division of Finance shall, at least annually, plainly disclose to all state employees the costs of compensation and benefits that are paid by the state in dollar figures.
