Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502 Overtime policies for state employees.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(a): "Accrued overtime hours" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(a)(i): for a nonexempt employee, overtime hours earned during a fiscal year that, at the end of the fiscal year, have not been paid and have not been taken as time off by the nonexempt state employee who accrued them; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(a)(ii): for an exempt employee, overtime hours earned during an overtime year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(b): "Appointed official" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(b)(i): each department executive director and deputy director, each division director, and each member of a board or commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(b)(ii): any other person employed by a department who is appointed by, or whose appointment is required by law to be approved by, the governor and who:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(b)(ii)(A): is paid a salary by the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(b)(ii)(B): who exercises managerial, policy-making, or advisory responsibility.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(c): "Department" means, except as otherwise provided in this section, the Department of Government Operations, the Department of Corrections, the Department of Financial Institutions, the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Services, the Insurance Department, the Public Service Commission, the Labor Commission, the Department of Agriculture and Food, the Department of Human Services, the Department of Natural Resources, the Department of Transportation, the Department of Commerce, the Department of Workforce Services, the State Tax Commission, the Department of Cultural and Community Engagement, the Department of Health, the National Guard, the Department of Environmental Quality, the Department of Public Safety, the Commission on Criminal and Juvenile Justice, all merit employees except attorneys in the Office of the Attorney General, merit employees in the Office of the State Treasurer, merit employees in the Office of the State Auditor, Department of Veterans and Military Affairs, and the Board of Pardons and Parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(d): "Elected official" means any person who is an employee of the state because the person was elected by the registered voters of Utah to a position in state government.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(e): "Exempt employee" means a state employee who is exempt as defined by the FLSA.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(f): "FLSA" means the Fair Labor Standards Act of 1978, 29 U.S.C. Sec. 201 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(g): "FLSA agreement" means the agreement authorized by the FLSA by which a nonexempt employee elects the form of compensation the nonexempt employee will receive for overtime.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(h): "Nonexempt employee" means a state employee who is nonexempt as defined by the division applying FLSA requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(i): "Overtime" means actual time worked in excess of an employee's defined work period.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(j): "Overtime year" means the year determined by a department under Subsection (5)(b) at the end of which an exempt employee's accrued overtime lapses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(k): "State employee" means every person employed by a department who is not:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(k)(i): an appointed official;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(k)(ii): an elected official; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(k)(iii): a member of a board or commission who is paid only for per diem or travel expenses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(l): "Uniform annual date" means the date when an exempt employee's accrued overtime lapses.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m): "Work period" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(i): for a nonexempt employee, except a nonexempt law enforcement or hospital employee, a consecutive seven day, 24 hour work period of 40 hours;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(ii): for an exempt employee, a 14 day, 80 hour payroll cycle;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(iii): for a nonexempt hospital employee, the period the division establishes by rule according to the requirements of the FLSA; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(iv): for a nonexempt law enforcement employee as defined in the FLSA:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(iv)(A): who is employed by the Department of Natural Resources, the period the division establishes by rule according to the requirements of the FLSA; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(1)(m)(iv)(B): who is employed by a department other than the Department of Natural Resources, the period the division establishes by rule in accordance with Subsection (2).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(2): Except for the Department of Natural Resources, the division shall require each department employing a nonexempt law enforcement employee to designate one of the following work periods applicable to that employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(2)(a): 80 hours in a 14 consecutive day payroll cycle; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(2)(b): 160 hours in a 28 consecutive day payroll cycle.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(3): Each department shall compensate each state employee who works overtime by complying with the requirements of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(a): Each department shall negotiate and obtain a signed FLSA agreement from each nonexempt employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(b): In the FLSA agreement, the nonexempt employee shall elect either to be compensated for overtime by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(b)(i): taking time off work at the rate of one and one-half hour off for each overtime hour worked; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(b)(ii): being paid for the overtime worked at the rate of one and one-half times the employee's regular hourly wage.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(c): A nonexempt employee who elects to take time off under this Subsection (4) shall be paid for any overtime worked in excess of the cap established by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(d): Before working any overtime, a nonexempt employee shall obtain authorization to work overtime from the employee's immediate supervisor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(e): Each department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(e)(i): for an employee who elects to be compensated with time off for overtime, allow overtime earned during a fiscal year to be accumulated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(e)(ii): for an employee who elects to be paid for overtime worked, pay them for overtime worked in the paycheck for the pay period in which the employee worked the overtime.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(f): If a department pays a nonexempt employee for overtime, that department shall charge that payment to that department's budget.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(4)(g): At the end of each fiscal year, the Division of Finance shall total all the accrued overtime hours for nonexempt employees and charge that total against the appropriate fund or subfund.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(a)(i): Except as provided in Subsection (5)(a)(ii), each department shall compensate each exempt employee who works overtime by granting the employee time off at the rate of one hour off for each hour of overtime worked.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(a)(ii): The director of the division may grant limited exceptions to the compensation requirement described in Subsection (5)(a)(i), where work circumstances dictate, by authorizing a department to pay an exempt employee for overtime worked at the employee's regular hourly wage if that department has funds available.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(b)(i): Each department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(b)(i)(A): establish in its written human resource policies a uniform annual date for each division that is at the end of any pay period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(b)(i)(B): communicate the uniform annual date to its employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(b)(ii): If any department fails to establish a uniform annual date as required by this Subsection (5), the director of the division, in conjunction with the director of the Division of Finance, shall establish the date for that department.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(c): The overtime authorized for an exempt employee under this Subsection (5) is not an entitlement, a benefit, or a vested right.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(d): At the end of the overtime year, upon transfer to another department at any time, and upon termination, retirement, or other situations where the employee will not return to work before the end of the overtime year:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(d)(i): any of an exempt employee's overtime that is more than the maximum established by division rule lapses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(d)(ii): unless authorized by the director of the division under Subsection (5)(a)(ii), a department may not compensate the exempt employee for that lapsed overtime by paying the employee for the overtime or by granting the employee time off for the lapsed overtime.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(e): Before working any overtime, each exempt employee shall obtain authorization to work overtime from the exempt employee's immediate supervisor.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(5)(f): If a department pays an exempt employee for overtime under authorization from the director of the division, that department shall charge that payment to that department's budget in the pay period earned.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(a): ensure that the provisions of the FLSA and this section are implemented throughout state government;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(b): determine, for each state employee, whether the employee is exempt, nonexempt, law enforcement, or has some other status under the FLSA;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c): in coordination with modifications to the systems operated by the Division of Finance, make rules, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(i): establishing procedures for recording overtime worked that comply with FLSA requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(ii): establishing requirements governing overtime worked while traveling and procedures for recording that overtime that comply with FLSA requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(iii): establishing requirements governing overtime worked if the employee is "on call" and procedures for recording that overtime that comply with FLSA requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(iv): establishing requirements governing overtime worked while an employee is being trained and procedures for recording that overtime that comply with FLSA requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(v): subject to the FLSA and Subsection (2), establishing the maximum number of hours that a nonexempt employee may accrue before a department is required to pay the employee for the overtime worked;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(vi): subject to the FLSA, establishing the maximum number of overtime hours for an exempt employee that do not lapse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(c)(vii): establishing procedures for adjudicating appeals of an FLSA determination made by the division as required by this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(d): monitor departments for compliance with the FLSA; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(6)(e): recommend to the Legislature and the governor any statutory changes necessary because of federal government action.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(7): 63A-17-602; 67-19a-301
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(7)(a): In coordination with the procedures for recording overtime worked established in rule by the division, the Division of Finance shall modify its payroll and human resource systems to accommodate those procedures.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(7)(b): 63A-17-602; 67-19a-301 Notwithstanding the procedures and requirements of Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act, Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(7)(c): Upon receipt of an appeal under this section, the director shall notify the executive director of the employee's department that the appeal has been filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-502(7)(d): If the employee is aggrieved by the decision of the director, the employee shall appeal that determination to the Department of Labor, Wage and Hour Division, according to the procedures and requirements of federal law.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503 Accumulated annual leave -- Conversion to deferred compensation plan.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503(1): The division shall implement a program whereby an employee may, upon termination of employment or retirement, elect to convert any unused annual leave into any of the employee's designated deferred compensation accounts that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503(1)(a): are sponsored by the Utah State Retirement Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503(1)(b): are qualified under Section 401(k) or Section 457 of the Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503(2): (1) Any annual leave converted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-503(3): No employee may convert hours of accrued annual leave to the extent that any hours so converted would exceed the maximum amount authorized by the Internal Revenue Code for each calendar year.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504 Accumulated annual leave -- Annual conversion to deferred compensation plan.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(1): If the Legislature in an annual appropriations act with accompanying intent language specifically authorizes and fully funds the estimated costs of this use, the division shall implement a program that allows an employee, in the approved calendar year, to elect to convert up to 20 hours of annual leave, in whole hour increments not to exceed $250 in value, into any of the employee's designated deferred compensation accounts that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(1)(a): are sponsored by the Utah State Retirement Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(1)(b): are qualified under Section 401(k) or Section 457 of the Internal Revenue Code.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(2): (1) Any annual leave converted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(2)(a): converted into the employee's deferred compensation account at the employee's pay rate at the time of conversion; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(2)(b): calculated in the last pay period of the leave year as determined by the Division of Finance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(3): An employee may not convert hours of accrued annual leave to the extent that any hours converted would:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(3)(a): exceed the maximum amount authorized by the Internal Revenue Code for the calendar year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-504(3)(b): cause the employee's balance of accumulated annual leave to drop below the maximum accrual limit provided by rule.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-509 Organ donor leave.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-509(1): An employee who serves as a bone marrow donor shall be granted a paid leave of absence of up to seven days that are necessary for the donation and recovery from the donation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-509(2): An employee who serves as a donor of a human organ shall be granted a paid leave of absence of up to 30 days that are necessary for the donation and recovery from the donation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-509(3): In recognition of National Donate Life Month, 2015, created by Proclamation No. 9248, 80 F.R. 18511 (April 1, 2015), the department shall distribute an electronic message to each employee during the month of April publicizing the leave offered under this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511 Parental leave -- Postpartum recovery leave.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1): 49-11-1202; 49-11-1202; 63E-1-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(a): "Child" means an individual who is younger than 18 years old.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(b): "Parental leave" means leave hours a state employer provides to a parental leave eligible employee to bond with a child or, in the case of a guardianship appointment, an incapacitated adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c): 49-11-1202 "Parental leave eligible employee" means an employee who, on the date an event described in Subsections (2)(a)(i)(A) through (D) occurs:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(i): is an employee of a state employer;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(ii): is in a position that receives retirement benefits under Title 49, Utah State Retirement and Insurance Benefit Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(iii): accrues paid leave benefits that can be used in the current and future calendar years;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(iv): 49-11-1202 is not reemployed as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(v): is assuming a parental role with respect to the child or the incapacitated adult for which parental leave is requested; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(A): is the child's biological parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(B): is the spouse of the person who gave birth to the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(C): is the adoptive parent of the child, unless the employee is the spouse of the pre-existing parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(D): is the intended parent of the child and the child is born under a validated gestational agreement in accordance with Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 8, Gestational Agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(E): is appointed the legal guardian of the child or the incapacitated adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(c)(vi)(F): is the foster parent of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(d): "Postpartum recovery leave" means leave hours a state employer provides to a postpartum recovery leave eligible employee to recover from childbirth that occurs at 20 weeks or greater gestation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e): "Retaliatory action" means to do any of the following to an employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e)(i): dismiss the employee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e)(ii): reduce the employee's compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e)(iii): fail to increase the employee's compensation by an amount that the employee is otherwise entitled to or was promised;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e)(iv): fail to promote the employee if the employee would have otherwise been promoted; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(e)(v): threaten to take an action described in Subsections (1)(e)(i) through (iv).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(f): 49-11-1202 "Postpartum recovery leave eligible employee" means an employee who:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(f)(i): is in a position that receives retirement benefits under Title 49, Utah State Retirement and Insurance Benefit Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(f)(ii): accrues paid leave benefits that can be used in the current and future calendar years;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(f)(iii): 49-11-1202 is not reemployed as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(f)(iv): gives birth to a child.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g): 63E-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(i): "State employer" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(i)(A): a state executive branch agency, including the State Tax Commission, the National Guard, and the Board of Pardons and Parole;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(i)(B): the legislative branch of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(i)(C): the judicial branch of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii): 63E-1-102 "State employer" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(A): an institute of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(B): the Utah Board of Higher Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(C): 63E-1-102 an independent entity as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(D): the Attorney General's Office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(E): the State Auditor's Office; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(g)(ii)(F): the State Treasurer's Office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(h): "Qualified employee" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(h)(i): a parental leave eligible employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(1)(h)(ii): a postpartum leave eligible employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsections (4) and (5), a state employer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(i): allow a parental leave eligible employee to use up to three work weeks of paid parental leave for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(i)(A): the birth of the parental leave eligible employee's child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(i)(B): the adoption of a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(i)(C): the appointment of legal guardianship of a child or incapacitated adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(i)(D): the placement of a foster child in the parental leave eligible employee's care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(a)(ii): allow a postpartum recovery leave eligible employee to use up to three work weeks of paid postpartum recovery leave for recovery from childbirth.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(2)(b): A state employer shall allow a qualified employee who is part-time or who works in excess of a 40-hour work week or its equivalent to use the amount of parental leave or postpartum recovery leave available to the qualified employee under this section on a pro rata basis as adopted by rule by the division under Subsection (12).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a): Parental leave described in Subsection (2)(a)(i):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(i): may not be used before the day on which:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(i)(A): the parental leave eligible employee's child is born;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(i)(B): the parental leave eligible employee adopts a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(i)(C): the parental leave eligible employee is appointed legal guardian of a child or incapacitated adult; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(i)(D): a foster child is placed in the parental leave eligible employee's care.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(ii): may not be used more than six months after the date described in Subsection (3)(a)(i);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(iii): may not be used intermittently, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(iii)(A): by mutual written agreement between the state employer and the parental leave eligible employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(iii)(B): a health care provider certifies that intermittent leave is medically necessary due to a serious health condition of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(iv): runs concurrently with any leave authorized under the Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993, 29 U.S.C. Sec. 2601 et seq.; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(a)(v): runs consecutively to postpartum recovery leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(b): The amount of parental leave authorized under Subsection (2)(a)(i) does not increase if a parental leave eligible employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(b)(i): has more than one child born from the same pregnancy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(b)(ii): adopts more than one child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(b)(iii): has more than one foster child placed in the parental leave eligible employee's care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(b)(iv): is appointed legal guardian of more than one child or incapacitated adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(c): A parental leave eligible employee may not use more than three work weeks of paid parental leave within a single 12-month period, regardless of whether during that 12-month period the parental leave eligible employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(c)(i): becomes the parent of more than one child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(c)(ii): adopts more than one child;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(c)(iii): has more than one foster child placed in the parental leave eligible employee's care; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(3)(c)(iv): is appointed legal guardian of more than one child or incapacitated adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(a): Postpartum recovery leave described in Subsection (2)(a)(ii):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(a)(i): shall be used starting on the day on which the postpartum recovery leave eligible employee gives birth, unless a health care provider certifies that an earlier start date is medically necessary;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(a)(ii): shall be used in a single continuous period, unless otherwise authorized in writing by the director of the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(a)(iii): runs concurrently with any leave authorized under the Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993, 29 U.S.C. Sec. 2601 et seq.; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(a)(iv): runs consecutively to parental leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(4)(b): The amount of postpartum recovery leave authorized under Subsection (2)(a)(ii) does not increase if a postpartum recovery leave eligible employee has more than one child born from the same pregnancy.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(5)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (5)(b), a qualified employee shall give the state employer notice at least 30 days before the day on which the qualified employee plans to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(5)(a)(i): begin using parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(5)(a)(ii): stop using postpartum recovery leave under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(5)(b): If circumstances beyond the qualified employee's control prevent the qualified employee from giving notice in accordance with Subsection (5)(a), the qualified employee shall give each notice described in Subsection (5)(a) as soon as reasonably practicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(6): Except as provided in Subsections (3)(a)(iv) and (4)(a)(iii), a state employer may not charge parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section against sick, annual, compensatory, excess, or other leave a qualified employee is entitled to.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(7): A state employer may not compensate a qualified employee for any unused parental leave or postpartum recovery leave upon termination of employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(8)(a): Following the expiration of a qualified employee's parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section, the state employer shall ensure that the qualified employee may return to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(8)(a)(i): the position that the qualified employee held before using parental leave or postpartum recovery leave; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(8)(a)(ii): a position within the state employer that is equivalent in seniority, status, benefits, and pay to the position that the qualified employee held before using parental leave or postpartum recovery leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(8)(b): If during the time a qualified employee uses parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section the state employer experiences a reduction in force and, as part of the reduction in force, the qualified employee would have been separated had the qualified employee not been using the parental leave or postpartum recovery leave, the state employer may separate the qualified employee in accordance with any applicable process or procedure as if the qualified employee were not using the parental leave or postpartum recovery leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(9): During the time a qualified employee uses parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section, the qualified employee shall continue to receive all employment related benefits and payments at the same level that the qualified employee received immediately before beginning the parental leave or postpartum leave, provided that the qualified employee pays any required employee contributions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(10): A state employer may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(10)(a): interfere with or otherwise restrain a qualified employee from using parental leave or postpartum recovery leave in accordance with this section; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(10)(b): take retaliatory action against a qualified employee for using parental leave or postpartum recovery leave in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(11): A state employer shall provide each employee written information regarding a qualified employee's right to use parental leave or postpartum recovery leave under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511(12): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the division shall, on or before July 1, 2022, make rules for the use and administration of parental leave and postpartum recovery leave under this section, including a schedule that provides paid parental leave or postpartum recovery leave for a qualified employee who is part-time or who works in excess of a 40-hour work week on a pro rata basis.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5 Safe leave.
----------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1): 49-11-1202; 63A-17-511; 63E-1-102 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(a): "Child" means an individual younger than 18 years old.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(b): "Immediate family" means a qualified employee's:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(b)(i): parent, spouse, child, or sibling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(b)(ii): an individual that the qualified employee claims as a dependent for state or federal income tax purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c): 49-11-1202 "Qualified employee" means an employee of a state employer who:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(i): is in a position that receives retirement benefits under Title 49, Utah State Retirement and Insurance Benefit Act;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(ii): accrues paid leave benefits that can be used in the current and future calendar years;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(iii): 49-11-1202 is not reemployed as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(iv): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(iv)(A): is the victim of domestic violence, sexual assault, stalking, or human trafficking; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(c)(iv)(B): has an immediate family member who is the victim of an incident described in Subsection (1)(c)(iv)(A).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(d): 63A-17-511 "Retaliatory action" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(e): "Safe leave" means paid leave hours that a state employer provides to a qualified employee for a reason described in Subsection (2)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f): 63E-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(i): "State employer" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(i)(A): a state executive branch agency, including the State Tax Commission, the National Guard, and the Board of Pardons and Parole;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(i)(B): the legislative branch of the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(i)(C): the judicial branch of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii): 63E-1-102 "State employer" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(A): an institution of higher education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(B): the Utah Board of Higher Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(C): the State Board of Education;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(D): 63E-1-102 an independent entity as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(E): the attorney general's office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(F): the state auditor's office; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(1)(f)(ii)(G): the state treasurer's office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a): Subject to Subsection (3), a state employer shall allow a qualified employee to use up to one week of safe leave per calendar year for a reason related to, or arising out of, an incident described in Subsection (1)(c)(iv)(A) or (B), including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(i): to obtain services from a domestic violence shelter, rape crisis center, or similar shelter or service program;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(ii): to temporarily or permanently relocate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(iii): to file a complaint or report with law enforcement;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(iv): to enroll a child in a new school;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(v): to meet with a district or county attorney's office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(vi): to attend or participate in a court hearing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(vii): to obtain psychological or emotional counseling;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(viii): to receive medical treatment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(a)(ix): to take another action that is necessary to maintain, improve, or restore the physical, psychological, emotional, or economic health or safety of the qualified employee or the qualified employee's immediate family member.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(b): A state employer shall allow a qualified employee to use the amount of safe leave available to the qualified employee on a pro rata basis, as adopted by rule by the division under Subsection (12), if the qualified employee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(b)(i): is a part-time employee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(2)(b)(ii): works in excess of a 40-hour work week or the equivalent of a 40-hour work week.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(3): A state employer may not grant a qualified employee safe leave under Subsection (2) unless the qualified employee has first exhausted all of the qualified employee's available accrued annual, compensatory, and excess leave balances.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4): The amount of safe leave authorized under Subsection (2):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4)(a): may be used intermittently;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4)(b): may not be used more than two years after the date of an incident described in Subsection (1)(c)(iv)(A) or (B), unless the qualified employee's use of safe leave is for a reason related to, or arising out of, the criminal prosecution of an individual alleged to be the perpetrator of an incident described in Subsection (1)(c)(iv)(A) or (B);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4)(c): runs concurrently with leave authorized under the Family and Medical Leave Act of 1993, 29 U.S.C. Sec. 2601 et seq.;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4)(d): does not increase if the qualified employee or the qualified employee's immediate family member is the victim of more than one of the incidents described in Subsection (1)(c)(iv)(A) or (B); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(4)(e): does not accrue annually.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(5)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (5)(b), a qualified employee shall give a state employer notice at least seven days before the day on which the qualified eligible employee plans to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(5)(a)(i): begin using safe leave; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(5)(a)(ii): stop using safe leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(5)(b): If circumstances beyond a qualified employee's control prevent the qualified employee from giving the state employer notice in accordance with Subsection (5)(a), the qualified employee shall give the state employer each notice described in Subsection (5)(a) as soon as reasonably practicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(6): Except as provided in Subsection (4)(c), a state employer may not charge safe leave against sick, annual, compensatory, excess, or another leave to which a qualified employee is entitled.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(7): A state employer may not compensate a qualified employee for any unused safe leave upon the qualified employee's termination of employment.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(8)(a): After the expiration of a qualified employee's safe leave, the state employer shall ensure that the qualified employee may return to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(8)(a)(i): the position that the qualified employee held before using safe leave; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(8)(a)(ii): a position within the state employer that is equivalent in seniority, status, benefits, and pay to the position that the qualified employee held before using safe leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(8)(b): If, during the time that a qualified employee uses safe leave, the state employer experiences a reduction in force and, as part of the reduction in force, the qualified employee would have been separated from employment if the qualified employee was not using safe leave, the state employer may separate the qualified employee in accordance with any applicable process or procedure as if the qualified employee was not using safe leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(9): During the time a qualified employee uses safe leave, the qualified employee shall continue to receive all employment related benefits and payments at the same level that the qualified employee received immediately before using safe leave, if the qualified employee pays any required employee contribution.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(10): A state employer may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(10)(a): interfere with or otherwise restrain a qualified employee from using safe leave; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(10)(b): take retaliatory action against a qualified employee for using safe leave.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(11): A state employer shall provide each qualified employee written information regarding the qualified employee's right to use safe leave in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(12): On or before January 1, 2025, the division shall make rules, in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, establishing requirements for:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(12)(a): the use and administration of safe leave under this section; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-511.5(12)(b): a schedule that provides safe leave for a qualified employee who is part-time or who works in excess of a 40-hour work week on a pro rata basis.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513 State employer required to provide leave to a legislator on an authorized legislative day.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a): "Authorized legislative day" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(i): the day on which the Legislature convenes in annual general session, and each day after that day, until midnight of the 45th day of the annual general session;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(ii): a special session day;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(iii): a veto override session day;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(iv): an interim day designated by the Legislative Management Committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(v): an authorized legislative training day; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(vi): any other day on which a meeting of a committee, subcommittee, commission, task force, or other entity is held, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(vi)(A): the committee, subcommittee, commission, task force, or other entity is created by statute or joint resolution;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(vi)(B): the legislator's attendance at the meeting is approved by the Legislative Management Committee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(a)(vi)(C): service and payment for service by the legislator is not in violation of the Utah Constitution, including Article V and Article VI, Sections 6 and 7.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b): "Authorized legislative training day" means a day that a Legislative Expenses Oversight Committee designates as an authorized legislative day for training or informational purposes, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(i): chair training;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(ii): an issue briefing;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(iii): legislative leadership instruction;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(iv): legislative process training;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(v): legislative rules training;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(vi): new legislator orientation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(b)(vii): another meeting to brief, instruct, orient, or train a legislator in relation to the legislator's official duties.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(c): "Legislator" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(c)(i): a member of the Utah Senate;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(c)(ii): a member of the Utah House of Representatives; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(c)(iii): an individual who has been elected as a member described in Subsection (1)(c)(i) or (ii), but has not yet been sworn in or begun the individual's term of office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d): "Retaliatory action" means to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d)(i): dismiss the employee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d)(ii): reduce the employee's compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d)(iii): fail to increase the employee's compensation by an amount that the employee is otherwise entitled to or was promised;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d)(iv): fail to promote the employee if the employee would have otherwise been promoted; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(d)(v): threaten to take an action described in Subsections (1)(d)(i) through (iv).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(1)(e): "State employer" means any employer in the state executive branch.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(2): A state employer who employs an individual who is a legislator:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(2)(a): shall grant leave to the individual on an authorized legislative day for the number of hours requested by the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(2)(b): may not interfere with, or otherwise restrain the individual from, using the leave described in Subsection (2)(a); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(2)(c): may not take retaliatory action against the individual for using the leave described in Subsection (2)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-513(3): The leave described in Subsection (2) is leave without pay unless the state employer and the individual described in Subsection (2) agree to terms that are more favorable to the individual.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602 Position classification grievances -- Scope -- Procedure.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(1)(a): For the purpose of position classification grievances, the process that culminates in assigning a career service position to an appropriate class specification is a matter of position classification and may be grieved.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(1)(b): The process that culminates in assigning a salary range to the class specification is not a position classification and may not be grieved as a classification grievance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(a): Upon receipt of a position classification grievance, the director shall refer the grievance to a classification panel of three or more impartial persons trained in state classification procedures.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(b): The classification panel shall determine whether or not the classification assignment for career service positions was appropriate by applying the statutes, rules, and procedures adopted by the division that were in effect at the time of the classification change.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(c): The classification panel may:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(c)(i): obtain access to previous audits, classification decisions, and reports;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(c)(ii): request new or additional audits by human resource analysts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(c)(iii): consider new or additional information.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(d): The classification panel may sustain or modify the original decision and, if applicable, recommend a new classification.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(2)(e): The classification panel shall report the classification panel's recommendation to the director, who shall make the classification decision and notify the grievant.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3): 63G-4-402
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(a): Either party may appeal the director's decision to an impartial hearing officer trained in state classification procedures selected through a public bid process by a panel consisting of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(a)(i): a current or former government employee with experience in human resource management;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(a)(ii): two department executive directors;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(a)(iii): a private sector human resources executive appointed by the governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(a)(iv): a representative of the Utah Public Employees Association.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(b): The successful bid shall serve under contract for no more than three years.  At the end of that time, the division shall reissue the bid.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-602(3)(c): 63G-4-402 The hearing officer shall review the classification and make the final decision.  The final decision is subject to judicial review pursuant to the provisions of Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
In addition to the definitions found in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(a): "Administrative law judge" means an individual who is employed or contracted by a state agency who:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(a)(i): presides over or conducts formal administrative hearings on behalf of an agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(a)(ii): has the power to administer oaths, rule on the admissibility of evidence, take testimony, evaluate evidence, and make determinations of fact; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(a)(iii): issues written orders, rulings, or final decisions on behalf of an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(b): "Administrative law judge" does not mean:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(b)(i): an individual who reviews an order or ruling of an administrative law judge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(1)(b)(ii): the executive director of a state agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-701(2): 63A-17-708 "Committee" means the Administrative Law Judge Conduct Committee created in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704 Hiring of administrative law judges.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(1): (6) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(2): If an applicant for an administrative law judge position is selected for an interview in accordance with applicable law and division rule, the agency shall interview the applicant by means of a hiring panel.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(3): (2) The hiring panel described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(3)(a): the head of the hiring agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(3)(b): the head of another agency, appointed by the director; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(3)(c): the director.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(4): (3) Each individual described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5): After the hiring panel completes the interviews for an administrative law judge position:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(a): the hiring panel shall select the top three applicants for the administrative law judge position; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(b): the head of the hiring agency shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(b)(i): consider any opinions or feedback from the other members of the hiring panel with respect to the top three applicants; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(b)(ii)(A): hire an applicant from the top three applicants to fill the administrative law judge position; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(5)(b)(ii)(B): decide not to hire any of the top three applicants and restart the hiring process to fill the administrative law judge position.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-704(6): This section does not apply to an administrative law judge who is appointed by the governor.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705 Performance evaluation of administrative law judges.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(1): The division shall prepare a performance evaluation for each administrative law judge contracted or employed by a state agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2): The performance evaluation for an administrative law judge shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2)(a): the results of the administrative law judge's performance evaluations conducted by the employing agency since the administrative law judge's last performance evaluation conducted by the division in accordance with the performance evaluation procedure for the agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2)(b): information from the employing agency concerning the administrative law judge's compliance with minimum performance standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2)(c): the administrative law judge's disciplinary record, if any;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2)(d): the results of any performance surveys conducted since the administrative law judge's last performance review conducted by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(2)(e): any other factor that the division considers relevant to evaluating the administrative law judge's performance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(3): If an administrative law judge fails to meet the minimum performance standards the division shall provide a copy of the performance evaluation and survey to the employing agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-705(4): The division shall conduct performance reviews every four years for administrative law judges contracted or employed by an agency.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706 Performance surveys.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(1): All administrative law judges shall be on a four-year staggered cycle for performance evaluations.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(2): The performance survey shall include as respondents a sample of each of the following groups as applicable:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(2)(a): attorneys who have appeared before the administrative law judge as counsel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(2)(b): staff who have worked with the administrative law judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division may include an additional classification of respondents if the division:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(3)(a): considers a survey of that classification of respondents helpful to the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(3)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act establishes the additional classification of respondents by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(4): A survey response is anonymous, including any comment included with a survey response.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(5): If the division provides any information to an administrative law judge or the committee, the information shall be provided in a manner to protect the confidentiality of a survey respondent.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(6): (3) If the division establishes an additional classification, in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7): The performance survey shall include questions relating to whether the administrative law judge's behavior furthers the following elements of procedural fairness:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(a): neutrality, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(a)(i): consistent and equal treatment of the individuals who appear before the administrative law judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(a)(ii): concern for the individual needs of the individuals who appear before the administrative law judge; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(a)(iii): careful deliberation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(b): respectful treatment of others; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(7)(c): providing individuals a voice and opportunity to be heard.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8): The performance survey may include questions concerning an administrative law judge's:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a): legal ability, including the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(i): demonstration of understanding of the substantive law and any relevant rules of procedure and evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(ii): attentiveness to factual and legal issues before the administrative law judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(iii): adherence to precedent and ability to clearly explain departures from precedent;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(iv): grasp of the practical impact on the parties of the administrative law judge's rulings, including the effect of delay and increased litigation expense;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(v): ability to write clear opinions and decisions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(a)(vi): ability to clearly explain the legal basis for opinions;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b): temperament and integrity, including the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(i): demonstration of courtesy toward attorneys, staff, and others in the administrative law judge's department;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(ii): maintenance of decorum in the courtroom;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(iii): demonstration of judicial demeanor and personal attributes that promote public trust and confidence in the administrative law judge system;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(iv): preparedness for oral argument;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(v): avoidance of impropriety or the appearance of impropriety;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(vi): display of fairness and impartiality toward all parties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(b)(vii): ability to clearly communicate, including the ability to explain the basis for written rulings, court procedures, and decisions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(c): administrative performance, including the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(c)(i): management of workload;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(c)(ii): sharing proportionally the workload within the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(8)(c)(iii): issuance of opinions and orders without unnecessary delay.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(9): If the division determines that a certain survey question or category of questions is not appropriate for a respondent group, the division may omit that question or category of questions from the survey provided to that respondent group.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(10)(a): The survey shall allow respondents to indicate responses in a manner determined by the division, which shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(10)(a)(i): on a numerical scale from one to five; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(10)(a)(ii): in the affirmative or negative, with an option to indicate the respondent's inability to respond in the affirmative or negative.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(10)(b): To supplement the responses to questions on either a numerical scale or in the affirmative or negative, the division may allow respondents to provide written comments.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-706(11): The division shall compile and make available to each administrative law judge that administrative law judge's survey results with each of the administrative law judge's performance evaluations.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-707 Complaints.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-707(1): A complaint against an administrative law judge shall be filed with the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-707(2): Upon receipt of a complaint, the division shall conduct an investigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-707(3): If the division's investigation determines that the complaint is frivolous or without merit, it may dismiss it without further action.  A complaint that merely indicates disagreement, without further misconduct, with the administrative law judge's decision shall be treated as without merit.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-707(4): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act The contents of all complaints and subsequent investigations are classified as protected under


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708 Administrative Law Judge Conduct Committee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708(1): There is created the Administrative Law Judge Conduct Committee to investigate, review, and hear complaints filed against administrative law judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708(2): The committee shall be composed of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708(2)(a): the director, or the director's designee, as chair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708(2)(b): four executive directors, or their designees, of agencies that employ or contract with administrative law judges, to be selected by the director as needed.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-708(3): The division shall provide staff for the committee as needed.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709 Procedure for review of complaint by conduct committee.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(1): Upon a determination that a complaint requires further action, the director shall select four executive directors or their designees and convene the committee.  The executive director of the agency that employs or contracts with the administrative law judge who is the subject of the complaint may not be a member of the committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(2): The division shall provide a copy of the complaint, along with the results of the division's investigation, to the committee and the administrative law judge who is the subject of the complaint.  If the committee directs, a copy of the complaint and investigation may also be provided to the attorney general.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(3): The committee shall allow an administrative law judge who is the subject of a complaint to appear and speak at any committee meeting, except a closed meeting, during which the committee is deliberating the complaint.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(4): Title 52, Chapter 4, Open and Public Meetings Act The committee may meet in a closed meeting to discuss a complaint against an administrative law judge by complying with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(5): After deliberation and discussion of the complaint and all information provided, the committee shall provide a report, with a recommendation, to the agency.  The recommendation shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(5)(a): a brief description of the complaint and results of the division's investigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(5)(b): the committee's findings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(5)(c): a recommendation from the committee whether action should be taken against the administrative law judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(6): Actions recommended by the committee may include no action, disciplinary action, termination, or any other action an employer may take against an employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-709(7): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act The record of an individual committee member's vote on recommended actions against an administrative law judge is a protected record under


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710 Required training.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(1): Each year that an administrative law judge receives a performance evaluation conducted by the division under this chapter, the administrative law judge shall complete the procedural fairness training program described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(2): The division shall establish a procedural fairness training program that includes training on how an administrative law judge's actions and behavior influence others' perceptions of the fairness of the adjudicative process.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3): The procedural fairness training program shall include discussion of the following elements of procedural fairness:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(a): neutrality, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(a)(i): consistent and equal treatment of the individuals who appear before the administrative law judge;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(a)(ii): concern for the individual needs of the individuals who appear before the administrative law judge; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(a)(iii): unhurried and careful deliberation;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(b): respectful treatment of others; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(3)(c): providing individuals a voice and opportunity to be heard.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(4): The division may contract with a public or private person to develop or provide the procedural fairness training program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-710(5): Title 63G, Chapter 22, State Training and Certification Requirements The division shall ensure that the procedural fairness training program complies with

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-802 Education benefit plan for law enforcement and correctional officers.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-802(1): 53-13-103; 53-13-104 As used in this section:

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-802(4)(b): 5.5% for a bachelor's degree; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-802(4)(c): 5.5% for a master's degree.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-802(5): Expenses incurred by an agency to provide additional compensation under this section may be only from the agency's existing budget.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806 Definitions -- Infant at Work Pilot Program -- Administration -- Report.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(a): "Eligible employee" means an employee who has been employed by the Department of Health and Human Services for a minimum of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(a)(i): 12 consecutive months; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(a)(ii): 1,250 hours, excluding paid time off during the 12-month period immediately preceding the day on which the employee applies for participation in the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(b): "Infant" means a baby that is at least six weeks of age and no more than six months of age.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(c): "Parent" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(c)(i): a biological or adoptive parent of an infant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(c)(ii): an individual who has an infant placed in the individual's foster care by the Division of Child and Family Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(1)(d): "Program" means the Infant at Work Pilot Program established in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(2): There is created the Infant at Work Pilot Program for eligible employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(3): The program shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(3)(a): allow an eligible employee to bring the eligible employee's infant to work subject to the provisions of this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(3)(b): be administered by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(3)(c): be implemented for a minimum of one year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(4): The division shall establish an application process for eligible employees of the Department of Health and Human Services to apply to the program that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(4)(a): a process for evaluating whether an eligible employee's work environment is appropriate for an infant;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(4)(b): guidelines for infant health and safety; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(4)(c): guidelines regarding an eligible employee's initial and ongoing participation in the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(5): If the division approves the eligible employee for participation in the program, the eligible employee shall have the sole responsibility for the care and safety of the infant at the workplace.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(6): The division may not require the Department of Health and Human Services to designate or set aside space for an eligible employee's infant other than the eligible employee's existing work space.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(7): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division, in consultation with the Department of Health and Human Services, shall make rules that the department determines necessary to establish the program in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-806(8): On or before June 30, 2025, the division, in consultation with the Department of Health and Human Services, shall submit a written report to the Business and Labor Interim Committee that describes the efficacy of the program, including any recommendations for additional legislative action.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808 On-site child care for state employees.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(1): 35A-3-201 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(1)(a): 35A-3-201 "Child care" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(1)(b): "Licensed child care provider" means a person who holds a license from the Department of Health and Human Services to provide center based child care in accordance with Title 26B, Chapter 2, Part 4, Child Care Licensing.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(1)(c): "On-site child care center" means a child care center established in a facility that is owned or operated by an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(2): An agency may enter into a contract with a licensed child care provider to operate an on-site child care center for the benefit of the agency's employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(3): A licensed child care provider that operates an on-site child care center for an agency shall maintain professional liability insurance.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(4)(a): An agency may charge a licensed child care provider a reasonable fee for operating an on-site child care center so that the agency incurs no expense.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(4)(b): The fee in Subsection (4)(a) shall include costs for utility, building maintenance, and administrative services supplied by the agency that are related to the operation of the on-site child care center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(5): An agency may consult with the Office of Child Care within the Department of Workforce Services, the Department of Health and Human Services, and the Division of Facilities Construction and Management for assistance in establishing an on-site child care center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-808(6): The state is not liable for any civil damages for acts or omissions resulting from the operation of an on-site child care center.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904 Political activity of employees -- Rules and regulations -- Highway patrol -- Hatch Act.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(1): Except as otherwise provided by law or by rules made under this section for federally aided programs, the provisions of this section apply with regard to political activity of career service employees in all grades and positions.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(2): Career service employees may voluntarily participate in political activity subject to the following provisions:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(2)(a): if any career service employee is elected to any partisan or full-time nonpartisan political office, that employee shall be granted a leave of absence without pay for times when monetary compensation is received for service in political office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(2)(b): no officer or employee in career service may engage in any political activity during the hours of employment, nor may any person solicit political contributions from employees of the executive branch during hours of employment for political purposes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(2)(c): partisan political activity may not be a basis for employment, promotion, demotion, or dismissal, except that the director shall adopt rules providing for the discipline or punishment of a state officer or employee who violates any provision of this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(3): (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(3)(a): Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, no member of the Utah Highway Patrol may use the member's official authority or influence for the purpose of interfering with an election or affecting the results of an election.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(3)(b): (3) No person may induce or attempt to induce any member of the Utah Highway Patrol to participate in any activity prohibited by this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(4): Nothing contained in this section may be construed to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(4)(a): preclude voluntary contributions by an employee to the party or candidate of the officer's or employee's choice; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-17-904(4)(b): permit partisan political activity by any employee who is prevented or restricted from engaging in the political activity by the provisions of the federal Hatch Act.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 63A - Chapter 19 - Government Data Privacy Act

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(1): 63A-19-302 "Chief privacy officer" means the individual appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(2): 63C-24-102 "Commission" means the Utah Privacy Commission established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(3): 63A-16-1102 "Cyber Center" means the Utah Cyber Center created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(4): "Data breach" means the unauthorized access, acquisition, disclosure, loss of access, or destruction of personal data held by a governmental entity, unless the governmental entity concludes, according to standards established by the Cyber Center, that there is a low probability that personal data has been compromised.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(5): 67-3-13 "Designated governmental entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(6): 63A-19-201 "Governing board" means the Utah Privacy Governing Board established in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(7): 63G-2-103 "Governmental entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(8): "High risk processing activities" means a governmental entity's processing of personal data that may result in a significant compromise to an individual's privacy interests, based on factors that include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(8)(a): the sensitivity of the personal data processed;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(8)(b): the amount of personal data being processed;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(8)(c): the individual's ability to consent to the processing of personal data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(8)(d): risks of unauthorized access or use.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(9): 63G-2-103 "Individual" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(10): "Legal guardian" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(10)(a): the parent of a minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(10)(b): an individual appointed by a court to be the guardian of a minor or incapacitated person and given legal authority to make decisions regarding the person or property of the minor or incapacitated person.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(11): 63A-19-301 "Office" means the Office of Data Privacy created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(12): 63A-19-501 "Ombudsperson" means the data privacy ombudsperson appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(13): "Personal data" means information that is linked or can be reasonably linked to an identified individual or an identifiable individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(14): "Process" or "processing" means any operation or set of operations performed on personal data, including collection, recording, organization, structuring, storage, adaptation, alteration, access, retrieval, consultation, use, disclosure by transmission, transfer, dissemination, alignment, combination, restriction, erasure, or destruction.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(15): 63G-2-103 "Record" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(16): 63G-2-103 "Record series" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(17): 63A-12-113 "Retention schedule" means a governmental entity's schedule for the retention or disposal of records that has been approved by the Records Management Committee pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(18): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(18)(a): "Sell" means an exchange of personal data for monetary consideration by a governmental entity to a third party.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(18)(b): "Sell" does not include a fee:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(18)(b)(i): charged by a governmental entity for access to a record; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(18)(b)(ii): assessed in accordance with an approved fee schedule.

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(19)(a)(ii): a commission;

Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(19)(a)(iv): a council;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-101(19)(a)(v): an institution;
