Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102 State data privacy policy.
-----------------------------------------------------------
It is the policy of Utah that:Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(1): an individual has a fundamental interest in and inherent expectation of privacy regarding the personal data that the individual provides to a governmental entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(2): a governmental entity shall act in a manner respecting personal data provided to the governmental entity that is consistent with the interests and expectations described in Subsection (1);
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3): the state shall encourage innovation to enhance the ability of a governmental entity to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(a): protect the privacy of an individual's personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(b): provide clear notice to an individual regarding the governmental entity's processing of the individual's personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(c): process personal data only for specified, lawful purposes and only process the minimum amount of an individual's personal data necessary to achieve those purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(d): implement appropriate consent mechanisms regarding the uses of an individual's personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(e): provide an individual with the ability to access, control, and request corrections to the individual's personal data held by a governmental entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(f): maintain appropriate safeguards to protect the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(g): account for compliance with privacy related laws, rules, and regulations that are specific to a particular governmental entity, program, or personal data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(3)(h): meet a governmental entity's and an individual's business and service needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(4): the state shall promote training and education programs for employees of governmental entities focused on:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(4)(a): data privacy best practices, obligations, and responsibilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(4)(b): the overlapping relationship with privacy, records management, and security; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-102(5): the state shall promote consistent terminology in data privacy requirements across governmental entities.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201 Utah Privacy Governing Board.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(1): There is created the Utah Privacy Governing Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2): The governing board shall be composed of five members as follows:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2)(a): the governor, or the governor's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2)(b): the president of the Senate, or the president's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2)(c): the speaker of the House of Representatives, or the speaker's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2)(d): the attorney general, or the attorney general's designee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(2)(e): the state auditor, or the state auditor's designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(3)(a): A majority of the members of the governing board is a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(3)(b): The action of a majority of a quorum constitutes an action of the governing board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(4): The governor, or the governor's designee is chair of the governing board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(5): The governing board shall meet at least two times a year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(6): 63A-19-601 The governing board may recommend specific matters to the state auditor under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-201(7): The office shall provide staff and support to the governing board.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202 Governing board duties.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1): The governing board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(a): recommend changes to the state data privacy policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(b): by July 1 of each year, approve the data privacy agenda items for the commission and make recommendations for additional items for the data privacy agenda;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(c): hear issues raised by the ombudsperson regarding existing governmental entity privacy practices;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(d): evaluate and recommend the appropriate:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(d)(i): structure and placement for the office within state government; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(d)(ii): authority to be granted to the office, including any authority to make rules; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(e): recommend funding mechanisms and strategies for governmental entities to enable compliance with data privacy responsibilities, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(e)(i): appropriations;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(e)(ii): rates;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(e)(iii): grants; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(1)(e)(iv): internal service funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(2): In fulfilling the duties under this part, the governing board may receive and request input from:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(2)(a): governmental entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(2)(b): elected officials;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(2)(c): subject matter experts; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-202(2)(d): other stakeholders.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301 Office of Data Privacy.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(1): There is created within the department the Office of Data Privacy.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(2): The office shall coordinate with the governing board and the commission to perform the duties in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3): 63A-12-110 The office shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a): create and maintain a strategic data privacy plan to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(i): assist state agencies to implement effective and efficient privacy practices, tools, and systems that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(i)(A): protect the privacy of personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(i)(B): comply with laws and regulations specific to the entity, program, or data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(i)(C): empower individuals to protect and control their personal data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(i)(D): enable information sharing among entities, as allowed by law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(a)(ii): account for differences in state agency resources, capabilities, populations served, data types, and maturity levels regarding privacy practices;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(b): review statutory provisions related to governmental data privacy and records management to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(b)(i): identify conflicts and gaps in data privacy law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(b)(ii): standardize language; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(b)(iii): consult impacted agencies and the attorney general regarding findings and proposed amendments;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(c): work with state agencies to study, research, and identify:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(c)(i): additional privacy requirements that are feasible for state agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(c)(ii): potential remedies and accountability mechanisms for non-compliance of a state agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(c)(iii): ways to expand individual control and rights with respect to personal data held by state agencies; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(c)(iv): resources needed to develop, implement, and improve privacy programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(d): monitor high-risk data processing activities within state agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(e): receive information from state agencies regarding the sale, sharing, and processing personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(f): coordinate with the Cyber Center to develop an incident response plan for data breaches affecting governmental entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(g): coordinate with the state archivist to incorporate data privacy practices into records management;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(h): 63A-12-110 coordinate with the state archivist to incorporate data privacy training into the trainings described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(3)(i): create a data privacy training program for employees of governmental entities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(4): The data privacy training program described in Subsection (3)(i) shall be made available to all governmental entities, and shall be designed to provide instruction regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(4)(a): data privacy best practices, obligations, and responsibilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(4)(b): the relationship between privacy, records management, and security.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (5)(b), an employee of a state agency shall complete the data privacy training program described in Subsection (3)(i):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5)(a)(i): within 30 days of beginning employment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5)(a)(ii): at least once in each calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5)(b): An employee of a state agency that does not have access to personal data as part of the employee's work duties is not required to complete the data privacy training program described in Subsection (3)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(5)(c): Each state agency is responsible for monitoring completion of data privacy training by the state agency's employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-301(6): To the extent that resources permit, the office may provide expertise and assistance to governmental entities for high risk data processing activities.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302 Chief privacy officer -- Appointment -- Powers -- Reporting.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(1): The governor shall, with the advice and consent of the Senate, appoint a chief privacy officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(2): The chief privacy officer is the director of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3): 63A-19-401 The chief privacy officer:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(a): shall exercise all powers given to and perform all duties imposed on the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(b): has administrative authority over the office;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(c): may make changes in office personnel and service functions under the chief privacy officer's administrative authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(d): may authorize a designee to assist with the chief privacy officer's responsibilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(e): 63A-19-401 shall report annually, on or before October 1, to the Judiciary Interim Committee regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(e)(i): recommendations for legislation to address data privacy concerns; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-302(3)(e)(ii): 63A-19-401 reports received from state agencies regarding the sale or sharing of personal data provided under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401 Duties of governmental entities.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1): 63G-2-702; 63G-2-703; 63G-2-704; 63A-19-402; 63A-19-403; 63A-19-404
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1)(a): Except as provided in Subsections (1)(b) and (c), a governmental entity shall comply with the requirements of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1)(b)(i): If a governmental entity or a contractor described in Subsection (4)(a) is subject to a more restrictive or a more specific provision of law than found in this part, the governmental entity or contractor shall comply with the more restrictive or more specific provision of law.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1)(b)(ii): For purposes of Subsection (1)(b)(i), Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act, is a more specific provision of law and shall control over the provisions of this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(1)(c): 63G-2-702; 63G-2-703; 63G-2-704; 63A-19-402; 63A-19-403; 63A-19-404 A governmental entity that is exempt under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2): 63A-19-406 A governmental entity:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(a): shall implement and maintain a privacy program before May 1, 2025, that includes the governmental entity's policies, practices, and procedures for the process of personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(b): 63A-19-406 shall provide notice to an individual or the legal guardian of an individual, if the individual's personal data is affected by a data breach, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(c): shall obtain and process only the minimum amount of personal data reasonably necessary to efficiently achieve a specified purpose;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(d): shall meet the requirements of this part for all processing activities implemented by a governmental entity after May 1, 2024;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(e): shall for any processing activity implemented before May 1, 2024, as soon as is reasonably practicable, but no later than January 1, 2027:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(e)(i): identify any non-compliant processing activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(e)(ii): document the non-compliant processing activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(e)(iii): prepare a strategy for bringing the non-compliant processing activity into compliance with this part;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(f): may not establish, maintain, or use undisclosed or covert surveillance of individuals unless permitted by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(g): may not sell personal data unless expressly required by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(h): may not share personal data unless permitted by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(i): that is a designated governmental entity, shall annually report to the state privacy officer:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(i)(A): the types of personal data the designated governmental entity currently shares or sells;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(i)(B): the basis for sharing or selling the personal data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(i)(C): the classes of persons and the governmental entities that receive the personal data from the designated governmental entity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(ii): that is a state agency, shall annually report to the chief privacy officer:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(ii)(A): the types of personal data the state agency currently shares or sells;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(ii)(B): the basis for sharing or selling the personal data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(i)(ii)(C): the classes of persons and the governmental entities that receive the personal data from the state agency; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(j): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(j)(i): except as provided in Subsection (3), an employee of a governmental entity shall complete a data privacy training program:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(j)(i)(A): within 30 days after beginning employment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(j)(i)(B): at least once in each calendar year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(2)(k): is responsible for monitoring completion of data privacy training by the governmental entity's employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(3): An employee of a governmental entity that does not have access to personal data of individuals as part of the employee's work duties is not required to complete a data privacy training program described in Subsection (2)(j)(i).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(4)(a): A contractor that enters into or renews an agreement with a governmental entity after May 1, 2024, and processes or has access to personal data as a part of the contractor's duties under the agreement, is subject to the requirements of this chapter with regard to the personal data processed or accessed by the contractor to the same extent as required of the governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(4)(b): An agreement under Subsection (4)(a) shall require the contractor to comply with the requirements of this chapter with regard to the personal data processed or accessed by the contractor as a part of the contractor's duties under the agreement to the same extent as required of the governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-401(4)(c): The requirements under Subsections (4)(a) and (b) are in addition to and do not replace any other requirements or liability that may be imposed for the contractor's violation of other laws protecting privacy rights or government records.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402 General governmental privacy requirements -- Personal data request notice.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(1): A governmental entity shall provide a personal data request notice to an individual, or the legal guardian of an individual, from whom the governmental entity requests or collects personal data.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2): The personal data request notice described in Subsection (1) shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(a): the reasons the individual is asked to provide the personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(b): the intended purposes and uses of the personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(c): the consequences for refusing to provide the personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(d): the classes of persons and entities that:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(d)(i): share the personal data with the governmental entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(d)(ii): receive the personal data from the governmental entity on a regular or contractual basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(2)(e): the record series in which the personal data is or will be included, if applicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(3): The governmental entity shall provide the personal data request notice by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(3)(a): posting the personal data request notice in a prominent place where the governmental entity collects the personal data;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(3)(b): including the personal data request notice as part of any document or form used by the governmental entity to collect the personal data; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(3)(c): conspicuously linking to or displaying a QR code linked to an electronic version of the personal data request notice as part of any document or form used by the governmental entity to collect the personal data.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(4): The personal data request notice required by this section is in addition to, and does not supersede, any other notice requirement otherwise applicable to the governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(5): The governmental entity shall, upon request, provide the personal data request notice to an individual, or the legal guardian of an individual, regarding personal data previously furnished by that individual.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-402(6): The governmental entity may only use personal data furnished by an individual for the purposes identified in the personal data request notice provided to that individual.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-403 Procedure to request amendment or correction of personal data.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-403(1): A governmental entity that collects personal data shall provide a procedure by which an individual or legal guardian of an individual may request an amendment or correction of personal data that has been furnished to the governmental entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-403(2): The procedure by which an individual or legal guardian of an individual may request an amendment or correction shall comply with all applicable laws and regulations to which the personal data at issue and to which the governmental entity is subject.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-403(3): The procedure to request an amendment or correction described in this section does not obligate the governmental entity to make the requested amendment or correction.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-404 Retention and disposition of personal data.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-404(1): A governmental entity that collects personal data shall retain and dispose of the personal data in accordance with a documented record retention schedule.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-404(2): Compliance with Subsection (1) does not exempt a governmental entity from complying with other applicable laws or regulations related to retention or disposition of specific personal data held by that governmental entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405 Data breach notification to the Cyber Center and the Office of the Attorney General.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(1)(a): A governmental entity that identifies a data breach affecting 500 or more individuals shall notify the Cyber Center and the attorney general of the data breach.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(1)(b): In addition to the notification required by Subsection (1)(a), a governmental entity that identifies the unauthorized access, acquisition, disclosure, loss of access, or destruction of data that compromises the security, confidentiality, availability, or integrity of the computer systems used or information maintained by the governmental entity shall notify the Cyber Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2): The notification under Subsection (1) shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(a): be made without unreasonable delay, but no later than five days from the discovery of the data breach; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b): include the following information:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(i): the date and time the data breach occurred;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(ii): the date the data breach was discovered;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(iii): a short description of the data breach that occurred;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(iv): the means by which access was gained to the system, computer, or network;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(v): the individual or entity who perpetrated the data breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(vi): steps the governmental entity is or has taken to mitigate the impact of the data breach; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(2)(b)(vii): any other details requested by the Cyber Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(3): For a data breach under Subsection (1)(a), the governmental entity shall provide the following information to the Cyber Center and the attorney general in addition to the information required under Subsection (2)(b):
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(3)(a): the total number of people affected by the data breach, including the total number of Utah residents affected; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(3)(b): the type of personal data involved in the data breach.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(4): If the information required by Subsection (2)(b) is not available within five days of discovering the breach, the governmental entity shall provide as much of the information required under Subsection (2)(b) as is available and supplement the notification with additional information as soon as the information becomes available.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(5)(a): A governmental entity that experiences a data breach affecting fewer than 500 individuals shall create an internal incident report containing the information in Subsection (2)(b) as soon as practicable and shall provide additional information as the information becomes available.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(5)(b): A governmental entity shall provide to the Cyber Center:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(5)(b)(i): an internal incident report described in Subsection (5)(a) upon request of the Cyber Center; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-405(5)(b)(ii): an annual report logging all of the governmental entity's data breach incidents affecting fewer than 500 individuals.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406 Data breach notice to individuals affected by data breach.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(1): A governmental entity shall provide a data breach notice to an individual or legal guardian of an individual affected by the data breach:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(1)(a): after determining the scope of the data breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(1)(b): after restoring the reasonable integrity of the affected system, if necessary; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(1)(c): without unreasonable delay except as provided in Subsection (1)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(2): A governmental entity shall delay providing notification under Subsection (1) at the request of a law enforcement agency that determines that notification may impede a criminal investigation, until such time as the law enforcement agency informs the governmental entity that notification will no longer impede the criminal investigation.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3): The data breach notice to an affected individual shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3)(a): a description of the data breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3)(b): the individual's personal data that was accessed or may have been accessed;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3)(c): steps the governmental entity is taking or has taken to mitigate the impact of the data breach;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3)(d): recommendations to the individual on how to protect themselves from identity theft and other financial losses; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(3)(e): any other language required by the Cyber Center.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4): Unless the governmental entity reasonably believes that providing notification would pose a threat to the safety of an individual, or unless an individual has designated to the governmental entity a preferred method of communication, a governmental entity shall provide notice by:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(a)(i): email, if reasonably available and allowed by law; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(a)(ii): mail; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(b): one of the following methods, if the individual's contact information is reasonably available and the method is allowed by law:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(b)(i): text message with a summary of the data breach notice and instructions for accessing the full notice; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(4)(b)(ii): telephone message with a summary of the data breach notice and instructions for accessing the full data breach notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(5): A governmental entity shall also provide a data breach notice in a manner that is reasonably calculated to have the best chance of being received by the affected individual or the legal guardian of an individual, such as through a press release, posting on appropriate social media accounts, or publishing notice in a newspaper of general circulation when:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(5)(a): a data breach affects more than 500 individuals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-406(5)(b): a governmental entity is unable to obtain an individual's contact information to provide notice for any method listed in Subsection (4).


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501 Data privacy ombudsperson.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(1): The governor shall appoint a data privacy ombudsperson with the advice of the governing board.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2): The ombudsperson shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2)(a): be familiar with the provisions of:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2)(a)(i): this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2)(a)(ii): Chapter 12, Division of Archives and Records Service and Management of Government Records; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2)(a)(iii): Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(2)(b): serve as a resource for an individual who is making or responding to a complaint about a governmental entity's data privacy practice.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(3): The ombudsperson may, upon request by a governmental entity or individual, mediate data privacy disputes between individuals and governmental entities.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(4): After consultation with the chief privacy officer or the state privacy officer, the ombudsperson may raise issues and questions before the governing board regarding serious and repeated violations of data privacy from:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(4)(a): a specific governmental entity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-501(4)(b): widespread governmental entity data privacy practices.


Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601 Enforcement.
---------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(1): Upon instruction by the board, the state auditor shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(1)(a): investigate alleged violations of this chapter by a governmental entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(1)(b): provide notice to the relevant governmental entity of an alleged violation of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(1)(c): for a violation that the state auditor substantiates, provide an opportunity for the governmental entity to cure the violation within 30 days.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(2): If a governmental entity fails to cure a violation as provided in Subsection (1)(c), the state auditor shall report the governmental entity's failure:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(2)(a): for a designated governmental entity, to the attorney general for enforcement under Subsection (3); and
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(2)(b): for a state agency, to the Legislative Management Committee.
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(3): After referral by the state auditor under Subsection (2)(a), the attorney general may file an action in district court to:
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(3)(a): enjoin a designated governmental entity from violating this chapter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 63A-19-601(3)(b): require a designated governmental entity to comply with this chapter.
